*Source Text:* *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era, Cave of Mystery (Dongxuan) Section, Precepts Category*

*Essential Regulations for Cultivation, Rituals, and Precepts, Scroll One*
Compiled by Daoist Zhu Faman of the Three Caverns

The sagely respond to the world, ever relying on scriptural teachings. Without establishing the true treasures, how could salvation be achieved? Their mouths utter jade-like texts, expounding these numinous mysteries, returning to purity and reverting to simplicity—all hinges upon this, rooted in the heart. For those who seek learning, the method is manifest herein.

The *Scripture of Generating the Spirit* states: During the Dragon Han kalpa, the Heavenly Worthy expounded the *Scriptures of the Cavern of Perfection*; during the Crimson Brightness kalpa, the *Scriptures of the Cavern of Mystery*; and during the Kaihuang kalpa, the *Scriptures of the Cavern of Divinity*. These Three Cavern Scriptures, replete with profound and arcane teachings, adapt to the capacities of beings, liberating and guiding gods and humans, enabling the six destinies to return to the real and the three vehicles to awaken to truth. Practices vary in elevation, methods in profundity—thirty-six divisions thus emerge and become illustrious.

The *True Treasury Scripture* says: First, the *Shangqing*; second, the *Wonderful Perfection*; third, the *Great One*; fourth, the *Wonderful Grove*; fifth, the *Transformation and Enlightenment*; sixth, the *Immortals*; seventh, the *Yellow Grove*; eighth, the *Supreme Perfected*; ninth, the *Teachings of the Dao*; tenth, the *Supreme Refinement*; eleventh, the *Supreme Meritorious Virtue*; twelfth, the *Scriptures of the Dao and Its Power*. These twelve divisions of scriptures are stored within the Great Cavern’s Treasury of the Jade Clarity Realm.

First, the *Cavern of Mystery*; second, the *Primal Yang*; third, the *Primal Celestial Stem*; fourth, the *Great Kalpa*; fifth, the *Supreme Enlightenment*; sixth, the *Inner Tones*; seventh, the *Refinement of Life*; eighth, the *Numinous Secrets*; ninth, the *Dispelling of Demons*; tenth, the *Boundless*; eleventh, the *Massage*; twelfth, the *Supreme Communication*. These twelve divisions of scriptures reside within the Treasury of the Supreme Clarity Realm.

First, the *Great Clarity*; second, the *Penetrating Vision*; third, the *Assembly of Immortals*; fourth, the *Cavern Abyss*; fifth, the *Inner Secrets*; sixth, the *True One*; seventh, the *Assembly of Spirits*; eighth, the *Middle Essence*; ninth, the *Boundless*; tenth, the *Palace Assembly*; eleventh, the *Yellow Court*; twelfth, the *Lesser Kalpa*. These twelve divisions belong to the Treasury of the Great Clarity Realm.

Thus, the revealed scriptures of the Three Caverns are inscribed upon golden tablets, their models transmitted by the seven sages, elucidated in jade-like texts. Once in ten thousand kalpas, the Dao emerges in accordance with the people.

The *Statutes of the Supreme Perfected* states: In the first year of the Han An era, on the first day of the fifth month, the Most High Lord Lao bestowed upon Zhang Daoling at Mount Heming the *Scriptures of Orthodox Unity and the Alliance of Awe*, comprising nine hundred and thirty scrolls, along with seventy scrolls of talismans and charts, totaling one thousand scrolls. He also transmitted the *Great Cavern True Scripture* in twenty-one scrolls to those who had already attained perfection.

The *Scripture of Great Peace* records:
A perfected one asked, “What are the Heavenly Scriptures? The Earthly Scriptures? The Human Scriptures? The Dao Scriptures? The Sagely Scriptures? The Worthy Scriptures? The Auspicious Scriptures? The Inauspicious Scriptures? The Scriptures of Life? The Scriptures of Death?”

The divine being replied: “Those who cultivate and accumulate the true Dao—this is the Heavenly Scripture. Heaven delights in life, and the Dao also delights in life; thus, it is the Heavenly Scripture. Those who cultivate and accumulate virtue—this is the Earthly Scripture. Earth delights in nurturing, and virtue also delights in nurturing; thus, it is the Earthly Scripture. Those who cultivate harmony and delight in bestowing—this is the Human Scripture. Harmonious qi flows and circulates; humans possess wealth and should likewise circulate it; thus, harmony is the Human Scripture. Those who cultivate and accumulate the teachings of the Dao from the high, middle, and low antiquity—these are the Dao Scriptures. Those who cultivate and accumulate the sagely texts of the high, middle, and low antiquity—these are the Sagely Scriptures. Those who cultivate and accumulate the worthy teachings of the high, middle, and low antiquity—these are the Worthy Scriptures. If one’s teacher is auspicious, these are the Auspicious Scriptures; if one’s teacher is inauspicious, these are the Inauspicious Scriptures. If one’s teacher lives, these are the Scriptures of Life; if one’s teacher dies, these are the Scriptures of Death.”

The Dao is made manifest by the sagely; the Way is propagated by humans. The *Scriptures of the Dao* state: “If lords and kings can preserve the myriad things, all will transform of themselves. Know that when the human king possesses the Dao, the Great Dao flourishes; when the human king lacks the Dao, the Great Dao declines.”

*Notes on Transmitting Scriptures*
White feathers and black quills mark the words of successive generations...

Gold fish and jade dragons—how could these be the faith of ordinary men?

That which may be transmitted yet cannot be received, that which is hard to behold and harder still to follow: such distinctions arise from the depth or shallowness of one’s vessel, the coarseness or refinement of one’s karmic conditions. The Primordial Beginning illumines the three vehicles’ dharma-mirror, encompassing all divergent streams; the Most High unfolds the subtle words of the two scrolls, universally guiding all back to the One.

The *Sutra of Original Appearance* states: “The body is the root of the three evils, the foundation of divine immortals. It is called by ten names: first, the Field of Good Fortune; second, the Garden of Thorns; third, the House of Seeds; fourth, the Gate of Abandoned Life; fifth, the Realm of the Dao; sixth, the Village of Pus and Blood; seventh, the Vessel of Treasures; eighth, the Basin of Shards; ninth, the Chamber of Bright Wisdom; tenth, the Person of Ninefold Nightly Darkness. One who knows this principle may be called a Perfected Person.”

Yet those who speak without substance must not be allowed to hear the scriptures; only those who possess both substance and speech may receive transmission.

The *Sutra of Ascending Mystery* states: “In the degenerate age, the people are beset by three fears—let them be carefully examined. First, jealousy toward the Dao and its teachings is to be feared; second, slander is to be feared; third, greed and desire are to be feared. Jealousy toward the Dao and its teachings obstructs the circulation of scriptural dharma; slander of dharma-teachers causes the common people’s faith in the Dao to wane; greed for wealth and sensuality renders one despised by others. Of these three, two lie without, one within. Only by eliminating these three afflictions may one transmit the Dao.”

The *Sutra of Original Boundary* states: “One who fulfills the ten good vows may be entrusted with transmission. What are the ten good vows? First, the vow to depart from the defiled and杂境界 of the world; second, the vow to leave the household life, forsake worldly attachments, follow conditions to beg alms, widely establish fields of merit, constantly practice compassion and forbearance, and forever abandon notions of self and others; third, the vow to encounter superior friends who guide and instruct; fourth, the vow to meet an enlightened teacher and quietly receive the supreme Dao; fifth, the vow to hear the true dharma and practice accordingly; sixth, the vow to behold the Heavenly Worthy and personally receive the sacred decree; seventh, the vow to deliver all beings, placing others before oneself; eighth, the vow to widely proclaim the dharma-sound to dispel ignorance; ninth, the vow that all sentient beings may awaken the intention for the Dao, exhorting them to create scriptures and images, construct numinous temples, and offer incense, flowers, lamps, and candles according to their means, so that all who have not yet awakened may universally behold the dharma-gate; tenth, the vow that one’s own mind remain steadfast and unretreatant. Only one who fulfills these ten vows may be entrusted with transmission.”

The *Sutra of Ascending Mystery* states: “In future ages, those who wish to circulate the *Inner Teachings Sutra of Numinous Treasure* must possess eleven qualities to gain the trust of the people before they may propagate this scripture. First, they must uphold the precepts completely, with no inner transgressions; second, they must relieve the orphaned, the elderly, and the poor, possessing a heart of compassion and pity...”

Third, they must urge others to shun evil and cultivate goodness with the devotion of a parent for a child; fourth, they must not seek fame or reputation, treating praise and blame as one; fifth, in secluded places, they must diligently perform rites and worship, cultivating all meritorious deeds as if in the presence of a great assembly; sixth, they must not deceive, so that the people trust them as they trust the four seasons; seventh, they must wholly renounce glory and splendor, refusing all ranks and titles; eighth, they must forsake wife and children, dwelling alone in quietude; ninth, they must draw near to the wise and learned, broadly inquiring into the good Dao; tenth, though in seclusion, they must not remain solitary in mind, but discuss and deliberate with the worthy, never clinging obstinately to their own views; eleventh, they must always act with humility and reverence toward others. These are the eleven qualities that accord with the practice of the Inner Teachings.

There are also ten marks by which one may be entrusted with the transmission of this scripture. First, they must ardently seek superior dharma, following goodness as water flows downward; second, they must delight in drawing near to the wise and learned, harboring no suspicion or doubt; third, they must be discerning, able to distinguish truth from falsehood; fourth, they must be cautious, never speaking beyond their conduct; fifth, they must be gentle and harmonious, seldom committing transgressions; sixth, they must be able to take as teachers those superior to themselves, without arrogance or pride; seventh, they must revere their teachers and value the teachings as a pauper values treasure; eighth, they must serve their teachers and elders, sparing no effort or toil; ninth, they must feel a sense of repayment toward their former teachers; tenth, they must diligently request and receive instruction, unremitting day and night. These are the ten marks.

It is further said: Even one of lowly status, if possessed of true virtue unknown to others, may be worthy of upholding this dharma. Such a person may emerge unexpectedly, in a place beyond suspicion, and should be entrusted with the transmission of this scripture.

The *Hidden Commentary on the Jade Scripture* states: If one receives the scriptures without reverence, and teacher and disciple cultivate them improperly, they will suffer no response and later fall ill, even among their livestock.

The *Scripture of Great Peace* says: To withhold transmission from one who is worthy is to block the Dao of Heaven, and the harm falls upon oneself; to transmit to one who is unworthy is to invite retribution later.

The *Fixed Resolve* states: To withhold transmission from one who is worthy causes others to be cut off from the Dao; to hasten transmission to one who is unworthy brings immediate punishment in this life, and in the next, one violates the statutes twice over.

For coarse conduct is easily tainted, while sublime practice is difficult to follow. Though learners are as numerous as trees in a forest, those who succeed are few. The slightest deviation from the true canon binds one to transgression.

The *Precepts of the Woman in Blue* says: To receive the Dao without discerning its weight, to transmit it to the unworthy, to covet wealth and profit, to take from others for one’s own gain, to borrow without returning—treating what is borrowed as one’s own treasure—shortens one’s lifespan by 1,024 years.

The precepts state: One must not recklessly transmit the treasure of the scriptures to the faithless, nor reveal the true essentials of the Dao, lest Heaven shorten one’s lifespan by 96,000 years.

The *Yellow Register Simplified Writs* says: To transmit the scriptures when unqualified invites judgment by the Court of Luminous Brahma; to persist in transmission despite three warnings of the wind-knife brings judgment by the Court of Rectification; to present credentials to a teacher when one’s rank is unsuited, or to intimidate a teacher with authority, brings judgment by the Court of the Four Luminaries; to fail to observe the proper forms of deference brings judgment by the Court of Grand Ritual; to receive the scriptures with stinginess, failing to prepare the proper ritual offerings, brings judgment by the Court of Celestial Surveillance; to transmit without invoking the oath to the Five Emperors brings judgment by the Court of Execution; to carelessly reveal the titles of the scriptures or expose the celestial truths brings judgment by the Court of Heavenly Oaths; to fail in the proper observance of incense and lamps brings judgment by the Court of Numinous Might; to fail to transmit the dharma to three disciples as an "opening teacher," to seven as a "registering teacher," or to nine as a "transmitting teacher" brings judgment by the Court of Luminous Might; to have fulfilled the merit requirements for the Three Teachers and reached the required years, yet deliberately conceal and sever the dharma-gate, brings judgment by the Court of the Great Yin; to receive the dharma and fail to establish meritorious works brings judgment by the Court of Luminous Capital; to receive the dharma and fail to broadly transform others, leaving no name in the register of those delivered, brings judgment by the Court of the Lower Prime; to receive the dharma and fail to make vows for the Three Teachers brings judgment by the Court of Luminous Capital; to receive the dharma and fail to deliver even one person, obstructing the path of the worthy and seeking merit for oneself, brings judgment by the Court of the Dark Capital; to receive the scriptures and fail to properly arrange the altar, high seat, canopy, incense, and lamps brings judgment by the Court of Luminous Capital.

The *Statutes of Illuminating the True* state: For each of the true writs, one must use silk of a length corresponding to the years of one’s life; any discrepancy brings judgment by the Dark Court.

The statutes say: When receiving the true writs, one must use three golden dragons, casting them into the water府, mountain dwellings, or residences. Failure to cast them in all three places results in the Three Officials seizing the person, and one’s life register will be marked with a violation, bringing judgment by the Court of the Nine Capitals.

The statutes say: For the patterned silks of the Five Emperors, each must be forty feet in length, to invoke the Five Emperors as witnesses to the oath. Any violation brings judgment by the Court of the Yellow Springs.

The statutes say: One must use five taels of superior gold to pledge the Five Peaks as surety for the treasure of the scriptures. Any violation brings judgment by the Court of the Yin Officials.

The statutes say: One must use 240,000 gold coins to secure the twenty-four qi. If gold coins are unavailable, bronze coins may be used. Any violation brings judgment by the Court of the Capital Spirits.

The statutes say: Incense and lamps must be used to open the Nine Treasuries. Any violation brings judgment by the Court of the Great Yin.

The statutes say: One who receives the scriptures must maintain the fast. Any violation brings judgment by the Court of the Great Yang.

The statutes say: The celestial texts are secret and weighty; without faith, they are not treasured. Thus, the sages of old used faith to test the heart. Without faith, one demeans the Dao; without oaths, one trivializes the treasure. Any violation brings judgment by the Left and Right Courts.

The statutes say: To receive the scriptures without the Five Emperors as teachers, or to rashly peruse the texts without invoking the oath, incurs the same penalty as the statute for stealing the scriptures, bringing judgment by the Court of Luminous Law.

The above statutes are difficult to follow and easy to violate. Searching the texts and reflecting on their contents, none can fail to shudder. To sit upright and refrain from transmission is to obstruct and sever the dharma; to begin in accord with the intent of transmission yet deviate from the ten practices is to be torn between advance and retreat, with the fires of remorse intertwined.

How much worse for those of greedy and cruel disposition, whose hearts are hardened like leather armor! They do not inquire into the conduct of their predecessors, seeking only to possess the treasures of their disciples. They transmit the scriptures without regard for their sacred meaning, never once considering the restraints and prohibitions. Lacking the ritual offerings and pledges of the fast, how could they observe the rules of oaths and covenants? When disciples see their teachers’ example, they later imitate such transmission, unafraid of the underworld’s records, seeking only fame and profit. They destroy the Dao and corrupt the dharma—such people are the very source of this ruin.

The *Scripture of Western Ascension* states:
"In delusion they transmit to one another,
Passing it on in endless succession.
Falsehood invades the true,
And emptiness takes form as if real.
Deceiving themselves, they cannot discern truth,
Clinging to profit and guarding their gains.
The eternal Dao is forgotten,
And fools, blind to their own faults,
Are like wood that kindles its own fire,
Only to burn and rot away."
How true these words are—let us take them to heart and urge one another forward.

The *Statutes of Illuminating the True* in the *Transmission Copy* states:
"When receiving the true scriptures and dharma pledges, one must deduct two-tenths to offer to the ancestral masters, and another two-tenths to distribute to the poor."

The mountain-dwelling Daoist Yu Xinchong provided incense and lamps to establish merit for his disciples. For violations, he was examined by the Three Officials’ Bureau.

The *Statutes of the Great True* states:
"Those who receive governance from the Celestial Master must divide and allocate their households. They may not, like independent practitioners, retain twelve portions for themselves but must dedicate five of ten portions to merit. Upon entering the Celestial Master’s governance, this decree is to be proclaimed so all may know. Those who violate it shall be judged by the Five Punishments."

The *Statutes of the Four Poles Illuminating the Dao* states:
"Whenever transmitting the precious scriptures of Highest Clarity, if one receives offerings from disciples, one-third is to be scattered among mountain-dwelling recluses to relieve the destitute and impoverished. One portion is for one’s own ritual vestments, and one portion is to establish merit for the disciple’s seven ancestors. On the day of scattering offerings to mountain recluses, one should vow that all destitute, impoverished, and diligent hidden scholars in the world may soon attain the Dao, transcend the world, and ascend as immortals. On the day of making one’s ritual vestments, one should vow that one’s own body may share the same countenance as the divine immortals, donning their robes and headdresses to obtain the rules of immortal transcendence. When lighting lamps and burning incense, one should vow that the disciple and one’s own seven generations of ancestors may swiftly escape the knife mountains and the three paths of the five sufferings, ascend to the Southern Palace, return to the womb to be reborn as immortals, and in all matters follow the dharma to attain the true Dao. Those who violate these covenants and neglect the statutes shall be examined and punished in their own bodies."

The statutes further state:
"When receiving the precious scriptures of Highest Clarity, if the pledges and offerings presented to the master are insufficient to meet the required limits, one may not receive the scriptures. After receiving them, if the years for transmission have arrived, one may not accept offerings from others. All must be transmitted to the former master to fulfill the prior limits before the threefold division may proceed. If one violates these statutes, one’s seven ancestors shall be examined."

The *Statutes of Illuminating the True* states:
"If one who has received scriptures has not yet fulfilled the initial pledges but later encounters a worthy person who offers pledges and requests transmission, one must first use the received pledges to fulfill the former master’s limits. The remainder may then be used for one’s own dharma practice. Violations shall be examined by the Fire Officials’ Bureau."

The above three cases differ in their division of transmissions. Following the scriptures’ requirements, modern practitioners now use a twelvefold division, exhausting all for personal gain—this is arrogance toward superiors and violence toward inferiors, an extreme of reckless negligence.

**Transmission Year Limits**
The sages respond to the turning of kalpas,
And the Dao’s resonance is true.
Only when the Dao converges may one transmit,
Not to the unworthy or those lacking the five virtues.

The talismans state:
"After learning the Dao and receiving scriptures, one may transmit to one person every forty years. Those who have extended their lifespan may transmit to one person every four hundred years. Those who have attained earthly immortality may transmit to one person every four thousand years. Those who have attained celestial immortality may transmit to one person every forty thousand years. Those who have attained the supreme Dao may transmit to one person every forty thousand kalpas. The statutes for transmitting the Great Law of the Supreme Numinous Treasure are complete."

The *Hidden Instructions for Ascending to Perfection* states:
"When celestial perfected beings transmit scriptures, or when numinous persons transmit scriptures, they may pass them on six times in three thousand years, ten times in two thousand two hundred years, five times in one thousand years, or three times in seven hundred years. The above year limits are recorded in the jade registers and golden statutes of the sagely emperors and their masters—no later generation may presume to compare."

The *Scripture of the Sage’s Chronicle* states:
"Those whose names are inscribed on golden tablets and jade records will have eyes like sunlight, green teeth, and white blood. Those who possess the golden scriptures and jade registers of Highest Clarity will have shoulder blades like the River Chariot constellation and protruding bones on their chests. Those who hold the cinnabar slips and azure texts of the Great Ultimate will have lines on their palms resembling inverted human figures. Those with dark, purple names will have four rings in their eyes, with purple light at the center. Those with jade registers of Great Clarity will have voices like jade tones and golden echoes, square mouths, and round eyes. Those with golden names in the Great Simplicity will have white veins visible on their abdomens and purple qi in their mouths. Those with dark registers in the Dipper will have nine apertures in their hearts, brocade patterns on their lungs, a jade pellet beneath their jaws, green sinews in their eyes, and upward-curving brows. Such are the signs of the immortal perfected. Their comings and goings, actions and retreats, are not mere escape from the corpse. The transmission year limits may be followed as before."

Today’s masters, however, cannot guarantee their lifespans. They encounter scriptural teachings as if a mustard seed were cast onto a needle’s point, or as if a blind turtle were to chance upon a floating log’s hole. If they adhere strictly to the year limits, their wishes may be thwarted. Thus, they should act with compassion and benevolence, harboring the supreme Dao in their hearts, and fulfilling the ten vows before transmission may proceed.

The *Hidden Instructions for Ascending to Perfection* states:
"For a student of utmost dedication, one should diligently focus on the numinous and unseen, and petition the mysterious master. If even a slight affinity exists, enlightenment will surely follow. Only when the limits of the assembled perfected beings are met may one form an alliance. Once allied, one must cultivate, and in cultivation, one must persevere to the end. Then I shall share my gold with them as a friend. Those who do not meet these conditions need not strive in vain. To merely guard the scriptures until one’s satchel is full is to burden one’s seven ancestors, and the stones of the river’s examination will only multiply. The ancients called this 'fine skin,' but I name it 'ear-learning'—hearing the Dao, they crawl forward on their knees; when the Dao is silent, all is forgotten."

The Dao must be transmitted and received to be obtained; cultivation is not in vain. Like the forbidden arts of the world, without transmission, their use is ineffective. This single statement is enough for profound realization.

The *Statutes of the Mysterious Capital* states:
"Daoist and female officials who wear the insignia of office may not recklessly transmit the Dao to others. Only those of utmost sincerity and diligence may be permitted to receive it. For the wicked and rebellious, three generations shall be examined."

The *Natural Instructions* states:
"Before transmission, master and disciple must first observe a fast for three months, or ten, thirty, or twenty days. Then, together, they ascend a mountain peak or altar to transmit the scriptures. After receiving them, if the disciple encounters a worthy person of sincere heart and devotion to the Dao, they may present precious offerings to seek transmission without waiting for the year limits. If no such person appears, the remaining dharma offerings may be transmitted later to serve as a field of merit for all. The master may not selfishly retain them—such a sin is grave indeed."

The *Luminous Perfection Regulations* states:
"Those who superficially honor the Three Treasures yet fail to focus their minds, who treat scriptures and dharma with disdain, and profane sacred texts with irreverence; or who transmit teachings to disciples without adhering to the prescribed years; or who, without invoking Heaven and Earth, privately transmit without oaths, creating their own methods and violating the Four Pledges—such sins are grave indeed. In death, they shall suffer the shaving of their heads and the yoke of bondage, then be forced to climb the Sword Trees where eight winds blow from all directions, causing the trees to sway violently. Their feet shall fall upon the Knife Mountains, ascending and descending without end, their hands and bodies torn and wounded, the pain unbearable, the torment unendurable. For ten thousand kalpas, they shall be reborn among the lowest and most foolish; or afflicted with the six maladies, deaf and blind, forever cut off from the Dao, eternally barred from the gates of learning. They shall revolve through the Five Sufferings, sinking in the mire of sin, unable to attain liberation, forever planting the roots of evil. Those who transmit scriptures unlawfully bring this punishment upon themselves. Master and disciple must cherish and honor the wondrous Dao.

Thus concludes the first scroll of *Essential Regulations and Precepts, Wondrous Volume*.
*Essential Regulations and Precepts, Collected Notes*, Scroll Two.
Compiled by Daoist Zhu Faman of the Three Caverns.
Scripture Copying Notes."

The dragon’s script shines resplendent, the phoenix’s calligraphy flows with compassion; the purple brush inscribes its verses, the azure forest resounds with its echoes. In the Floating Black Realm, it broadly delivers devas and humans; within the refining pool, the torch of lofty wisdom blazes bright. The August Person inscribed it in kalpas past, the Azure Lad transmitted it in years gone by. Once the primordial chapter was opened, the Thearch’s brush was set to work. The Dharma-bridge is thus erected, and the shore of blessings may be ascended—such is made manifest in the act of copying and transcribing.

The *Sutra of the Fundamental Boundary* states: Should there be one who, with paper and ink, silk and fine cloth, carves jade or engraves gold, copies and transcribes, binds and mounts with cords and rollers, circulates and recites, proclaims to the unhearing—know that such a person has entered the portion of the Dao, their name inscribed in the Golden Register, their characters listed in the Jade Chapters.

The *Great Precepts* declare: Copying scriptures renders one’s descendants generation after generation wise and discerning, vast in learning and profound in mystery, ever encountering sagely eras. Know that today’s enlightened worthies and erudite scholars all owe their attainment to the copying of the Three Caverns’ sacred scriptures. Not only do they gain benefit in future lives, but even in the present they reap blessings.

The *Great Precepts* further state: For every coin spent in copying sacred scriptures, one receives a seventy-four myriad-fold recompense; for ten thousand coins, the reward is beyond reckoning. To relinquish one and gain ten thousand is ever praised—how much more so the seventy-four myriad-fold? The merit is towering, the virtue majestic. Even the wealthy and noble cannot receive such in vain.

The *Regulations of the Thousand Perfected* state: Should one copy the scriptures of the Three Vehicles—intending to copy the Great Vehicle but copying the Middle or Lesser instead—one incurs the five grave transgressions. But if intending to copy the Lesser or Middle and copying the Great Vehicle, no offense is committed.

**Recitation and Invocation of Mantras**

The scriptures issue from the sacred mouth, the Dharma is cultivated by the ordinary; their wondrous meaning is hard to fathom, while a coarse mind easily falters. Since written words are never solitary, each section and rank differs, and the invocations vary accordingly. Follow what is recited and practiced, each clarifying its own canonical rules.

1. **Reciting the *Sutra of Original Form***: Invoke the mantra.
   First strike the Dharma-drum thirty-six times, bow to the scripture thrice, and recite the mantra:
   *Profound, profound, the Perfect Dao of utmost truth,
   Pure and still, it returns to the Primordial Sovereign.
   Celestial perfected gather in radiant splendor,
   A hundred spirits converge beneath the resplendent sun.
   The four assemblies offer their hearts in devotion,
   Thus assembling the great immortal essence.
   The heavens’ halls open in due time,
   All kneel in reverent accord.
   Wondrous teachings spread transforming grace,
   Delivering the three paths from suffering.*

2. **Reciting the *Yellow Court Scripture***: Invoke and visualize.
   The *Alliance Rites of the Four Poles* state: When reciting the *Yellow Court Scripture*, one must burn incense and purify with fasting, don the ritual vestments, and enter the chamber facing north. Bow four times, kneel, and knock the teeth twenty-four times. Petition the Most High, Myriad Perfected, Jade Dawn, Supreme Great Dao Lord: “Your disciple now enters the chamber to recite and chant the Jade Scripture, refining the spirit and guarding the treasury. I beseech the flourishing of the Palace of the Stomach, that my body may ride the void, ascend to the imperial court, and upon completion, turn east to bow four times to the Great Thearch.”
   Again knock the teeth twelve times and petition the Great Thearch of Fusang and the Divine King of Yang Valley: “Your disciple now enters the chamber to unfold and chant the Jade Scripture. I beseech a tranquil chamber where magic mushrooms spontaneously grow, jade blossoms shine in splendor, the Three Luminaries illumine with clarity, and myriad embryonic immortals attain union with the imperial spirits.”
   Upon completion, face east and recite ten times for one cycle. After one cycle, return to face north and bow four times, then face east and bow four times. No further petition is needed. Should one violate these regulations, they shall suffer the punishment of the wind-blades.

3. **Reciting the *Scriptures of Lord Lao***: Invoke and visualize.
   The *Hidden Instructions of the Supreme Ultimate* state: First burn incense, arrange the ritual vestments, and bow ten times. Visualize within the heart the Great Dharma Master of the Mysterious Center, Lord Lao the Perfected of the River’s Edge, and Master Yin.
   The *Mantra of Unfolding the Scripture* states:
   *Profound, profound, the ancestral school of the Perfect Dao,
   Supreme virtue embodies the Vast Origin.
   Though the celestial perfected are distant and wondrous,
   They draw near through the Sovereign of the Muddy Pellet.
   Palaces and chambers are all of seven treasures,
   Windows and doors naturally part.
   Purity ever attracts the true,
   Riding the purple clouds in luminous ascent.
   Sun and moon illuminate left and right,
   Ascending as immortals, preserving eternal years.
   Seven ancestors ascend to heaven,
   Their generations become the gate of virtue and power.*
   Upon completion, knock the teeth thirty-six times and swallow saliva thirty-six times. First visualize the Azure Dragon on the left, the White Tiger on the right, the Vermilion Bird before, and the Dark Warrior behind. Beneath the feet, the eight trigrams’ divine tortoise and thirty-six lions prostrate ahead. The headscarf bears the Seven Stars, the five viscera generate the five qi, and a net of script covers the body. The Three Ones attend the scripture, each accompanied by a thousand chariots and ten thousand riders. Heaven and earth each have eighteen thousand jade maidens and jade lads guarding them.
   For every five hundred characters read, knock the teeth three times and swallow saliva three times.

4. **Reciting the *Supreme Purity Scriptures***: Invoke and visualize.
   The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state: When reading the *Supreme Purity Scriptures*, face north and bow nine times before the seat, then ascend facing east, turning left to face north.
   The *Hidden Commentary on the Jade Scripture’s Mantra of Unfolding the Scripture* states:
   *Subtle, subtle, the gate of the Mysterious School,
   Radiant and bright, it pierces the Hollow Cavern.
   The Perfect Dao arises from stillness and silence,
   Where one beholds the Three Pristine Palaces.
   The Great Dao is accomplished here,
   Riding the luminous clouds and dragons.
   On left and right attend the scripture’s guardians,
   Jade maidens and jade lads.
   The body crosses the river of immortality,
   Untangling the nets to follow the divine wind.
   Seven ancestors and the womb-born
   Become the ancestral school of immortals.*
   The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state: Knock the teeth nine times and visualize nine-colored clouds filling the chamber. The Azure Dragon, White Tiger, Lion, Dark Tortoise, immortal lads and jade maidens, and the officials of the Three Realms and Five Thearchs all guard left and right. Proceed before and behind, riding the heavens and reclining upon the earth while reciting the scripture. Upon completion, descend from the western side of the platform and bow as at the beginning.
   The *Jade Commentary* states: Knock the teeth thirty-six times and swallow saliva thirty-six times. First visualize the Perfected of the Returning Wind and the Blended Unity, along with a hundred spirits and myriad perfected, then begin reading the scripture.

5. **Reciting the *Numinous Treasure* scriptures and mantras.**
   The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state: When reading the *Numinous Treasure Scriptures*, face east, burn incense before the scripture, bow three times, and ascend the seat facing north.

The *Hidden Commentary on the Jade Scripture: Mystic Essence of the Opening Scripture Mantra* states:
Silent, it reaches the ultimate source,
Voidly towering, aeons high as Mount Meru.
Vast and open, the profound scripture unfolds—
Who can fathom its depths?
Once entering the Great Vehicle’s path,
Who reckons the kalpas’ span?
Neither born nor destroyed,
Yet born from the lotus.
Transcending the paths of the Three Realms,
With compassionate heart, one unbinds the world’s snares.
The Perfected, of unsurpassed virtue,
Generation after generation, become immortals.

Upon completion, knock the teeth thirty-six times and swallow saliva thirty-six times. Visualize the qi of the Five Viscera in their five colors, ascending to infuse the essence of the Five Stars, then begin reading the scripture.

6. **Reciting the *Scriptures of the Three Sovereigns*.**
The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state: When reading the *Scriptures of the Three Sovereigns*, face south, burn incense before the scripture, bow twice, and ascend the seat facing west, then turn left to face south.

The *Hidden Commentary on the Jade Scripture: Mystic Essence of the Opening Scripture Mantra* states:
The Supreme’s talisman of settled spirit,
Inscribed with the mandate of heaven and earth’s grace.
At the summons, they need not await their chariots—
Myriad immortals swiftly gather.
Calling forth spirits, great or small,
How much less the impure and defiled?
With pure fast, cut off worldly affairs,
In subtle communion, face the divine.
Ascend to the Jade Clarity Palace,
To roam and feast beyond the Nine Distances.

Upon completion, the *Simplified Texts* state: Knock the teeth three times and visualize three-colored clouds filling the chamber. The Azure Dragon, White Tiger, Vermilion Bird, and Dark Warrior guard the four directions, while divine youths and jade maidens attend left and right. Swallow qi three times, then recite the scripture. When finished, descend from the eastern side of the platform and bow as at the beginning.

7. **Pacing the Void.**
The *Hidden Commentary on the Jade Scripture* states: When reciting the *Scripture of Pacing the Void*, first knock the teeth three times and swallow saliva three times. Visualize the sun and moon before your face, entering through the nostrils into the Grotto Chamber’s Golden Flower Palace. Radiance emerges from behind the neck, blazing forth as a nine-colored orb, subtly penetrating the Jade Pillow to illumine the ten directions. Follow this light as you circumambulate the scripture.

The sun enters through the left nostril, the moon through the right. Upon completion, knock the teeth again as before, then recite the Secret Mantra of Commanding Demons.

The *Ritual Observances of the Hundred Families’ Fast* states that the Mantra of Commanding Demons reads:
*Yellow Center’s strategem-qi severs demons,
The Ancestral Inspector curbs the strong.
Essence severs the perverse and seals it—
The Supreme has decreed,
The Supreme’s chamber urgently summons the Northern Thearch.
Proceed to the Jade Palace,
Receive and bear the majestic command.
Proclaim the Demon Kings of the Five Qi,
Lush and dense, in accord with the mandate.
Pierce the secret treasury of jade,
The script’s pattern attains flourishing.
The Three Heavens revolve in brightness,
The Six Heavens’ revolutions end.
How worthy!*

The *Precentor* may intone: *All officials, visualize the nine-colored orb, swallow saliva three times, and contemplate the Secret Mantra of Commanding Demons. Pace the Void according to the method.*

**Entering and Exiting the Dao’s Portal.**
Contemplate the *Golden Register Simplified Texts*.

**Entering the Dao’s Portal in the Morning:**
Outside the portal of the fasting hall, knock the teeth three times.
The incantation reads:
*Fourfold Luminous Merit Officers,
Messengers of Communicating with the Perfected,
Jade Lads of Transmitting Words,
Jade Maidens of Attending in Stillness—
Convey my words,
To the hall’s presiding spirits.
Primal qi of the Upper Origin,
Enter my body.*

Then proceed to the *Laozi’s Visualization Chart*, which states:
One Fourfold Luminous Merit Officer,
One Messenger of Communicating with the Perfected,
Two Jade Lads of Transmitting Words,
Two Jade Maidens of Attending in Stillness.

The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state:
**Entering the Dao’s Portal at Night:**
Outside the portal, face it and knock the teeth three times.
The incantation reads:
*Fourfold Upper Merit Officers,
Dragon-Tiger Messengers,
Upright One’s Primal Qi,
Attending in Stillness’s Plain Maidens—
At night, when making petitions,
May the Luminous Lad and Upper Mystery Maiden
Accompany me into the Yellow Chamber’s interior,
Conveying all petitions,
Ensuring they ascend on high.*

Then proceed to the *Laozi’s Visualization Chart*, which states:
One Fourfold Upper Merit Officer,
Two Dragon-Tiger Messengers,
One Attending in Stillness’s Plain Maiden,
One Luminous Lad,
One Upper Mystery Maiden.

The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state:
**Exiting the Portal:**
Knock the teeth three times.
The incantation reads:
*Exiting yin, entering yang,
Myriad spirits open the passage.
With affairs concluded, the gates close—
Pray seal the Yellow Chamber.
Jade Maidens of Attending in Stillness,
Brightly attend the divine palace.*

The *Visualization Chart* states:
The Jade Maidens are the wondrous qi of spontaneity,
Responding to stimuli to form shapes.
Their forms and substance are luminous and pure,
Clear and bright as jade.
Hidden, they possess moisture;
Manifest, they are without perversity.
The adept’s true steps gradually ascend,
Advancing and retreating in form,
Entering and exiting in the Dao.
The Dao’s qi is subtly wondrous,
Responding to all, great and small.
In due order, they guide from low to high.
Thus, by day, Jade Maidens guard the palace;
By night, the Plain Maidens convey affairs,
Aiding in peril and ascending the Dao’s arena.

The *Golden Register Simplified Texts* state:
**Exiting the Portal at Night:**
Turn left and knock the teeth three times.
The incantation reads:
*Mystic Upper Great Yin,
Eight windows open in brightness.
Facing where petitions are made,
The Maiden conveys the numinous.
With affairs complete, return to your stations—
Myriad spirits silently repose.*

**Notes on the Lecture Manual:**
The true scriptures and sacred canons
Illumine the various heavens,
Jade characters and golden texts
Transmitted to this day.
The Dao is profound and abstruse,
Its secret treasury hard to open.
Were it not for the greatly capable,
How could the benighted be enlightened?

**I. On Orientation.**
The *Scripture of Ascending the Mystery* states: When lecturing on scriptures, the Dharma Master and Scripture Master sit facing each other. The seat is five feet high, and they may sit facing any of the four directions, with three bows as the limit.

**II. On Visualization.**
The *Laozi’s Visualization Chart* states: When lecturing, first visualize the Three Colors, then the Three Ones. The Dao’s practice has six periods; when lecturing, it is always the three periods of post-meal, afternoon, and settling into stillness. Enter the fasting hall at these three periods, offer incense, bow three times, and circumambulate to sit in order.

When seated, if there is an assembly, the Dharma Master strikes the seat with a board, then places it before the knees. Closing the eyes and clasping the hands, visualize the head’s qi as azure, the hands’ qi as red, and the feet’s qi as white. The three qi encircle the body. Then visualize the Three Ones: the spirits of the three places are of one Dao.

The Dao is fundamentally one, yet in response to stimuli it manifests as three. Within and beyond the Three Realms, there is nowhere it does not reside. Governing transformation and presiding over beings, it is called the Three Heavens. The Most High proclaims teachings and attends to the scriptures, called the Three Primes. Lord Lao descends to humanity to perfect virtue, called the Three Ones.

The Three Ones dwell within humans, and humans possess three palaces: the brain is named the Upper Prime Palace, its spirit called Yi; the heart is named the Middle Prime Palace, its spirit called Xi; below the navel is named the Lower Prime Palace, its spirit called Wei. All resemble infants, each one inch in length. In silent sitting with proper posture, they are desireless and non-active, their bodies devoid of sensory response.

Next, visualize the Three Masters. First rise and face the seat, bowing three times before the Three Worthies at the seat’s front. Then visualize the Scripture Master, Register Master, and Initiation Master, each receiving one bow, totaling six bows, before ascending the high seat.

Next, visualize the attendants and guards. Upon ascending the seat and settling into a grand posture with the board set aside, strike the drum thirty-six times, swallow saliva thirty-six times, and with eyes closed, behold the Azure Dragon to the left, White Tiger to the right, Vermilion Bird before, and Dark Warrior behind. Beneath the feet, the Eight Trigrams’ divine tortoise and thirty-six lions prostrate in front. The headscarf bears the Seven Stars, the five viscera generate the five qi, and the net-patterned scripture covers the body. The Three Ones attend to the scriptures, each accompanied by a thousand sages and ten thousand riders, with jade lads and maidens as guards.

Visualization is the foremost of tranquil contemplation; entering samādhi is the gateway to stilling thoughts. Discernment and spiritual wandering are swift without haste.

Beneath the seat, visualize the Three Masters and Three Ones; upon ascending, further contemplate the majestic attendants. Three bows suffice to honor the Three Worthies; six bows disrupt the harmony of the four assemblies. Now, beneath the seat, there is no need for visualization—simply complete the three bows. Upon ascending, sit composed, first visualizing the Three Ones, then the Three Masters, and finally the majestic attendants. This simplified method of visualization allows the mind to circulate effortlessly, avoiding the entanglements of excessive detail, thus aligning with contemporary practice. Strictly adhering to ancient traditions, it is recorded here as follows.

**III. On Hymns and Recitations.**
The *Sutra of Original Form* states: When the patron of the fast invites the Dharma Master to begin the lecture, they rise with three offerings of incense in a precious censer, approach the Dharma Master, bow three times while kneeling, and request: "Disciples, fortunate across a thousand kalpas, have encountered the Dharma Wheel. The teachings bequeathed by the Primordial Beginning now circulate in the world. Today, though we uphold the Dao, we long to hear the numinous voice. We only beseech the Dharma Master to bestow the grace of compassion."

If the Dharma Master consents, they ascend the high seat and chant:
*"Disciples gaze upon the Dharma Master,
Daring to present our plea.
Sentient beings have long dwelled in darkness,
Yearning to hear the supreme Dharma sound.
Great compassion dispels the long night,
Establishing transformation anew across ten thousand kalpas.
The host establishes this meritorious fast,
Extending blessings to the four assemblies."*

When the Dharma Master ascends the high seat, they chant:
*"The fast’s duty lies in the Dao’s work,
The wondrous scriptures prized by the Primordial Beginning.
Thus is built the bridge of kalpas past,
To broadly ferry all beings and things.
Today, a pure fast is established,
Canopies and seats adorned in five hues.
Heavenly immortals wander above,
The Five Emperors arrayed in their directional offices.
The Merit Officers transmit decrees,
Guarding and attending to left and right.
I ascend the dragon-chariot seat,
Jade steps attached to the loom’s rest.
The Divine Empyrean aids in protection,
Heavenly demons dare not raise their eyes.
The Five Spirits remain unmoved,
As the Most High’s domain is proclaimed."*

Upon settling into the seat, they chant:
*"Within the non-action of the Great Dao,
Accumulated qi gives rise to form.
For the multitudes, a bridge is built,
Thus bequeathing the peerless scriptures.
Cultivating them, one attains eternal joy,
No longer born within the Three Realms.
Burning away the dust of the six senses,
With a single mind, listen in tranquil contemplation."*

Upon descending the seat, they chant:
*"The wondrous scriptures spread transformation,
Their distant, profound sounds echoing in the empyrean.
Equally receiving unimpeded wisdom,
The Three Beams ferry across the Yellow Ford.
Divine Empyrean’s Merit Officers,
Weary, briefly rest their spirits.
For the three assemblies’ toil, there shall be reward,
Repayment shall not betray the vow.
Further reports must be made,
Lest the officers grow resentful in waiting."*

Descending the seat and returning to their position, they bow to the Three Treasures.

In discussing the establishment of meritorious fields, all should aspire to brevity and simplicity. Excessive complexity makes practice difficult to follow. Today, it suffices for the practitioner to receive the patron’s bow and invitation, along with the hymns for ascending and descending the seat, to complete the Dharma ritual. Why insist on elaborate details? Thus, both methods are preserved here, lest preferences lead to omissions.

**On Arousing the Mind**
When hearing the Great Vehicle expounded, all must calm their minds and focus their attention. Though words pass through the ears, awakening is singular, yet outcomes differ due to six conditions, each yielding unequal practice:
1. Some perceive heterodoxy masquerading as orthodoxy and recognize its falsity;
2. Some mistake heterodoxy for orthodoxy and thus enter delusion;
3. Some hear the Great but awaken to the Small, entering the coarse;
4. Some hear the Small but awaken to the Great, entering the wondrous;
5. Some advance from the heart, spontaneously generating vows;
6. Some retreat from the heart, thus incurring fault.

This arises from the skill or clumsiness of the teaching, as well as the depth or shallowness of awakening.

The *Sutra of Original Boundary* states: If one awakens to the principle through a wise master’s skillful exposition of all dharmas—neither cultivated nor attained, neither extinguished nor born, neither existent nor nonexistent, neither cause nor effect, yet both existent and nonexistent, neither non-cause nor non-effect—skillfully resolving conditioned origination and provisional names, this is the Middle Way. Those who comprehend this teaching can resonate with diverse beings.

As the *Sutra of Original Boundary* states: *"The Heavenly Worthy expounds the Dharma with a single sound,
Yet sentient beings, according to their kind, each attain understanding."*
Further, as the *Sutra of Original Form* clarifies: The Heavenly Worthy, at Mount Chanli, expounded the *True Writ of the Cavernous Mystery*. For seventy thousand kalpas, they did not rise from the seat, and seven million beings, without constraint, attended. The dragon kings of the ten directions emitted light and came to listen to the Dharma.

The Heavenly Worthy’s disciple, Jinghui, said: *"Even dragons and beasts delight in the Dao—how much more so humans?"*
As the words concluded, a dragon king suddenly grew enraged, summoning clouds and hail that piled ten zhang high. Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy emitted the five-colored qi, weaving clouds into a canopy. Above, it shielded against the snow and hail, unshaken and unmoved, continuing the exposition as before. With such majestic power, the ten directions all awakened.

The *Scripture of Primordial Origin* states: If one expounds the doctrines of the Lesser Vehicle—teachings of arising and ceasing, of being and non-being, of cause and effect—such a speaker is called an "enlightened master."

The *Great Perfection Regulations* says: When listening to the Dharma, one should harmonize the five tones, attune the five virtues, and regularly practice chanting. Prolonged and refined melodies, gentle speech and measured words, gradually calming the voice—reciting sacred texts in response to the Dharma’s song, one eventually achieves a resonance like jade, forever severing the roots of worldly sound.

If one studies scriptures and cultivates practice, the *Thousand-Character Classic* should come first. Through exposition, one gains mastery, delivering others and perfecting oneself, transforming beings without end—this is the path of the Great Vehicle. Even if one’s talent is yet unrefined, one should arouse courageous resolve, aspiring to the Great Vehicle to transcend the Three Realms. Do not cling to the Lesser Vehicle, coveting offerings and delighting in the pleasures of humans and gods. Pursuing private gain, seeking petty benefits while neglecting great merit, composing ritual texts for others to solicit faith—intoxicated by wine and lust, indulging in sensory pleasures, falsely claiming the Great Vehicle while failing to comprehend it, learning minor arts yet vainly seeking great accomplishment—such delusion leads only to suffering. How pitiful!

The *Precepts of the Mysterious Capital* states: When a Dharma master propagates the teachings throughout the world to save the myriad people, it is the Way of all beings. One must not greedily accept wealth or transmit teachings to slaves and servants—violating this precept incurs a penalty of one year’s illness.

If a virtuous Dharma master practices austerity, wearing only the proper robes of the Way, it is fitting to make offerings. The *Great Precepts* says: To offer incense, oil, vegetarian meals, or a single coin’s worth of Dharma robes to a master brings a reward twenty-four myriad times greater. The merit is vast, the recompense profound—generation after generation will abound in prosperity, never knowing want.

First: If one mistakes the heterodox for the orthodox, one can discern what is not orthodox. As the *True Treasury Scripture* relates: The King of Tufang steadfastly believed in the true Dao. A sorcerer arrived, seeking to convert the king, teaching him false ways. Transforming his form, he soared into the sky, accompanied by music and chants. The palace women and maidens, gazing upon him, were bewitched. For three weeks and five days, none awoke from their delusion. The king admonished him: "You are a demonic trickster—leave at once!" The sorcerer replied: "I am the true Dao, exhorting the king to cultivate goodness." The king said: "I have heard that those who possess the Dao conceal their names and hide their traces, unknown to the multitude. The true Dao is formless—what has form is false." He commanded his minister, Tongling, to debate the sorcerer. Tongling declared: "External paths are full of deceit—there is nothing worth discussing." When they debated the source of wisdom, the sorcerer could not stand his ground. He vanished like a fleeting shadow, and his three thousand followers dared not emerge. Naturally, they were eradicated, and the kingdom returned to purity, turning toward the Great Vehicle. Thus, one knows that the heterodox cannot harm the orthodox—this has been so since ancient times.

Second: If one believes the heterodox to be orthodox, one falls into heterodoxy. As the *True Treasury Scripture* relates: The King of Zitong was virtuous but lacked wisdom. He was deluded by a wild fox, who said to its fox followers: "King Zitong delights in goodness and rejects evil, but his wisdom is shallow. I possess wondrous arts—able to fly and conceal myself. Before the royal palace, a hundred *zhang* above the earth, I will appear as a dignified man, discoursing on emptiness and expounding the Dharma. I will persuade the king to make offerings, even to the point of surrendering his life, and gather them to feast upon. Is this not a supreme plan?" The fox followers all voiced their approval. The fox king then recited hundreds of volumes of illusionary scriptures. It flew before the palace, a hundred *zhang* above the ground, seated in midair, reciting scriptures. The king’s family and attendants, young and old, wept in sorrow, sighing without end. They offered all the kingdom’s treasures in alms. Over thirty people then surrendered their lives. The fox king proclaimed: "Those who give their lives are the highest of beings." Suddenly, a fierce wind arose, and the corpses and treasures were all seized, taken to the fox den, where they feasted on human flesh. The fox then sent its young, transformed into human form, bearing treasures to the marketplace. Among the butchers’ stalls, fierce dogs fought over bones, startling the fox cubs. Unaware, they reverted to their true forms, and the dogs tore them apart. The butchers, terrified, reported this to the market officials, who informed the province. The province then memorialized the king. Seeing the treasures, the king recognized them all. He said: "These were all offered to the sacred Dao—how did they fall into the hands of wild foxes?" At that time, a great minister named Xianling addressed the king: "The teachings you heard earlier were the work of fox spirits. Though they recited the words, they did not understand their meaning. They urged others to do good, but their hearts and words were at odds. Their flight before the palace revealed their falsity." The king asked: "What can be done about this mistake?" Xianling replied: "Gather the troops and surround those hills." The foxes then transformed into human form, bowing to the king. When fierce dogs approached, they reverted to wild foxes, and the dogs tore them apart. The king ordered his ministers to excavate the fox dens, where they recovered the stolen goods. Thus, one knows that without profound wisdom, a king may be deluded by the heterodox.

Third, if one hears the great but awakens to the small, one enters the coarse. As the *Shengxuan Jing* states: Dao Ling asked, "Among the multitude, those of minor practice are many, while those of great aspiration are few. If we do not expound the teachings, there will be no means for awakening. Yet if we teach the great Dao, we may encounter those of small capacity; if we teach the lesser vehicle, we may obstruct those of great practice." The Heavenly Worthy replied: "This is not difficult. The capacity lies in the conditions of the request, not in their number. Those who request with small conditions shall be taught the small; those who request with great conditions shall be taught the great. Yet their awakening and entry are also without constancy—some hear the small and awaken to the small, some hear the small and awaken to the great, some hear the great and awaken to the great, and some hear the great yet regress to the small. Formerly, there were over eight thousand four hundred good men and women who, though they understood and believed, clung to the pursuit of the supreme Dao. They harbored the mind of attainment, seeking the thought of non-attainment, and rigidly adhered to the great vehicle. Yet their efforts bore no fruit, and after more than four thousand years, they attained only the rank of earth immortals."

Fourth, if one hears the small but awakens to the great, one enters the wondrous. The *Shengxuan Jing* states: The Heavenly Worthy said, "When I first expounded the Dao in the Great Fuli Kingdom of the Beginning Azure Heaven, there was an earth immortal surnamed Hong, named Faqi, who, for the sake of teaching, requested that I open and expound the teachings. Observing his capacity, I deemed him unready for the great Dao and, following his mind, taught the Three Mixed Sutras. At that time, among the countless assembly, there were over one hundred eighty-six thousand who, upon hearing the lesser vehicle, deeply awakened to the great Dao, instantly transcended the Three Realms, and swiftly departed the Dao realm."

Fifth, if one advances from the heart and spontaneously generates the vow. The *Benji Jing* states: "If there are those who praise and expound the wondrous meaning, one should praise and extol their merit and virtue, lest external demons disrupt and disturb their work." It further states: "When explaining the meaning and purport, do not allow the Dharma master to encounter obstructions. Provide for their needs with clarity, supplying what they lack, so that the wondrous teachings may surely circulate." The *Benxiang Jing* states: "When the Heavenly Worthy expounded the Dao, eighty-four thousand in the assembly opened their minds and understood, generating the mind of the unsurpassed true and correct Dao without retrogression. They instantly eliminated seventy-two knots and a hundred kinds of afflictions." It further states: "There was a son of a elder named Falong, who, with faith, understanding, and reverence, led seven hundred twenty thousand to devote their minds to the true emptiness of the supreme Dao." The *Zhenzang Jing* states: "When the Heavenly Worthy expounded the Dao, three youths each generated distinct vows: the first, Huili, vowed to cultivate and practice; the second, Baoming, vowed to expound the sutras; the third, Shanji, vowed to study the Dao." The sutra states: "Huili and his retinue all vowed, saying, 'We shall cultivate the great vehicle without retrogression, comprehend the nature of all dharmas, reach their ultimate limit, awaken to the great vehicle, and accomplish the supreme Dao.'" "Baoming generated the vast vow, saying, 'I shall expound the great vehicle Dharma, vowing to ferry sentient beings to the place of liberation and accomplish the supreme Dao.'" "Shanji, with heroic vigor and diligence, generated the vast vow, saying, 'I shall study the great vehicle Dao, cultivate the Four Great Cities, vanquish the five rebellious thieves, expel the seven delusive demons, slay the ten obstructive maras, cleave the darkness of ignorance, carve out the hearts of the three thieves, and remain steadfast and unyielding.'" It further states: "There were great disciples who cultivated, recited, and expounded the revered sutras, generating faith and practicing without negligence. One should know that such persons, in the presence of all the worthies, perform meritorious deeds and plant fields of blessing. For immeasurable kalpas, they have revered the great vehicle of their teachers. Now, encountering these sutras, they generate faith."

Sixth, if one retreats from the heart and thereby incurs transgression. The *Shengxuan Jing* states: "There were eight hundred seventy-two persons who, upon hearing the great vehicle, included eight men and eleven women who generated disbelief and withdrew from their seats. They were deluded by heavenly maras and heterodox paths, their minds confused. These individuals immediately fell gravely ill, their hair and body hair falling out. They died and entered the Three Wretched Realms, being born deaf and blind. Even if they possessed ears and eyes, they would only speak of goodness and praise, never perceiving or hearing anything." One should know that the depth or shallowness of awakening to the Dharma arises entirely from the mind. These various conditions sufficiently demonstrate and confirm this.

There are four conditions for receiving and upholding the *Chao*:
Though the sutra texts speak of emptiness and existence, without cultivation, they cannot be accomplished. If one cultivates and upholds them, one must be true and steadfast, aligning one’s practice with the rules and standards. As one ascends through the Dao ranks, those who defile or disdain the numinous texts shall clearly incur punishment.

First, the condition of reading and recitation.
The *Siji Mingke* states: "When reciting the sutras, one must ensure that words and phrases connect without omission or skipping. If one loses a single sentence in the celestial sound, one must recite a hundred more words; if one loses two sentences, two hundred more; if one loses five sentences, five hundred more. If one initially loses a sentence while reciting, one must recite an entire section to compensate. Upon the thirtieth infraction, one shall undergo the punishment of the Mountain of Knives." It further states: "When reciting the sutras, one must fix one’s gaze on the text and concentrate the mind on the divine truth. One must not, while facing the sutra, entertain other thoughts or distracting notions, thereby disrupting the celestial sound. Upon the thirtieth infraction, one shall undergo the punishment of the Mountain of Knives." It further states: "When reciting fewer than a thousand words, one must not drink while facing the sutra. From a thousand to five thousand words, one may drink once; from five thousand to ten thousand words, twice; above ten thousand words, thrice. Upon the thirtieth infraction, one shall incur the punishment of the left official. If one recites up to ten thousand words and becomes mentally fatigued or qi-exhausted, one may pause to rest, then resume and complete the section. However, one must not leave unfinished sentences overnight. Upon the tenth infraction, one shall die and enter hell." "When reciting the sutras, if good men and women wish to listen, men should stand to the left and women to the right, with distinct positions for east and west, and separate places for Daoists and laity. Men and women must not be mixed or disorderly, nor share the same bed or seat."

Monks must follow behind those who have left the household and may not walk ahead; violations shall incur the punishment of the left official. The *Xuandu Precepts* states: "If one discusses worldly affairs while reciting the sutras, three *sheng* of oil shall be forfeited as penalty." It further says: "If one’s recitation becomes disordered and one asks to clarify a corrupted passage, five *sheng* of oil shall be forfeited." The *Qingwen Xia* states: "Recite the sutras as if facing the Most High. One must not act arrogantly, laugh frivolously, or discuss vulgar matters of worldly honor and profit. The attendant immortal youths shall report one’s name to the Three Heavens’ Rectifiers, who will memorialize the Most High thrice. If this occurs, you shall surely lose the sutras, and ghosts and spirits will torment you with chaotic punishments. You shall not die a natural death—how then can you attain immortality?"

It further states: "If one receives the sutras without a master’s transmission, the attendant immortal youths shall constantly oversee one’s punishments, and calamity shall extend to seven generations." The *Golden Register Simplified Text* says: "When the senior monk recites the sutras, he shall bow once to the scripture master, the register master, and the preceptor, while the rest shall follow the usual procedures. All shall do so upon first ascending the seat; after one recitation, if the sutras are recited again, the initial rites need not be repeated, but they shall be performed once more the following day. During recitation, one must not converse with those of lower rank. If a passage is left unfinished, one may not pause midway; if one does pause, one must restart from the beginning. After five hundred words, one may drink clear water or swallow saliva."

This differs slightly from the *Four Poles Alliance Regulations*. The *Alliance Regulations* state: "After ten thousand words, one may pause and resume from where one left off," which seems more lenient, whereas this text is entirely strict.

During recitation, one must maintain focused mindfulness and observe the precepts to elicit spiritual responses. The *Original Boundary Sutra* states: "If one recites and practices this sutra diligently day and night, wherever one resides shall naturally be peaceful and joyful. Wherever one is reborn, one shall dwell in a pure land." It further says: "If one receives, upholds, delights in, and recites even a single verse of this sutra, in that very moment, one shall eradicate immeasurable and boundless karmic afflictions from past lives. It is like a room filled with darkness for ages—with a single thought, the light of a lamp dispels all darkness. If one enters the great sea and encounters fierce winds, reciting this sutra shall calm the waves. If one enters mountains and forests and meets poisonous insects or ferocious beasts, reciting this sutra shall make them retreat. If one encounters bandits or enemies, reciting this sutra shall dissolve enmity. If one is in fear, reciting this sutra shall dispel ghosts and demons. Know that with a serene mind and focused recitation, nothing shall fail to be accomplished."

The Great Brahmā King, facing a great drought in his kingdom, invited the revered sutras and thereby ended the disaster. A king afflicted with many troubles, his kingdom beset by obstacles, invited the revered sutras, and his illnesses and delusions were swiftly cured. Know that the sutras possess spiritual power, and recitation shall surely bring response.

The *Supreme Ultimate Hidden Commentary* states: "When reciting the *Daode Jing*, thirty-six thousand immortal youths and jade maidens shall attend, burning incense, scattering flowers, and summoning the assembled immortals." It further says: "After reciting the *Daode Jing* ten thousand times, a cloud chariot shall descend to welcome you. If it does not come, recite it thrice in a month, and it shall surely arrive." The *True Treasury Sutra* states: "Once, the Jade Seal Youth burned incense and recited this sutra. Suddenly, immortal youths and jade maidens filled the sky, arriving all at once to burn rare incense and praise the sacred text, astonishing the entire kingdom. The Jade Seal Youth remained unperturbed. Today, in households holding purification rites, though the reciter may possess the finest voice and diction, those seated below often fail to focus their minds. Some chatter incessantly, whispering to one another; others vie for sensual pleasures or compete for wealth. The great virtuous ones recline in slumber, heads bowed in arrogance. If those above cannot uphold rectitude, how can those below be reverent? First, this breaches proper decorum; second, it fails to inspire faith; third, it invites the host’s disdain; fourth, it brings divine punishment upon oneself. One must reflect deeply—better to earnestly admonish the virtuous. If one can encourage the assembly to diligence, what cause is there for concern? If one neglects mutual exhortation, one extinguishes the Dao and its teachings."

**Second: The Benefits of Listening to Sutra Recitation**
The *Natural Scripture Formula* states: "When listeners reach a passage in the sutra, they should bow in their hearts and make vows with sincere devotion, and they shall surely receive a response." The *Xuandu Precepts* states: "If one listens to the sutras while leaning or sitting improperly, one shall forfeit one *sheng* of oil. If one’s mind is not focused on purity and emptiness, or if one’s thoughts wander and one appears weary to others, three *sheng* of oil shall be forfeited. If one listens with a concentrated mind, it is no different from receiving and upholding the sutras oneself." The *Original Boundary Sutra* states: "If one listens to this sutra with a single-minded, upright focus, rejoicing and leaping with delight, savoring its meaning and forgetting sleep and food, unaware of the passage of time, know that this person has encountered it in past lives. Though temporarily born in the lower realms, they are entrusted with wisdom in the human world. Before long, they shall ascend as immortals and ultimately attain the Dao."

**Third: The Conditions for Making Offerings to Those Who Uphold the Sutras**
The *True Treasury Sutra* states: "The Heavenly Worthy asked the Youth of Good Clarity: 'If one gives away gold, jade, and precious treasures, is this person’s merit great?' The youth replied: 'The merit is rare, yet it does not compare to the merit of expounding, transcribing, receiving, upholding, and making offerings to this sutra, which surpasses the former by a hundred thousand million times. This sutra is called the City of Dharma Power, the Benevolent Protector of All Beings, the Remover of Delusions and Obstacles.'"

The *Original Boundary Sutra* states: "If one gives away family wealth, or even sells wife and children to purchase fragrant oils, various ritual implements, and vegetarian meals to offer and provide for those who uphold this sutra, the merit thus obtained is immeasurable. Why? Because this person can accomplish the merit of the Heavenly Worthies of the Ten Directions and give birth to all the sages."

Thus the *Scripture of Ascending the Mystery* states: "The merit of making offerings to those who uphold the sutra is comparable, followed by providing fragrant oils and lamps, and presenting banners and flowers."

The *Original Boundary Sutra* states: "If a king or commoner offers this sutra with palace halls, canopied seats, jeweled parasols, banners, incense, flowers, lamps, and candles, then you, the four assemblies, along with the Heavenly Emperors, the Three and Five Officials, the celestial dragons, spirits, ghosts, vajra warriors, and the true attendants of the sutra, should lead your retinues to follow, revere, and make offerings, protecting their lands and safeguarding their people."

The *Scripture of Fundamental Conduct* states: "Formerly, there was a woman who received and upheld this sutra, reciting it morning and evening. Her husband constantly provided incense and offerings. The wife then ascended to heaven and was titled the Primordial Sovereign of Pure Conduct. After the husband’s life ended, the sutra entered the great mountains. When he fully recounted the merit of his support, the wife came and bestowed the sutra upon him. He then ascended to the Southern Palace, and after a hundred years, was reborn into a royal family, where he greatly received the sutra’s teachings and became a True Person of the Nine Palaces.

There was also a worthy gentleman who upheld this sutra, but his wife, begrudging and unwilling to share with her husband, caused him to ascend to heaven alone. Later, she transformed into a starving vulture. Through his transformative guidance, she regained a female form, received and upheld the sutra’s teachings, and is now the Empress Consort of the Primordial Sovereign of the Southern Culmen.

Know this: upholding the sutra and revering the Dharma is clearly not in vain. To slander and scorn it is to invite one’s own punishment."

The *Fourfold Luminous Sutra on the Causes of Slandering the Dharma* states: The *True Treasury Sutra* says: "Beings who do not believe in the Dharma slander it and extinguish it. They do not believe that the Three Treasures exist within the roots of faith, nor that past and future are real. They do not believe the Great Vehicle is the foundation, nor that beings are equal in nature to the Heavenly Worthies. They do not believe that all dharmas are quiescent and rootless, without cause or effect, nor that beings have accumulated seeds from immeasurable kalpas, formless yet without birth or extinction. Such disbelief is called destroying the Dharma, extinguishing the Dharma. The Dharma cannot be extinguished, but obstructing and failing to perceive it is called extinguishing the Dharma. Having extinguished the Dharma, one obtains a bodily form, entering samsara without end, inevitably falling into hell with no chance of escape."

The *Scripture of Fundamental Marks* states: "If one regards the sutra as mere dirt or grass, utterly lacking reverence, or sees others practicing goodness and mocks them behind their backs, never offering support or respect—such a person comes from the six paths of rebirth, having only just attained human form, and thus does not believe in the Dharma."

The *True Treasury Sutra* states: "In a past kalpa, there were five impoverished men who did not believe in the sutra’s teachings, nor that beings possess the true nature of the Dao, nor that beings are the wondrous Dharma of the sutra, nor that beings are unborn and undying, nor that the minds of beings are vast as the sea, nor that beings are the gathering of the Great Void. Due to such disbelief, they contracted grave illness, entering the Dark Prison in life, in death, in eating, and in breathing. All good men and women should each reflect: do not give rise to disbelief."

The Heavenly Worthy then composed a verse:
*"Those who do not believe in the Dharma,
Slander the virtuous and good.
In death, they receive the retribution of Fengdu,
Their forms shattered on the sword trees.
For ten thousand kalpas, no end to their release,
Their souls and spirits ache with broken bowels.
Their cries resound without cease,
As hell-wardens boil them in cauldrons.
Suffering without respite,
Eyes glaring in all directions.
Who could endure such torment?
Deluded and recklessly wild.
I exhort the cultivators of truth:
Cultivate blessings to forever avoid calamity."*

Yet the words of the sages are fundamentally not false or exaggerated. It is disbelief in the Dharma that brings calamity upon oneself. If one further claims that the sutra is attended by eighteen thousand jade maidens and jade youths, disbelief only deepens. Some expose it carelessly, mix it with secular texts, fail to cleanse their mouths or hands, or neglect protective purity—any deviation from the proper ritual of reciting the sutra is called slander.

The *Lower Inquiry* states: "If the sutra is defiled and not cleansed with fragrant water, the hun and po souls will scatter and fall."

The *Original Boundary Sutra* states: "If anyone slanders this sutra, harboring disbelief, scorning the Dharma treasure, and doubting or destroying the sacred texts—know that such a person has for immeasurable kalpas sunk into the lower realms of ghosts, enduring all manner of suffering and passing through countless forms before barely regaining human birth. Yet they remain foolish and obstinate, understanding nothing, habituated to evil causes, unable to believe or accept. Their actions are unwholesome, every move a source of sin. Turning from the correct to the perverse, forsaking truth for worldliness, the Three Offices and Nine Bureaus record their deeds in the ledgers of transgressions, inscribing their names in the Black Register of the Dead. Some in this very life are constantly beset by suffering; others violate royal laws, arrested and beaten with whips."

Or they may suffer from afflictions of malignant winds and leprous infestations, beset by cares, distress, and hardship, impoverished and destitute. Or they may be deluded and confounded by external demons and heterodox ways, their minds still bound to the worldly realm, spurned and scorned by others. Wherever they wander, they encounter no favorable conditions; once they lose the human Way, they forever stray from the domain of the worthy. At death, they descend into hell, with no prospect of return, enduring retribution in dark prisons, bound fast behind heavy bars. Day and night they are tortured, never beholding the Three Luminaries. Some embrace the bronze pillar, their bodies charred and scorched; others ascend the mountain of knives, their pain and poison unbearable.
