If one sees fine blossoms, may all delight in scattering them before the sages, their marks of excellence complete;
If one sees chariots and horses, may all attain the Dao and non-action, riding phoenixes and mounting dragons;
If one sees stringed music and song, may all play with scriptures and expound them freely, finding joy in the Dao.

If one sees blessed food, may all be ever sated and full, enjoying the celestial kitchens of the world, their virtue flowing to their hosts as water returns to the sea, their ancestral temples enduring, ever dwelling in noble splendor, reborn with the four assemblies in royal households;

If one sees alms-giving, may all see misfortune vanish into the nine depths of darkness, blessings arise in the ten directions, their virtue vast as mountains and seas, all flourishing without exception, seven generations ascending to heaven, their descendants wise and loyal, their wealth and honor towering, every desire fulfilled, learning the Dao to become flying immortals, riding clouds and mounting dragons;

When Daoists sit without, may we four elements unite in virtue, our bodies one with the true Dao, ever abiding in the Mysterious Capital, our teachers and friends naturally present, delivering the ten directions, the world receiving grace, carefree in being and non-being, penetrating the wondrous gate with insight.

---

The One Hundred and Twenty-Nine Precepts, as stated in the *Scripture of Ascending the Mystery*:
Distance bodily conduct, depart from verbal transgressions, eliminate evil thoughts, eradicate karmic roots, sever sound and form, relinquish love and desire, abandon frivolous habits, wash away filth and defilement, ease contention and constraint, open what is oppressed, broaden the heart and nature, relax what is hurried, avoid fixation, reduce all toil, cast off all burdens, dispel doubts and fancies, restrain movement, subdue restlessness, weary of all ends, sever all obstacles, extinguish all traces, widen all views, dim all wisdom, suppress all obstructions, trace all delusions to their source, halt all leaks, sweep away all afflictions, heal all sores, discard all calculations, cease all seeking, fell all stumps, cut down all seeds, reap greed and recklessness, exhaust hesitation, scatter attachments, shed afflictions, govern the wandering mind, have no preferences, have no aversions, practice non-action, relinquish all notions of self, relinquish all notions of non-self, relinquish distinctions of self and other, dispel empty imaginings, banish confusion, banish lustful thoughts, diligently practice what is possible, doubt not emptiness, equalize beauty and ugliness, do not stray or regress, constantly abide in non-being, sever imaginings of existence, cultivate victorious thoughts, skillfully guard against harm, do not waver, think not of self, think not of others, think not of idle fancies, have no constant standard, have no fixed target, leave no lingering regrets, do not dwell on the past, have no hesitation, endure what is unendurable, the Dao is not this, sever all imaginings, constantly abide in non-being, non-being is not non-action, practice non-practice, act non-action, imagine non-imagining, arouse non-arousal, without boundary or cessation, without boundary in action, without boundary in thought, without boundary in abiding, examine all natures, understand there is no root, like formlessness, cannot be filled, yet by that which cannot be filled, order yourself, when there is no thought, use cessation to surpass, observe all things as empty space, the heart without desire yet ever benevolent, not distinguishing purity from impurity.

Know one, and eliminate one; do not, through one, arise in form. As through one, people transcend boundaries.

Know that through boundlessness one enters non-action; know that through non-action one enters emptiness; know that through emptiness one attains extinction; know that through extinction one becomes the Dao; know that through becoming the Dao one attains the greatest; know tranquility as tranquility, know tranquility as joy, know joy and sorrow no more, know the absence of sorrow as supreme peace.

Reduce attachments, refine intentions and attitudes, cease right and wrong, harbor no duality, cast off all burdens, lay aside all hindrances, sever all connections, carve away causes and conditions, guard the turning of the heart, engage in non-engagement, have no partiality, equalize good and evil, still all imaginings, relinquish notions of self, have no constant abode, unite in non-being, cease all cessation, abide in non-abiding, arouse without boundary, observe the dharma thread by thread, become one with non-being, know that being arises from non-being, know that through boundlessness one enters liberation, know that through the greatest one attains non-being, know that revering non-action is the ultimate.

These are the one hundred and twenty.

---

Below are the Nine Precepts:
Amidst the gathering of beloved multitudes, the heart rests in the treasury of Daoist precepts;
In the dwelling of sorrow and affliction, the heart abides in the hall of benevolent deliverance;
Within the chamber of dark obscurity, the aspiration lies at the threshold of extinction;
Leaning against an unstable dwelling, the heart is under the protection of expedient means;
Sitting upon the ground of serpents and vipers, the heart treads the path of renunciation;
Dwelling in the thicket of tigers and leopards, the heart resides in the sanctuary of merit and virtue □□;
□□□□□, the heart rests in the hermitage of contemplating extinction;
Standing □□□□, the heart is in the garden of thorns and brambles;
□□□□□, the heart is behind the barrier of armor and defense.

Such is the observance of precepts by us: practicing the expedient means of wisdom, delivering from the peril of death and rebirth, extinguishing all imaginings, eradicating all thoughts, returning to that which is extinguished by nothing, attaining the true Dao.

---

The One Hundred and Eighty Precepts of Lord Lao were originally expounded for the Covenant of Might and other assemblies.

Lord Lao said: Though a person may live ten thousand years, without upholding the precepts and disciplines, how do they differ from an ancient tree or enduring stone? Better to uphold the precepts for a single day, practice the Dao, and die, than to live without transgression. Upholding the precepts at death, one supplements the celestial offices and ascends as an immortal through liberation in the corpse.

Though a person may hold the position of king or duke in the world, at death they bear heavy transgressions, which do not benefit the hun and po souls—the souls suffer punishment. Orthodox Unity Daoists, enlightened and practicing accordingly.

When upholding the precepts, disciples bathe, abstain from the five flavors and five pungent plants, and change their clothing. Disciples should observe the ritual teachings of their masters, prostrate themselves, and listen to the prohibitions and precepts. Once the prohibitions and precepts are received, they should copy them once and recite them diligently in practice.

The master says: Let all worthies listen clearly. Among the ten thousand things under heaven, none endure forever. Human life is subject to death; things formed must decay. The sun rises and sets; the moon waxes and fills, then wanes. From ancient times to the present, who has ever remained forever? Only the Dao and its virtue endure. Today is also good, this month is also good, this hour is also good, all worthies are also good, the lineage of masters is also good, the disciples are also good, the ten thousand spirits are all present, the officers and soldiers have all arrived. Today, for the sake of Lord Lao, for the sake of teaching all worthies, for the sake of the world’s people cherishing their lives, for the sake of the disciples’ good hearts, we confer the prohibitions and weighty precepts. Let there be assent, and after the triple praise, we shall then expound the precepts.

The precepts state:
Disciples must not hoard excessively;
Must not steal people’s belongings;
Must not wrongfully take anything worth more than a single coin;
Must not raise pigs or sheep;
Must not eat the five pungent plants;
Must not write in cursive script for others;
Must not harm others with poisonous medicines;
Must not recklessly pick flowers or fruits;
Must not form close ties with soldiers;
Must not use gold or silver vessels for eating;
Must not treat disciples with disrespect;
Must not speak recklessly;
Must not eat alone;
Must not be privy to others’ marriages;
Must not gossip about others’ faults;
Must not speak of others’ private matters;
Must not encourage others to commit suicide;
Must not kill out of hatred;
Must not act selfishly;
Must not be arrogant;
Must not engage in abusive language or cursing;
Must not neglect the treatment of illness;
Must not bathe naked;
Must not drain water sources;
Must not disrespect the elderly;
Must not engage in flirtatious behavior;
Must not show partiality to relatives;
Must not live separately from the household;
Must not recklessly curse others to be slaves;
Must not brand the faces of slaves;
Must not rejoice in others’ deaths;
Must not stare at others with wide eyes;
Must not praise others to their faces while speaking ill of them behind their backs;
Must not cast poisonous medicines into deep waters, rivers, or seas;
Must not show partiality or distance toward others’ elders;
Must not forcibly beg or disturb the common people;
Must not act as the head of ceremonies for worldly people;
Must not engage in astrology, divination, or predicting celestial phenomena;
Must not teach others lewdness, or cause the separation of husband and wife;
Must regard disciples as one’s own children;
Must not spit bitterness toward others;
Must not snatch the fire from others’ underworld;
Must not claim others’ achievements as one’s own;
Must not slander others’ utensils as inferior;
Must not be picky about food, favoring some and disliking others;
Must not speak ill of others in their presence or absence;
Must not interfere in worldly rituals or unjust matters;
Must not, in winter, dig up hibernating creatures or disturb their self-preservation without urgent cause;
Must not wander recklessly;
Must not recklessly climb trees;
Must not throw filthy objects into wells;
Must not be greedy or attached to one’s household.

Must not slander virtuous people as slaves or servants;
Must ever cherish and pity all people, treating the ignorant as insects, and diligently seek life, day and night without weariness.

Must not destroy money or property;
Must diligently avoid evil people;
Must diligently consume food and drink;
Must not practice grain avoidance, for grain avoidance is not the Dao of immortality.

Must not discard written or inscribed objects before privies;
Must not be loquacious;
Must not raid nests or break eggs;
Must not associate with soldiers as companions;
Must not create taboos for others;
Must not sacrifice to ghosts and spirits in hopes of luck;
Must not recklessly bathe in lakes or seas;
Must not engage in lewdness with household members;
Must not store poison in vessels;
Must not gallop horses or drive chariots without cause;
Must not recklessly beat the six domestic animals or living beings.

Must not form food into balls with the hands;
For every ten thousand people, must wish that the host may gain a fortunate person, calling you "Master" and holding you in awe;
Do not act lightly or rashly, for the world despises many, and good people are few;
Do not be despondent, for the Dao itself protects you;
When others act with malice toward you, respond only with goodness;
Goodness repels evil as water extinguishes fire.

Must not discuss others’ food preferences with disciples;
Without cause, must not recklessly accept others’ gifts or fees;
Must not recklessly breach dikes or lakes;
Female disciples must not launder clothes for male disciples, and clothing must not exceed three changes;
Must not personally attend to the sick—let the sick come to you;
Must not eat the flesh of living beings, but only vegetables as a constant practice.

Practicing the Dao without a home, one may lodge and recite the One Hundred Eighty Precepts;
Spirits guard in threefold layers—be cautious where you stay, and inspect it first.
Entering a household, must first ask the names and titles of the elders;
Must not seek treasures extensively;
Must not drink alcohol;
Must not rebel or abandon fundamentals for trivialities;
Must not commit adultery with others’ wives;
Must not kill living or wriggling creatures;
Must not burn or ruin objects worth more than a single coin;
Must not throw food into fire;
Must not tread on the six domestic animals with the feet;
Must not send excessive written correspondence;
Must not set fire to fields, wildlands, or forests;
Must not know or prognosticate on military or state affairs;
Must not recklessly fell trees;
Must not frequently visit kings, nobles, or officials;
Must not covet wealth or property;
Must not overeat or overdrink;
Must not trade in slaves or servants;
Must not practice martial arts or music;
Must not speak of others’ misdeeds;
Must not separate families;
Must not send slanderous letters;
Must not exalt oneself;
Must not recklessly dig the earth or destroy mountains and rivers;
Must not blind others’ eyes;
Must not covet others’ possessions;
Must not criticize one’s teacher;
Must not disdain scriptural teachings;
Must not observe the mating of the six domestic animals;
Must not bully others with power;
Must not carry blades—those in the military are not bound by this precept;
Must not be easily angered;
Must not urinate while standing;
Must not wander with disheveled hair;
Must not curse others to death;
Must not use filthy substances to deceive others;
Must not speak of others’ parents’ past good or evil;
Must not reveal others’ private matters;
Must not be partial only to one’s own clan;
Must not levy taxes with secular people;
Must not design tombs, residences, or construct houses for others;
Must not teach others to hunt or harm living beings.

Must not show partiality toward disciples;
If someone gives something to one person, another must not resent them for not giving to themselves.

Must not form cliques with secular people;
Must not gallop about in worldly affairs or offer condolences at funerals;
Must not select fine dwellings or beds for rest;
Must not criticize others’ possessions or praise one’s own;
Must not startle or frighten others;
Must not slander others in official settings;
Must not forcibly take others’ possessions under the guise of kindness;
Must not wander aimlessly or race about day and night;
Must not cage birds or beasts;
Must not peer through walls to watch others’ women;
Must not block wells or ponds.

Must not recklessly open and read others’ letters;
Must reflect on the kindness that grants you long life and not act recklessly;
Must encourage others to enter famous mountains to study.
Must not hoard wealth or treasures to invite misfortune;
Must not bury or hide objects.

Must not wrong others;
Must diligently avoid suspicion;
Must treat one another with mutual respect, like parents, brothers, or sisters.
Must not light fires on level ground;
Must not scatter thorny branches on roads;
Must not recklessly perform rites before ghosts and spirits;
Must not keep excessive secular divination charts or books on the eight spirits;
Must not urinate on living plants or in water others drink;
Must not intimately associate with widows;
Must not recklessly borrow or offer others’ possessions as gifts or bribes;
Must not vouch for others in contracts or bonds;
Must not draft lawsuits or know others’ affairs;
Must not speak loudly or harshly—always maintain a gentle smile;
Must not read others’ confidential letters;
Must not startle birds or beasts;
When receiving food or drink from others, always burn incense and pray for the peace of all under heaven;
If someone curses you, do not respond;
If others slander you, cultivate the Great Dao within and do not fear;
When the world faces disasters, floods, or droughts, do not be troubled or weary.

When visiting households, must not expect food or drink;
Must not speak with women alone in dark rooms;
Without cause, must not gather for feasting;
Upon seeing others kill birds or beasts, must generate great compassion and wish to deliver them.
Must not disrespect the worthy and sagely;
I shall deliver you—when you encounter true persons or the sagely who achieve liberation through transformation, always follow the Dao;
Do not practice even one worldly rite;
Must reflect on frugality and emulate the pure and virtuous;
Measure food and drink with restraint.

Must not hoard possessions;
Must handle affairs and offerings with ease, avoiding excess difficulty.
When entering another country, must first inquire about its prohibitions;
Must not travel alone—go with others;
Diligently recite the One Hundred Eighty Precepts;
Must not act as a bandit or thief.

Lord Lao spoke to Ji, saying: "All the immortals, worthies, and sagely beings of ancient times attained the Dao through the One Hundred Eighty Precepts. The *One Hundred Illnesses* are expounded in the *Scripture of Laozi’s Emptiness and Non-Being*: Thus the sage seeks blessings before their signs appear and severs misfortune before it arises, for calamities grow from the slightest beginnings, and illness arises from the faintest stirrings.

People deem small good deeds of no benefit and so refuse to perform them; they regard minor wrongs as harmless and so refuse to amend them. Small goods left unaccumulated, great virtue cannot be achieved; minor evils left unchecked, great transgressions are formed. Therefore, these one hundred illnesses are set forth to make known the grounds of one’s downfall.

The One Hundred Illnesses:
Capricious joy and anger are one illness;
Forsaking righteousness for profit is one illness;
Lust that corrupts virtue is one illness;
Fixation and clinging attachment are one illness;
Wishing death upon those one hates is one illness;
Indulging greed to conceal faults is one illness;
Slandering others to praise oneself is one illness;
Arbitrarily altering matters to justify oneself is one illness;
Loose speech and fondness for talk are one illness;
Pursuing wrongs to gratify oneself is one illness;
Using cunning to belittle others is one illness;
Exploiting power to act recklessly is one illness;
Rejecting others while deeming oneself right is one illness;
Harming the vulnerable and solitary is one illness;
Overpowering others by force is one illness;
Coercing others through intimidation is one illness;
Seeking to outdo others in speech is one illness;
Lending without thought of repayment is one illness;
Distorting others to justify oneself is one illness;
Using rectitude to wound others is one illness;
Taking pleasure in others’ misfortune is one illness;
Boasting of one’s joy and anger is one illness;
Deeming oneself wise while foolish is one illness;
Claiming credit for one’s achievements is one illness;
Erasing others’ merits is one illness;
Resenting one’s toil is one illness;
Taking falsehood for truth is one illness;
Delighting in exposing others’ faults is one illness;
Using wealth to arrogantly belittle others is one illness;
Using status to disparage others is one illness;
Envying the rich while poor is one illness;
Mocking the noble while base is one illness;
Flattering others to curry favor is one illness;
Parading virtue to display oneself is one illness;
Sabotaging others’ success is one illness;
Disrupting the public for private gain is one illness;
Habitual mumbling and sighing are one illness;
Endangering others to secure oneself is one illness;
Harboring hidden malice is one illness;
Inciting rebellion is one illness;
Excessive stinginess and scant love are one illness;
Judging matters without justice is one illness;
Shifting blame onto others is one illness;
Obstructing and entrapping others is one illness;
Exploiting others’ weaknesses is one illness;
Swearing false oaths is one illness;
Bestowing favors in expectation of repayment is one illness;
Demanding repayment for unbestowed gifts is one illness;
Regretting gifts given to others is one illness;
Indulging in self-pity and contention is one illness;
Cursing insects and animals is one illness;
Using sorcery to harm others is one illness;
Slandering the highly talented is one illness;
Resenting those who surpass oneself is one illness;
Poisoning food and drink is one illness;
An unbalanced mind is one illness;
Mocking the worthy is one illness;
Dwelling on past grievances is one illness;
Refusing admonition and instruction is one illness;
Outwardly feigning closeness while inwardly distant is one illness;
Sending letters to ruin others is one illness;
Indulging in foolish chatter is one illness;
Fretful impatience and rashness are one illness;
Beating others without cause is one illness;
Insisting on one’s own correctness is one illness;
Excessive suspicion and scant trust are one illness;
Mocking the mad and deranged is one illness;
Squatting or lounging without propriety is one illness;
Vulgar and abusive speech is one illness;
Disrespecting the elderly and young is one illness;
Reviling others’ abilities is one illness;
Obstinacy and self-will are one illness;
Indulging in fine food and drink is one illness;
Taking pleasure in confining others is one illness;
Flattering like a demon or ghost is one illness;
Craving gain while harboring deceit is one illness;
Double-tongued and untrustworthy speech is one illness;
Reckless behavior while drunk is one illness;
Cursing wind and rain is one illness;
Cruel speech and fondness for killing are one illness;
Teaching others to harm is one illness;
Meddling in others’ affairs is one illness;
Peeping through holes and crevices is one illness;
Borrowing without thought of return is one illness;
Fleeing debts and theft are one illness;
Contradictory speech is one illness;
Delighting in opposition and conflict is one illness;
Teasing and provoking others is one illness;
Deliberately misleading others is one illness;
Plundering nests and destroying eggs is one illness;
Dismembering fetuses and mutilating forms is one illness;
Damaging others with water or fire is one illness;
Mocking the blind, deaf, mute, or disfigured is one illness;
Arranging others’ marriages is one illness;
Instructing others to beat others is one illness;
Teaching others to do evil is one illness;
Concealing malice and forsaking love is one illness;
Inciting misfortune and leading others astray is one illness;
Coveting whatever one sees is one illness;
Forcibly seizing others’ possessions is one illness.

Lord Lao said: "If one reflects on and eliminates these one hundred illnesses, no disasters or burdens will remain—these then become the *One Hundred Remedies*."

The One Hundred Remedies:
A gentle nature and yielding disposition are one remedy;
Conduct that is magnanimous and a mind that is harmonious are one remedy;
Movement and stillness governed by propriety are one remedy;
Rising and resting with moderation are one remedy;
Drawing near to virtue and distancing oneself from lust are one remedy;
Eliminating desire is one remedy;
Extending righteousness and upholding justice are one remedy;
Not taking what is not rightfully one’s own is one remedy;
A heart free from clinging attachment is one remedy;
Valuing what is useful in others is one remedy;
Wishing blessings upon others is one remedy;
Rescuing others from misfortune and aiding the distressed is one remedy;
Instructing the ignorant and benighted is one remedy;
Admonishing and correcting the perverse and disorderly is one remedy;
Disciplining and guiding the young and unlearned is one remedy;
Guiding those who are lost and misled is one remedy;
Supporting the elderly and weak is one remedy;
Assisting others with one’s strength is one remedy;
Sharing rightful portions with the poor is one remedy;
Compassion for the impoverished and distressed is one remedy;
Honoring the worthy regardless of status is one remedy;
Speech that is modest and humble is one remedy;
Reverence and humility are one remedy;
Not defaulting on debts is one remedy;
Comforting and consoling the faithful is one remedy;
Uprightness and solemn dignity are one remedy;
Extending rectitude and correcting crookedness are one remedy;
Not contending over right and wrong is one remedy;
Facing insults without contempt is one remedy;
Enduring humiliation without resentment is one remedy;
Extolling goodness and correcting evil is one remedy;
Choosing the good and rejecting the bad is one remedy;
Taking the greater share for oneself and leaving the lesser to others is one remedy;
Praising the worthy and good is one remedy;
Reflecting on oneself upon seeing the worthy is one remedy;
Not parading one’s own virtues is one remedy;
Attributing merit to others and taking hardship for oneself is one remedy;
Not boasting of one’s own goodness is one remedy;
Not erasing others’ merits is one remedy;
Not resenting toil and hardship is one remedy;
Embracing truth in thought and deed is one remedy;
Concealing others’ hidden faults is one remedy;
Feigning poverty to aid the needy is one remedy;
Honoring those who surpass oneself is one remedy;
Bearing poverty without complaint is one remedy;
Not exalting oneself is one remedy;
Taking pleasure in others’ accomplishments is one remedy;
Not delighting in others’ hidden faults is one remedy;
Observing gains and losses impartially is one remedy;
Cultivating hidden virtue and planting kindness is one remedy;
Never cursing or reviling others is one remedy;
Not judging others’ right and wrong is one remedy;
Kind and virtuous speech is one remedy;
Attributing misfortune and illness to oneself is one remedy;
Never haggling or quarreling is one remedy;
Bestowing without expectation of repayment is one remedy;
Not cursing animals is one remedy;
Offering blessings to others is one remedy;
A mind that is balanced and thoughts that are equanimous are one remedy;
A mind that is tranquil and thoughts that are settled are one remedy;
Not dwelling on past grievances is one remedy;
Correcting the perverse and assisting the crooked is one remedy;
Heeding admonition and accepting transformation is one remedy;
Not meddling in others’ affairs is one remedy;
Restraining anger and indignation is one remedy;
Dispelling anxious thoughts is one remedy;
Honoring and serving the elderly is one remedy;
Maintaining reverence and solemnity in the inner chambers is one remedy;
Cultivating filial piety and fraternal duty within is one remedy;
Concealing evil and extolling goodness is one remedy;
Maintaining integrity and adhering to one’s station is one remedy;
Taking pleasure in others’ fine food and drink is one remedy;
Assisting others in repaying loyalty is one remedy;
Averting eclipses of the sun and moon is one remedy;
Avoiding suspicion and keeping distance from doubt is one remedy;
Serene, expansive, and unhurried demeanor is one remedy;
Revering sacred texts is one remedy;
Contemplating the divine and meditating on the Dao is one remedy;
Propagating sagely teachings is one remedy;
Establishing merit without weariness is one remedy;
Honoring Heaven and revering Earth is one remedy;
Paying homage to the Three Luminaries is one remedy;
Serene and pure tranquility is one remedy;
Benevolence, caution, humility, and yielding are one remedy;
Loving life and detesting killing is one remedy;
Not amassing excessive wealth is one remedy;
Not violating prohibitions and taboos is one remedy;
Uprightness, integrity, fidelity, and trustworthiness are one remedy;
Not burning mountains or felling trees is one remedy;
Assisting others with an empty cart is one remedy;
Offering forthright admonition with loyalty and trust is one remedy;
Rejoicing in others’ virtue is one remedy;
Rescuing and aiding the poor and destitute is one remedy;
Carrying burdens for the elderly is one remedy;
Eliminating attachment and forsaking desire is one remedy;
A compassionate heart filled with pity is one remedy;
Praising others’ goodness is one remedy;
Bestowing alms when wealthy is one remedy;
Extending kindness when noble is one remedy."

These hundred remedies are exhorted for all to follow.
Thus, though the sage dwells in darkness, he dares not act wrongly;
though he abides in honor and emolument, he dares not seek profit.
He measures his form to clothe himself, gauges his belly to feed himself.

Observing the Three Hundred Great Precepts, it is said:
The Primordial Heavenly King bestowed them upon the Most High Dao Lord,
the Dao Lord transmitted them to the Emperor of the Grand Tenuity.
When the Emperor received the precepts, he chanted three verses:

*"Wisdom arises from original nonbeing,
luminous and bright, transcending the ten directions.
It binds emptiness and erects the mysterious heavens,
while all heavens draw from its flowing fragrance.
Its subtlety defies thought and discussion,
as emptiness responds and truth truly communicates.
Being is ultimately nonbeing,
while nonbeing contains all without exclusion.
Wisdom constantly observes the body—
this is the foremost task in learning the Dao.
Vast and boundless, it roams the mysterious expanse,
naturally recording my spirit.
The Heavenly Worthy ever protects and shelters,
while demon kings pledge their guardianship.
Resplendent is the golden radiant body,
transcending the Most High Immortals.
Wisdom engenders the root of precepts,
the true Dao takes precepts as its master.
From this the Three Treasures arise,
revered and received by lofty sages.
Riding this deathless boat,
one swiftly crosses the great expanse.
At this moment of preaching the precepts,
all heavenly perfected bow their heads."*

**Essential Precepts of the Wondrous Scroll on Compassion and Discipline, Fascicle Five Concludes**
**Essential Extracts on Ritual and Precepts, Fascicle Six**

The Three Hundred Great Precepts are divided according to the Three Primes:
One hundred eighty for the Lower Prime,
thirty-six for the Middle Prime,
eighty-four for the Upper Prime.

One must not kill living beings or moving creatures;
one must not consume alcohol;
one must not commit adultery with the wives of common folk;
one must not steal people’s property;
one must not envy the worthy or resent the capable;
one must not betray the kindness of one’s teacher;
one must not be disloyal to one’s superiors;
one must not deceive one’s subordinates;
one must not deceive or wrong fellow students who have not yet understood;
one must not treat disciples with contempt;
one must not speak kindly while harboring secret malice;
one must not speak of others’ faults;
one must not hoard the seven treasures or fail to bestow alms upon the four assemblies;
one must not delight in others’ wealth or use their goods as one’s own burden;
one must not keep blades, staves, or weapons;
one must not raise the six livestock;
one must not use vessels of gold or silver for eating;
one must not bury the dead with lavish funerals;
one must not covet honor and emolument;
one must not burn or ruin things buried in the earth;
one must not cast edible worldly things into fire or water;
one must not crave worldly flavors;
one must not eat the five pungent plants;
one must not write in cursive script;
one must not exchange coarse goods for others’ fine goods;
one must not knowingly involve oneself in military or state affairs;
one must not devise cunning schemes;
one must not visit kings or nobles without cause;
one must not discuss celestial timing or point out and analyze constellations;
one must not set fire to fields, wilds, or forests;
one must not pluck flowers from plants without cause;
one must not associate with evil people;
one must not fell trees or forests without cause;
one must not chatter excessively among people or speak in vulgar terms;
one must not eat alone among others;
one must not engage in worldly marriage affairs;
one must not practice worldly martial arts;
one must not reveal others’ hidden faults or private shame;
one must not presumptuously read others’ letters or documents;
one must not speak or walk alone with women;
one must not walk with women unless accompanied by a senior;
one must not sit with women or cohabit with them;
one must not eat with women or exchange clothing with them;
one must not personally instruct women;
one must not speak of the faults of others’ ancestors;
one must not flatter worldly people to their faces;
one must not cast poison into deep pools, rivers, or seas;
one must not favor one’s own clan;
one must not distance oneself from those of different surnames;
one must not cause miscarriage or harm fetuses;
one must not seek revenge out of hatred;
one must not show partiality toward disciples;
one must not gather crowds of people;
one must not send secret letters to slander others;
one must not exalt oneself;
one must not be arrogant;
one must not be self-righteous or obstinate;
one must not create superfluous taboos in the world;
one must not covet others’ possessions;
one must not drain ponds or reservoirs;
one must not criticize the talents or shortcomings of teachers or friends;
one must not treat scriptures with contempt or slander the words of the Dao;
one must not despise the elderly or sick;
one must not abandon or mistreat beggars;
one must not rely on power and authority to oppress the world;
one must not form cliques with one’s favorites;
one must not live separately from one’s parents under a different gate;
one must not harbor anger toward disciples;
one must not scold or reproach worldly people;
one must not curse others as slaves, servants, or beasts;
one must not strike servants’ faces or injure their limbs;
one must not delight in others’ misfortunes;
one must not collect harsh taxes or burden the world;
one must not survey land for others’ graves or dwellings;
one must not divine worldly fortunes or misfortunes;
one must not turn one’s back on proper conduct;
one must not mingle in crowds with worldly people;
one must not visit nobles without cause;
one must not seize what others desire;
one must not gallop through the world seeking fame;
one must not attend worldly celebrations or funerals to please others;
one must not claim others’ achievements as one’s own virtue;
one must not sleep on beds adorned with gold or carvings;
one must not dictate others’ preferences in food and drink;
one must not alarm the common folk with false talk of decline or misfortune;
one must not startle birds or beasts by driving them into desperate straits;
one must not frighten the elderly or young;
one must not treat officials or authorities with contempt;
one must not involve oneself in worldly disputes or debates over right and wrong;
one must not regret or withdraw offered kindness;
one must not wander or roam without restraint;
one must not recklessly climb high towers;
one must not cage flying birds or running beasts;
one must not block wells or ditches;
one must not rejoice in others’ misfortunes or calamities;
one must not place thorns across others’ paths;
one must not sacrifice to gods or spirits;
one must not bow to ghosts or spirits;
one must not expose oneself to the Three Luminaries or recklessly curse wind and rain;
one must not borrow or take others’ things without returning them to their owners;
one must not sever or seize others’ wealth;
one must not watch others commit wrongdoing;
one must not prevent others from doing good;
one must not fail to fast and recite the Dao on the fast days of the heavens;
one must not violate the fasts during the six fasting months;
one must not transgress the scriptural teachings, precepts, or prohibitions;
one must not act as an advocate in lawsuits;
one must not trust others to bring trouble upon the world;
one must not spread rumors of others’ faults;
one must not mock the ignorant, poor, or lowly;
one must not willfully add or remove a single word from the scriptures or precepts—heavenly officials will deduct from one’s allotted years;
one must not fabricate false speech;
one must not encourage others to plot against rulers, superiors, or teachers;
one must not be arrogant toward the Three Treasures or treat the Heavenly Worthy with contempt;
one must not encourage others to be unfilial to parents or siblings;
one must not falsely claim or adopt a special title as a perfected one;
one must not trust or employ heterodox teachings, demonic guards, or false spirits;
one must not accumulate excessive clothing;
one must not slander those who study the Dao;
one must not pretend to study without scriptures, deceiving people and spirits.
In all matters of Daoist study, one must neither act thus oneself nor teach others to do so.

Here follows the translation:

---

The precepts on observing the body, from the fifth to the one hundred and eightieth, constitute the Way of the noble person. They are titled *The Jade Purity Wisdom Precepts of the Lower Prime* (*Yu Qing Zhi Hui Xia Yuan Pin Jie*). The preceding precepts all bear the heading "Daoist study" (*daoxue*), which is here abbreviated. Below are set forth the thirty-six precepts of the Middle Prime (*Zhong Yuan*):

In Daoist study, one must not expect others to show deference;
one must not secretly copy another’s scriptures or precepts;
one must not adorn or embellish one’s robes and garments;
one must not keep one’s person unclean;
when ascending a high forest to recite scriptures, or walking together with others, one must yield the way and let them go first.

When studying with others, in summer one must tend the stove and provide for their needs;
when studying with others, in winter one must hold the inkstone and supply water;
when eating with others, one must share the rice and vegetables;
when eating with others, one must keep one’s place before oneself proper;
when studying with others, one must respect those who surpass oneself;
when dwelling with others, one must accept their arrangements;
when studying with others, one must bear in mind teachings not yet understood.

If others inflict harm upon oneself, and one receives that harm, one must harbor no resentment;
one must not nurse a vengeful intent to repay others.
When speaking with a woman, one must not gaze directly at her face or laugh while facing her.
When crossing water with a woman, one must not look at her directly.

If one loses something, one must not suspect one’s fellow students or others;
when losing something, one must submit to fate and repent, for many sins bring many calamities and illnesses.
One must humble oneself, reflect inwardly, and reform past faults to cultivate future virtue.

One must endure what others cannot endure;
one must sever what others cannot sever;
one must wear what others cannot wear;
one must eat what others cannot eat;
one must study what others cannot study;
one must tolerate what others cannot tolerate;
one must accept what others cannot accept;
one must cut off what others cannot cut off.

One must not allow the spirit to drift or scatter, nor the true thought to be obstructed;
one must keep the body clean, lest the hun and po souls depart.
If one has desires, the celestial perfected will be cut off, and demonic officials will be unable to descend.
If one has a household, the Three Poisons will not be extinguished, and the Three Perfected will not reside.
If one has a body, all demons will not depart, and concentrated thought will yield no response.

One must keep the heart still, silent, and empty, uniting with the true tree;
one must settle the mysterious spring, preventing reckless movement.
First extinguish the storehouse of consciousness and perception, then the true person will appear.

The precepts on observing the body, from the fifth to the two hundred and sixteenth, constitute the unsurpassed, correct, and true Dao. They are titled *The Jade Purity Wisdom Precepts of the Middle Prime* (*Yu Qing Zhi Hui Zhong Yuan Jie Pin*). Below are set forth the precepts of the Upper Prime (*Shang Yuan*), comprising eighty-four precepts:

In Daoist study, one must regard a vegetable diet as the norm;
one must bear in mind to deliver others before delivering oneself;
one must bear in mind to dwell in mountains and forests, in seclusion and concentrated thought;
one must bear in mind to burn fragrant incense, perfuming the heavens and penetrating demonic realms;
one must bear in mind to be among the worthy assembly, listening to wondrous sounds;
one must bear in mind to request and receive the scriptures of the Three Treasures, diligently making offerings;
one must bear in mind to establish merit by delivering others, never wearying through the kalpas;
one must bear in mind to uphold the fundamental virtue of one’s teachers and friends, never faltering through the kalpas;
one must bear in mind the purity within the kingdom, the king’s transformation bringing great peace, with no unrighteousness;
one must bear in mind neighboring kingdoms being well-governed, each guarding its borders;
one must bear in mind to pray for the common people, that they may always be safe and whole;
one must bear in mind to place all beings first, not seeking the Dao for oneself alone;
one must bear in mind to keep distant from ghosts and spirits, neither revering nor slighting them;
one must bear in mind to keep distant from heterodox arts and taboos;
one must bear in mind to keep distant from music, sensuality, singing, and dancing;
one must bear in mind to harbor no doubts about sacred texts, nor alter or subtract from the codes and laws;
one must bear in mind to be without seeking or desire;
one must bear in mind to honor the root and guard the true;
one must bear in mind that the mouth must not contradict the heart, nor the heart betray the body;
one must bear in mind to maintain purity and guard the true;
one must bear in mind to hold no divergent thoughts, contemplating only emptiness and stillness;
one must bear in mind stillness and tranquility, free from all suffering and pain;
one must bear in mind those in the world who are anxious and imperiled, bound by sin and afflicted with suffering;
one must bear in mind the sage and enlightened emperor who broadly propagates the Dao, and the flourishing of the imperial house;
one must bear in mind the mutual assistance of ruler and minister, always preserving the Dao;
one must bear in mind the timely arrival of the heavens and earth, the sun and moon, wind and rain, frost and snow;
one must bear in mind the causes and conditions by which one’s parents raised one;
one must bear in mind one’s seven generations of parents ascending to the heavenly halls;
one must bear in mind one’s teacher, that they may soon attain deliverance;
one must bear in mind one’s fellow students, that they may fathom the profound and abstruse classics;
one must bear in mind those of like aspiration, teaching and guiding one another into the correct Dao;
one must bear in mind not to violate the texts spoken by one’s own mouth;
one must bear in mind to regard others’ parents as one’s own parents;
one must bear in mind to regard others’ children as surpassing one’s own;
one must bear in mind to regard others’ bodies as surpassing one’s own;
one must bear in mind to regard others’ bodily injuries as more painful than one’s own;
one must bear in mind to regard others’ humiliations and evils as surpassing one’s own body;
one must bear in mind the severing of one’s karmic roots from past lives;
one must bear in mind that the tree of one’s life has withered, the spirit merging with the great void, through countless kalpas, the body uniting with the true Dao;
one must bear in mind that the roots of birth have been cut off, unable to generate worldly causes, conditions, or karmic ties;
one must bear in mind that the paths of the three destinies are blocked, and the hells forever stilled;
one must bear in mind that the midday meal nourishes the spirit, abandoning all rich and greasy foods;
one must bear in mind to be cautious with the great Dharma, always preserving the true primordial elixir of the Three Palaces;
one must bear in mind to observe the world with harmonious light, without arrogance toward the common;
one must bear in mind the scriptures and precepts of the Three Treasures, reciting them ceaselessly;
one must bear in mind to preserve the feminine unity, reciting the *Great Cavern Scripture*, as if facing the gods;
one must bear in mind ascending as an immortal to deliver the world, riding clouds and driving dragons;
one must bear in mind desiring to see those who share one’s teacher;
one must bear in mind seeing perfected persons and Daoist practitioners performing ritual and cultivation;
one must bear in mind seeing the sagely ruler governing the world, with those beyond the seas bowing in submission and riding the wind toward transformation;
one must bear in mind eating the natural delicacies of the celestial kitchens, free from hunger and thirst;
one must bear in mind conversing with celestial perfected beings, in serene non-action;
one must bear in mind summoning immortal youths and jade maidens;
one must bear in mind roaming eastward to the Azure Forest of the Eastern Florescence;
one must bear in mind roaming westward to the Peaceful Nurturance of the Western Florescence;
one must bear in mind roaming northward to the Azure Net of the Northern Florescence;
one must bear in mind roaming southward to the Great Cinnabar of the Southern Florescence;
one must bear in mind roaming and resting in the Jade Capital of the Central Florescence on Mount Kunlun;
one must bear in mind roaming the upper fasting halls, expounding and elucidating the sagely Dao, unfolding its profundities;
one must bear in mind roaming the Seven Treasures Palace of Jade Purity, paying homage to the Three Primes Heavenly Worthies;
one must bear in mind roaming the Cinnabar Rosy Clouds Palace of Jade Purity, paying homage to the Twenty-Four Lofty Sages of the Most High;
one must bear in mind roaming the Purple Palace, paying homage to the Thirty-Nine Lofty Sages of the Cavern Perfected;
one must bear in mind roaming the Seven Jeweled Flowing Rosy Clouds High Shade Jade Grove of the Most High Jade Capital, paying homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Most High, the Great Sages of the Ten Directions, and those who cycle through the kalpas anew;
one must bear in mind roaming the Golden Palaces of the Thirty-Six Heavens, paying homage to the Heavenly Emperors;
one must bear in mind roaming the Golden Radiance Palace of the Nine Heavens, paying homage to the Heavenly Emperors;
one must bear in mind roaming the Seven Treasures Palaces of the Six Heavens, observing the transformations of the Great Demon Kings, seeing one’s name recorded to enter the ranks of immortals and forever depart the registers of the Yellow Springs;
one must bear in mind roaming the palaces and dwellings of the various heavens, discussing scriptures and debating the Dao with the Heavenly Emperors;
one must bear in mind roaming the palaces of the sun and moon, their brilliance resplendent, paying homage to the Kings of the Sun and Moon, and drinking the golden nectar of their radiant essence;
one must bear in mind roaming the Flowing Light Palace of the Great Brahma Heaven, paying homage to the lower immortals and the assembly of Heavenly Emperors and sagely beings, listening to the wondrous and exquisite sounds of the heavens;
one must bear in mind roaming the Seven Treasures Forests of the various heavens, where the fragrance of reborn numinous incense wafts against the wind, perceptible two thousand *li* away, with lions and flying dragons roaring and howling within;
one must bear in mind roaming the various heavens, bathing and sitting upon lotus flowers, the natural and pure fragrance flowing abundantly, all celestial pools as one realm of human bliss;
one must bear in mind roaming the various heavens, listening to the celestial arts and music, free from worldly thoughts;
one must bear in mind roaming the outer heavens of the ten directions, making offerings to the assembly of Great Sages and the Unsurpassed True Persons;
one must bear in mind roaming the famous mountains and hidden palaces and grotto chambers of heaven and earth, paying homage to the assembly of sages who first attained the Dao;
one must bear in mind to keep secret the names and taboos of the celestial perfected, not violating them with one’s mouth;
one must bear in mind to regard the Daoist scriptures as the Way, harboring no divergent thoughts, always keeping the heart empty and the mind vast, contemplating the mysterious and void, abiding in serene emptiness.

---

The Precepts from the Fifth to the Three Hundredth are of the Supreme, Boundless Dao, known as the *Highest Jade Purity Wisdom Upper Prime Precepts*. The Subtle Heavenly Emperor states: If one upholds the precepts, when a disciple lodges alone in the mountains and forests or in fearful places, they should sound the celestial drum thirty-four times. With the heart fixed on the precepts, divine guardians will encircle them in threefold protection; malevolent spirits dare not approach, and blessings and virtue will ever follow. All the celestial benevolent spirits will respond and safeguard them, while former adversaries and creditors will all generate compassionate hearts.

*Essential Practices of Solemn Precepts and Wondrous Scrolls, Volume Six Concludes*
*Essential Compilation of Ritual Precepts, Volume Seven*
Compiled by Daoist Zhu Faman of the Three Caverns

**On Karmic Retribution**
To purify the heart and walk the straight path is beyond the reach of royal law; to act with whole sincerity in the true leaves no fear of hell’s comings and goings. Yet if the six senses cling to attachments, the five destinies of rebirth will follow; the weight of transgressions arises from one’s own conduct, and retribution is meted out accordingly. Not a hair’s breadth is lost, for the netherworld records every fault.

The *Scripture of the Three Primes’ Precepts* states: The Heavenly Bureau has thirty-six offices, the Earthly and Water Bureaus each have forty-two offices, totaling one hundred twenty offices across the Three Bureaus. Each office holds one *kao* (trial), the officials oversee one hundred twenty *kao*, the clerks one thousand two hundred *kao*, the soldiers twelve thousand *kao*, and the officers follow the sins committed in a person’s lifetime, hastening their trials.

**Categories of the Three Primes’ Transgression Precepts**
**Heavenly Bureau:** One Central Palace, twelve offices.
**Earthly Bureau:** One Central Palace, fourteen offices.
**Water Bureau:** One Central Palace, fourteen offices.

**Rituals of Merit and Demerit for Upper Perfected Ones:**
- The ranks, titles, and relative dignity of Upper Perfected Ones, and the rites for their merits and transgressions;
- The rites for the processions and circumambulations of the assembly of Upper Perfected Ones and Sages, and their merits and transgressions;
- The rites for the excursions and retinues of the Great Sages among the Upper Perfected, and their merits and transgressions.

**Comprehensive Records of Merit and Demerit for Upper Perfected Ones:**
- The ledgers of life and death, and the tally of merits and transgressions;
- The registers of life and death, and the reckoning of the weight of merits and demerits;
- The ledgers of the merits and demerits of ghosts and spirits, and the turning of the Wheel of Rebirth;
- The ledgers of the dark interrogations and deliverance of ghosts and spirits, and their merits and transgressions;
- The ledgers of the ascent and deliverance of deceased souls, and the weight of their merits and transgressions in rebirth;
- The ledgers of the refinement and pacification of deceased souls, and their merits and transgressions;
- The ledgers of the years and months of attainment and the ranks of immortals who have achieved the Dao, and their merits and transgressions;
- The ledgers of the songs and chants of the myriad demons, and their merits and transgressions.

**Transgressions of Those Who Study the Supreme Dao:**
- Doubting the scriptures and precepts, harboring dual intentions;
- Disdaining sacred texts, criticizing the scriptures;
- Disrespecting the master, violating the master’s covenant;
- Slandering the master, failing to revere the great principle;
- Stealing scriptures without a proper lineage;
- Teaching without a master’s guidance;
- Enticing others to transmit scriptures to disciples;
- Obtaining scriptures without receiving the master’s covenant and precepts;
- Transmitting scriptures without adhering to the prescribed years and months;
- Transmitting scriptures to unworthy recipients;
- Receiving teachings from a master without performing deliverance rites;
- Transmitting teachings to disciples without merit;
- Transmitting teachings without prior memorial to the deities;
- Transmitting scriptures without prior memorial to the Five Emperors;
- Transmitting scriptures without sincerity, belittling the Dao and its laws;
- Obstructing the path of the worthy, seeking personal merit and fame;
- Failing to pay homage to the master during the eight seasonal festivals;
- Neglecting to perform purification fasts;
- Performing purification fasts without devotion;
- Reciting scriptures with omissions or abridgments;
- Circumambulating out of order, engaging in disputes;
- Harboring anger toward masters, parents, or elders.

**Transgressions of Scholars and Common Folk:**
- Assailing good people;
- Engaging in malicious speech and slander;
- Criticizing masters or common folk;
- Drinking to the point of losing one’s nature;
- Killing living beings in secret;
- Indulging in greed, arrogance, and dissipation;
- Defiling the Dao and its laws;
- Cursing gods and spirits;
- Killing and harming sentient beings;
- Engaging in deceitful speech, double-tonguedness, and faithlessness;
- Committing lewd and defiling acts;
- Stealing others’ property;
- Envying the worthy and resenting the capable;
- Betraying the kindness of masters;
- Engaging in deceitful speech and slander;
- Revealing celestial patterns;
- Slandering the scriptures and laws;
- Repenting midway through scriptural practice;
- Being disloyal to superiors;
- Neglecting duties to subordinates;
- Deceiving fellow students;
- Deceiving common folk;
- Speaking kindly while harboring evil in the heart;
- Speaking of others’ faults and evils;
- Disrespecting the Three Luminaries (sun, moon, stars);
- Defiling and disrespecting gods and spirits.

The above sixty transgressions are overseen by the Heavenly Bureau’s Central Palace and its twelve offices, the Earthly Bureau’s Central Palace and its fourteen offices, and the Water Bureau’s Central Palace and its fourteen offices, with the Wind Blade Trial Officials presiding.

**Heavenly Bureau:** Left Palace, Left Office, twelve offices.
**Earthly Bureau:** Left Palace, Left Office, fourteen offices.
**Water Bureau:** Left Palace, Left Office, fourteen offices.

**Transgressions of Scholars and Common Folk:**
- Envying and resenting fellow students;

- Indulging in lewd speech and reckless lies;
- Coveting profit without satisfaction;
- Hoarding fine emoluments and treasures without bestowing or dispersing them;
- Delighting in others’ valuables and taking them for oneself;
- Wishing harm, ruin, and dispersal upon others;
- Privately keeping knives, staves, and weapons;
- Slaughtering and butchering the six livestock and killing living beings;
- Shooting and stabbing wild beasts and flying birds;
- Burning mountains for hunting;
- Catching fish with nets and traps;
- Using vessels of gold and silver for dining;
- Coveting and delighting in empty glory and emoluments;
- Burning and ruining things one sees;
- Casting food and drink into water;
- Craving rich, greasy, and meaty flavors;
- Indulging in the five pungent foods;
- Writing deceptive and false intentions in cursive script;
- Gathering and assembling crowds of people;
- Scheming to take others’ wives and daughters;
- Plotting against state affairs in one’s heart;
- Scheming to take others’ household possessions;
- Exchanging coarse items for others’ fine goods;
- Consorting with the Son of Heaven and feudal lords;
- Presuming to know celestial timing and the movements of stars;
- Setting fire to fields, wilderness, and mountain forests;
- Chopping down trees and plucking fruits and flowers;
- Associating and becoming intimate with evil people;
- Consorting with and emulating the ostentatious customs of the world;
- Eating alone among others;
- Engaging in worldly marriage affairs;
- Indulging in worldly music and entertainment;
- Praising people to their faces while slandering them in secret;
- Speaking of the virtues and vices of others’ superiors;
- Revealing others’ hidden evils and private shameful acts;
- Attacking good people and causing misfortune without reason;
- Presumptuously reading others’ writings and prying into their affairs;
- Speaking privately with women;
- Men and women sitting together in groups;
- Men and women sharing food and exchanging clothing;
- Men and women teaching improper conduct;
- Exalting oneself with arrogance and indulgence;
- Seeking revenge out of hatred;
- Separating from one’s family and household;
- Abandoning children and harming fetuses;
- Favoring one’s own clan while estranging those of other surnames;
- Poisoning water to harm living beings;
- Showing partiality toward certain disciples;
- Gathering and amassing crowds of people;
- Sending writings to flatter worldly people;
- Presuming to act according to one’s own nature;
- Creating groundless taboos;
- Coveting others’ possessions and affairs;
- Criticizing the strengths and weaknesses of teachers and friends;
- Disrespecting scriptural teachings and the words of the Dao;
- Disdaining and belittling the elderly and the sick;
- Abandoning and scorning beggars;
- Relying on power to oppress the world;
- Forming cliques with one’s favorites;
- Separating parents and siblings to live apart.

The above sixty transgressions are overseen by the Heavenly Bureau’s Left Palace and Left Office with twelve offices, the Earthly Bureau’s Left Palace and Left Office with fourteen offices, and the Water Bureau’s Left Palace and Left Office with fourteen offices, with the Solar Water Bureau’s Trial Officials presiding.

**Heavenly Bureau:** Right Palace, Right Office, twelve offices.
**Earthly Bureau:** Right Palace, Right Office, fourteen offices.
**Water Bureau:** Right Palace, Right Office, fourteen offices.

- Harboring anger and resentment toward disciples;
- Harboring anger and reproaching worldly people;
- Failing to release living beings and deliver the dying;
- Forgetting one’s teacher in wealth and honor;
- Eating the fruits of celestial fasts while forgetting the Dao;
- Believing others’ words and resenting one’s teacher or master;
- Publicly discussing others’ evil deeds;
- Mocking others for their foolishness, ignorance, poverty, and lowliness;
- Encouraging others to do evil;
- Preventing others from doing good;
- Taking pleasure in others’ faults;
- Turning one’s back on proper conduct;
- Failing to honor the Five Peaks and Three Rivers with their proper names;
- Defiling the Five Peaks and Three Rivers;
- Seizing what others desire;
- Galloping through worldly customs and competing for worldly gain;
- Seeking to please the crowd through worldly celebrations and condolences;
- Claiming others’ achievements as one’s own virtue;
- Naming others’ preferences in food and drink.

- Frightening the common people in their misfortune and distress;
- Frightening birds and beasts into confined and desolate places;
- Terrifying the elderly and the young;
- Disrespecting and belittling officials and authorities;
- Debating the right and wrong of worldly affairs;
- Recklessly discussing the rise and fall of the state;
- Bestowing favors only to regret them later;
- Caging flying birds and running beasts;
- Taking pleasure in others’ misfortune and calamity;
- Placing thorny brambles across others’ paths;
- Worshiping and paying homage to ghosts and spirits;
- Exposing one’s body before the Three Luminaries;
- Cursing and reviling wind, clouds, thunder, and rain;
- Failing to return borrowed items in a timely manner;
- Deceiving others to seek glory and praise;
- Displaying arrogance and contempt toward the Three Treasures while slighting the Heavenly Worthies;
- Plotting against one’s sovereign, elders, teachers, or masters;
- Encouraging others to be unfilial toward parents and siblings;
- Falsely claiming extraordinary titles and passing oneself off as a Perfected One;
- Trusting and following heterodox teachings and defending perverse views;
- Learning without a scriptural master’s instruction and deceiving both humans and spirits;
- Hoarding excess clothing without distributing it to the poor;
- Secretly copying others’ scriptures and precepts with negligence and carelessness;
- Adorning one’s coarse garments with extravagant embellishments;
- Ascending the high seat while unclean in body;
- Treating the master’s teachings with defilement and disrespect;
- Failing to hold fasts and make offerings when one’s teacher is in sorrow or distress;
- Abandoning one’s teacher to pursue worldly prosperity;
- Following the powerful and wealthy in hopes of gain;
- Failing to attend to one’s teacher in illness or hardship;
- Seeking comfort and pleasure while shunning those in peril;
- Entering and exiting the Daoist gate without opening or closing it properly;
- Speaking idly with others within the Daoist gate;
- Holding fasts and making offerings without transferring merit to the Three Officials;
- Grieving only for one’s own family while ignoring others’ hardship and distress;
- Blaming the Dao and faulting one’s teacher when one’s family suffers misfortune or illness;
- Claiming as one’s own attainment the scriptures and teachings received from one’s teacher;
- Transmitting the master’s Dao and methods without offering due reverence and gratitude;
- Failing to consult one’s teacher and report to the Five Emperors during the eight seasonal nodes;
- Wandering without restraint and indulging in excess;
- Ascending heights and gazing downward.

These sixty transgressions are overseen by the Twelve Offices of the Heavenly Bureau’s Right Palace and Right Mansion, the Fourteen Offices of the Earthly Bureau’s Right Palace and Right Mansion, and the Fourteen Offices of the Water Bureau’s Right Palace and Right Mansion, under the jurisdiction of the Examiners of the Great Yin Water Bureau.

The *Zhen Zang Jing* states:
- Those who steal others’ property enter the Metal Hammer Hell upon death;
- Those who wrongfully take even a single coin from another enter the Cauldron of Boiling Water Hell upon death;
- Those who engage in deceitful and frivolous speech enter the Tongue-Plucking Hell upon death;
- Those who kill out of hatred enter the Five Prisons of the Great Earth Hell upon death;
- Those consumed by greed, anger, and delusion enter the Great Cage Hell upon death;
- Those who disrespect the elderly and deceive others enter the Fengdu Hell upon death;
- Those who curse with venomous intent enter the Eight Gates Hell upon death;
- Those who shout and curse loudly enter the Confounding Plow Hell upon death;
- Those who slander and defame others enter the Northern Cold Hell upon death;
- Those who engage in double-tongued flattery enter the Fire Mountain Hell upon death;
- Those who spread rumors about others enter the Solid Earth Hell upon death;
- Those who delight in speaking ill of others enter the Dark Hell upon death;
- Those who destroy goodness and praise themselves enter the Great Sword Hell upon death;
- Those who are arrogant and self-conceited enter the Scorching Fire Hell upon death;
- Those who hoard poison to harm others enter the Lime Hell upon death;
- Those who secretly slander others in writing enter the Yellow Springs Great Gate Hell upon death;
- Those who treat scriptures and teachings with contempt enter the Obstructed Light Hell upon death;
- Those who slander sacred texts enter the Copper Fire Hell upon death;
- Those who rely on power to bully others enter the Blazing Furnace Hell upon death;
- Those who kill living beings and engage in licentious sacrifices enter the Boiling Mountain Hell upon death;
- Those who burn wild forests and hunt for sport enter the Divided Form Hell upon death;
- Those who criticize their teachers and elders enter the Grinding Mountain Hell upon death;
- Those who hoard wealth and possessions enter the Hungry Ghost Hell upon death;
- Those who expose others’ private affairs enter the Black Water Hell upon death.

*Essential Precepts and Rituals for Cultivation*, Scroll Seven—concluded.
*Essential Precepts and Rituals for Cultivation*, Scroll Eight.

Compiled by Daoist Zhu Faman of the Three Caverns, *The Compendium of Retreat Names*

To enter stillness and ascend to the True, one must rely on retreat and precepts, employing external methods to harmonize the inner rituals of the heart-mind. As the *Scripture of Salvation* states: When the cycles of Heaven and Earth reach their end, one must observe retreat, burn incense, and recite scriptures. When the constellations fall into disorder and the sun and moon lose their proper course, one must observe retreat, burn incense, and recite scriptures. When the four seasons lose their balance and yin and yang fall out of harmony, one must observe retreat, burn incense, and recite scriptures. When the sovereign faces calamity and warfare erupts on all sides, one must observe retreat, burn incense, and recite scriptures. When pestilence and poison spread, causing the multitudes to perish, one must observe retreat, burn incense, and recite scriptures. When teachers and companions pass from this life, one must observe retreat, burn incense, and recite scriptures.

The merit of retreat, precepts, and scripture recitation is profound. Above, it dispels celestial disasters and safeguards the emperor; below, it wards off poison and harm, delivering the multitudes. In life and death, all depend upon it—its blessings are beyond measure.

The *Scripture of the Sacred Record* states: There are six types of retreats. The first is the Shangqing Retreat, which has two methods: first, seclusion from the crowd to dine alone, calming the qi and transcending form; second, purifying the altar and solemnizing the assembly, following the rites of the Supreme Perfected. First, one delivers the Nine Ancestors, then one’s family, and finally oneself.

The second is the Lingbao Retreat, which has six methods:
1. The Golden Register Retreat, to deliver and protect the sovereign;
2. The Yellow Register Retreat, to deliver and uplift ancestral generations;
3. The Illuminating the True Retreat, to repent for the Nine Dark Realms;
4. The Three Primes Retreat, to confess transgressions of the precepts;
5. The Eight Nodes Retreat, to repent for past and recent faults;
6. The Natural Retreat, to pray for blessings on behalf of the people.

The third is the Dongshen Retreat, where purity and simplicity are paramount, transcending the dust to await the numinous.

The fourth is the Taiyi Retreat, where reverence and solemnity take precedence.

The fifth is the Zhijiao Retreat, where clarity and austerity are prized.

The sixth is the Tutan Retreat, where diligence and hardship are the measure of merit.

These various retreats, from ancient times to the present, have been held in great esteem. Though eras change and customs differ, some details may vary within the Lingbao Retreat, occasionally observed as a "half-day retreat." The half-day retreat is a form of "overnight invocation," where no verbal merit is accrued—only repentance is performed for one or two periods, without the threefold offering of incense. It omits the *Step-by-Step Invocation* and abbreviates the scripture veneration, or in minor retreats, three sighs suffice. Wishes may be adapted to the occasion, and rites adjusted for convenience. Since it is not a grand assembly, sincerity alone suffices.

*The Compendium of Retreat Months*
The *Three Primes Precepts* states: The first month is when the Celestial Official conducts his audit; the seventh month is when the Earthly Official conducts his audit; the tenth month is when the Water Official conducts his audit. These three months are suitable for prolonged retreats.

The *Scripture of Salvation* states: A prolonged retreat in the first month benefits the departed souls of past generations; a prolonged retreat in the seventh month benefits oneself; a prolonged retreat in the tenth month stabilizes the nation’s destiny.

The *Luminous True Rites* states: The first, third, fifth, seventh, ninth, and eleventh months—six months in a year—are retreat months.

The *Zhijiao Scripture* states: During these six retreat months, the Three Heavens command the Celestial Emperor and the Taiyi Envoys to inspect the transgressions of the world’s people. On these days, observing retreat removes the Ten Sufferings and allows one to pay homage to the Most High.

The *Eight Secret Sayings of the Supreme Clarity* states: The first, third, fourth, sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth, tenth, and eleventh months—nine months in a year—are the Nine Perfected Retreat Months.

*The Compendium of Retreat Days*
The *Great Offering Scripture of the Mysterious Capital* states: The fifteenth day of the first month is when the Celestial Official conducts his audit—the Shangyuan Retreat Day. The fifteenth day of the seventh month is when the Earthly Official conducts his audit—the Zhongyuan Retreat Day. The fifteenth day of the tenth month is when the Water Official conducts his audit—the Xiayuan Retreat Day. Observing retreat on these three days allows the Three Officials to inscribe one’s name in the Register of Good Deeds.

The *Scripture of the Royal Person’s Original Conduct* states: There are three retreat days in a month: the first, the fifteenth, and the twenty-ninth, which are suitable for pure retreat.

The *Flying Mystery Scripture of the Supreme Clarity* states: The Queen Mother of the West regularly observes retreat in the first, second, fourth, sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth, eleventh, and twelfth months—ten months in a year—on the third, fifth, ninth, fifteenth, and twenty-fifth days of each month. These five days each month are for pure retreat and focused cultivation.

The Primordial Beginning bestowed meditation upon the Supreme Perfected Mother of the Nine Numina of the Western Prime, gifting her a nine-colored phoenix robe, phoenix-cloud sandals, a divine phoenix purple wheel, and a flying feather canopy with twenty-four chariots. She decreed that on these days, if the people—men and women alike—observe pure retreat and recite scriptures, they shall attain their heart’s desires, shed the weight of three thousand grave offenses, and receive blessings from the Nine Heavens.

The *Scripture of the Sacred Record* states: The seventh day of the first month is called the *Assembly of Promotion and Reward*; the seventh day of the seventh month is called the *Assembly of Celebrating Life*; the fifth day of the tenth month is called the *Grand Assembly of Establishing Life*. On these three assembly days, the Three Officials review merits and transgressions. Observing retreat and presenting petitions on these days invokes sublime blessings.

It further states the Five La Days: The first day of the first month is *Celestial La*; the fifth day of the fifth month is *Earthly La*; the seventh day of the seventh month is *Moral La*; the first day of the tenth month is *People’s Year La*; and the festival day of the twelfth month is *Nobles’ La*. The Five La Days, together with the Three Primes, are called the *Eight Liberation Days*. On these days, one may prepare pure offerings, hold retreats to seek blessings, and also venerate ancestors—such a one is called a filial child, and their blessings are boundless. Other days are termed "licentious sacrifices" and incur transgressions.

The *Luminous True Rites* states: The first, eighth, fourteenth, fifteenth, eighteenth, twenty-third, twenty-fourth, twenty-eighth, twenty-ninth, and thirtieth days of the month are called the *Ten Upright Retreat Days*.

The *Sutra of Essential Teachings* states:
On the first day of the month, the Northern Dipper descends;
on the eighth day, the Northern Dipper’s Deity of Slaying Ghosts descends;
on the fourteenth day, the Envoy of the Great One descends;
on the fifteenth day, the Celestial Emperor descends.
When the Celestial Emperor descends, the sun, moon, stars, and all celestial officials descend with him.
On the eighteenth day, the Heavenly One descends;
on the twenty-third day, the Eight Divine Envoys of the Great One descend;
on the twenty-fourth day, the Northern Asterism descends;
on the twenty-eighth day, the Lower Great One descends;
on the twenty-ninth day, the Middle Great One descends;
on the thirtieth day, the Upper Great One descends.
When the Great One descends, the sun, moon, five planets, twenty-eight constellations, the jade armillary sphere, the Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper, the Deities of Life and Record, the Deities of Punishment and Slaying, the Great Sage and Venerable Spirits, the Perfected of Wondrous Conduct, and the Celestial Emperor and Great King all descend together.
On these days, celestial and terrestrial spirits alike tremble in reverence, traversing the world to observe human good and evil.
If on such days one maintains a steadfast heart, advances with diligence, does not transgress the scriptural teachings, honors and upholds the precepts, recites sutras and practices the Dao, and widely propagates the Dharma, the Great One rejoices, increasing their lifespan and blessings, inscribing their name on the left register, engraving it in the Jade Record, and conferring the title of Perfected.
If on such days one kills living beings, practices deceit, engages in licentiousness or theft, curses or humiliates Daoist priests, or slanders the scriptural teachings, the Great One grows furious, diminishing their lifespan and blessings, inscribing their name on the right register, reporting it to the Three Officials, and branding them a sinner.
On *jiǎzǐ* days, the Great One dispatches the Envoy of the Central Terrace to descend;
on the Eight Seasonal Nodes, the Eight Divine Envoys of the Great One descend.
On these days, one should also observe the retreat, and the Great One will rejoice.
On *gēngshēn* days, the concealed corpses within the body ascend to report one’s transgressions.
On one’s natal day, the body that has received the Dharma sees its officers and soldiers ascend to heaven to tally one’s merits and faults—one must observe the retreat on these days as well.

The *Inner Writ of the Three Sovereigns* states:
On *jiǎzǐ* days, the Celestial Sovereign’s attending officials descend at midnight;
on *jiǎxū* days, the Celestial Sovereign’s attending officials descend at dusk;
on *jiǎshēn* days, the Earthly Sovereign’s attending officials descend at the evening meal hour;
on *jiǎwǔ* days, the Earthly Sovereign’s attending officials descend at noon;
on *jiǎchén* days, the Human Sovereign’s attending officials descend at breakfast hour;
on *jiǎyín* days, the Human Sovereign’s attending officials descend at dawn.
When the celestial officials descend, the deities of the Five Peaks and Four Waterways take their positions according to direction, examining good and evil, reporting merits and recording transgressions—nothing fails to reach the ears of the portents.
One should observe the retreat on these days and stabilize the register at Southern Prosperity.

On *dīngmǎo* days, the Celestial Sovereign’s attending officials descend at sunrise;
on *dīngchǒu* days, the Celestial Sovereign’s attending officials descend at cockcrow;
on *dīngyǒu* days, the Earthly Sovereign’s attending officials descend at sunset;
on *dīnghài* days, the Earthly Sovereign’s attending officials descend at the hour of human rest;
on *dīngwèi* days, the Human Sovereign’s attending officials descend at the afternoon hour;
on *dīngsì* days, the Human Sovereign’s attending officials descend at the midday hour.
These six *dīng* days are the yin spirit days of the Three Sovereigns.
Observing the retreat on these days, the Perfected of the Five Peaks each dispatch five spirits to guard and protect, recording one’s name in the Register of Immortals.

On the timing of retreats:
The *Regulations of the Thousand Perfected* states: When determining the time for a retreat, first measure the shadow with a gnomon. On cloudy days, use a water clock to divide the hours.
The *Sutra of the Fundamental Conduct of the Sovereign* states: Retreats should follow the proper time, not arbitrary moments. The method begins by erecting a gnomon, marking its height in feet and inches, placing it in the central courtyard, and measuring the length of its shadow according to the twenty-four solar terms to determine the proper time.
After the Beginning of Spring, a shadow of six feet five inches is the proper time; five feet six inches is improper.
After Rain Water, six feet is proper; five feet two inches is improper.
After the Waking of Insects, five feet five inches is proper; four feet seven inches is improper.
After the Spring Equinox, five feet is proper; four feet two inches is improper.
After Pure Brightness, four feet five inches is proper; three feet seven inches is improper.
After Grain Rain, four feet is proper; three feet three inches is improper.
After the Beginning of Summer, three feet five inches is proper; two feet seven inches is improper.
After Grain Full, three feet is proper; two feet two inches is improper.
After Grain in Ear, two feet five inches is proper; one foot seven inches is improper.
After the Summer Solstice, two feet is proper; one foot two inches is improper.
After Lesser Heat, two feet five inches is proper; one foot seven inches is improper.
After Greater Heat, three feet is proper; two feet two inches is improper.
After the Beginning of Autumn, three feet five inches is proper; two feet seven inches is improper.
After the Limit of Heat, four feet is proper; three feet two inches is improper.
After White Dew, four feet five inches is proper; three feet seven inches is improper.
After the Autumn Equinox, five feet is proper; four feet two inches is improper.
After Cold Dew, five feet five inches is proper; four feet seven inches is improper.
After Frost Descent, six feet is proper; five feet two inches is improper.
After the Beginning of Winter, six feet five inches is proper; five feet seven inches is improper.
After Lesser Snow, seven feet is proper; six feet two inches is improper.
After Greater Snow, seven feet five inches is proper; six feet seven inches is improper.
After the Winter Solstice, eight feet is proper; seven feet two inches is improper.
After Lesser Cold, seven feet five inches is proper; six feet seven inches is improper.
After Greater Cold, seven feet is proper; six feet two inches is improper.

The *Huang Ren* states: All good men and women who maintain the fast without fail shall have their names recorded in the celestial registers of the Heavenly Officials. If they violate the precepts and lose proper measure, they shall be examined and punished by the Earthly Officials.

The *Dharma Master’s Notes on the Xuan Du Precepts* says: The fast is fundamentally rooted in purity and emptiness, its practice in tranquility and stillness, its foundation in humility, and its conduct in reverence.
