The term ‘Golden Talisman’ signifies that, with prolonged refinement, its essence becomes ever more profound and its transformations unceasing.

The eight registers are as above. When one has completed all ten scrolls, the scrolls are fulfilled in their entirety."*

From the *Báiwǔshí Jiāngjūn Lù* (One Hundred and Fifty Generals Register) downward to the *Yī Lù* (First Register) of the Celestial Master’s descendants, after ascending the Imperial Platform (*Huángtán*), they do not receive the *xìxíng* (comprehensive initiation). If they have not yet ascended the Imperial Platform, they all receive it from the *zhū gāodé* (senior virtuous masters) and transmit it.

All who study the Dao and establish merit must receive both inner and outer governance (*nèiwài zhì*), and they are all addressed as "subject" or "servant." Those who receive the Celestial Master’s appointment are addressed as "officials and functionaries." Those who perform the *Dàzhì* (Great Governance) rites are recorded without being called "born."

The *Xuándū Lǜ* (Mysterious Capital Statutes) states: "Those who receive talismanic documents and the like may have ghostly officials and soldiers in the locality; they may be seen wandering."

The *Běnxiàng Jīng* (Original Form Scripture) says:
*"Question:* Does the *sàijiǔ* (sacrificial dean) incur guilt if he accepts offerings when transmitting talismans to the common folk?
*Answer:* The *sàijiǔ* is a teacher among the people, and the masses regard him as a model. If he takes money without distributing it, later disciples will follow his example—this is the gravest offense. The calamity is far worse than a *jié* (eon of suffering), and the retribution will cycle endlessly through ten thousand ages. The Celestial Gate will never admit him, and he will forever be bound to the Three Evils."

---

**Chapter Tables (Zhāngbiǎo):**

**Question to Tianlǎo Píngcháng:**
*"Earlier, on the *Jiǎnrì* (Establishing Day), at the *wèishí* (3–5 PM) of the *jǐchǒu* (7th Heavenly Stem, *jǐ*), you submitted a memorial—why was it not reported?"*

Píngcháng replied: *"On the *jǐchǒu* day, I saw the incense case bearing the memorial at the gate, and the gate opened. If it had not opened, I would have left."*

Further questioned: *"When does the gate open during the nightly cycle?"*

Píngcháng answered:
- **Closed times:** *mǎo* (5–7 AM), *sì* (9–11 AM), *wèi* (1–3 PM), *yǒu* (5–7 PM), *hài* (9–11 PM), *chǒu* (11 PM–1 AM).
- **Open times:** *chén* (7–9 AM), *wǔ* (11 AM–1 PM), *shēn* (3–5 PM), *xū* (7–9 PM), *zǐ* (11 PM–1 AM), *yín* (1–3 AM).

**On *Zǐ* days (Water):**
- **Closed:** *Zǐ* is the day-stem god injuring the *shīmǔ* (master’s mother); these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.

**On *Chǒu* days (Earth):**
- **Closed:** *Chǒu* is the day-stem god injuring calves; these hours are forbidden: *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.
- **Open:** *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.

**On *Yín* days (Wood):**
- **Closed:** *Yín* is the day-stem god injuring livestock; these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.

**On *Mǎo* days (Wood):**
- **Closed:** *Mǎo* is the day-stem god injuring the *shīfù* (master’s father); these hours are forbidden: *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.
- **Open:** *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.

**On *Sì* days (Fire):**
- **Closed:** *Sì* is the day-stem god injuring parents; these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.

**On *Wèi* days (Fire):**
- **Closed:** *Wèi* is the day-stem god injuring women; these hours are forbidden: *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.
- **Open:** *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.

**On *Wǔ* days (Earth):**
- **Closed:** *Wǔ* is the day-stem god injuring all things; these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.

**On *Shēn* days (Metal):**
- **Closed:** *Shēn* is the day-stem god injuring the sick; these hours are forbidden: *yǒu, hài, chǒu*.
- **Open:** *chén, wǔ, shēn, mǎo, sì, wèi, xū, zǐ, yín*.

**On *Yǒu* days (Metal):**
- **Closed:** *Yǒu* is the day-stem god injuring travelers; these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, yǒu, hài, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, chǒu*.

**On *Xū* days (Wood):**
- **Closed:** *Xū* is the day-stem god injuring flying birds; these hours are forbidden: *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.
- **Open:** *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.

**On *Hài* days (Wood):**
- **Closed:** *Hài* is the day-stem god injuring travelers; these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.

**On *Chǒu* days (Earth):**
- **Closed:** *Chǒu* is the day-stem god injuring travelers; these hours are forbidden: *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.
- **Open:** *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.

**On *Jǐ* days (Earth):**
- **Closed:** *Jǐ* is the day-stem god injuring travelers; these hours are forbidden: *mǎo, sì, wèi, yǒu, hài, chǒu*.
- **Open:** *chén, wǔ, shēn, xū, zǐ, yín*.

---
**Establishing Day (*Jiǎnrì*):**
May submit memorials with **nine passages** (*jiǔtōng*). Favorable for promoting the Dao’s transformation, capturing malevolent ghosts and bandits.
**Taboos:** Do not post *zhūfú* (extermination talismans) to demolish shrines, or injure a household or master. Avoid the *shēn* hour with the *dǒuxì* (fighting stars) descending leftward.

**Purification Day (*Chúrì*):**
May submit memorials with **twelve passages**. Favorable for healing illnesses, dismantling tombs, and examining descendants.
**Taboos:** Do not post protective talismans for wealth; avoid the *yǒu* hour with *jīxīn* (personal intent).

**Completion Day (*Mǎnrì*):**
May submit memorials with **six passages**. Favorable for securing tombs and protecting wealth.
**Taboos:** Do not post *jiě* (dissolution) talismans; avoid a household becoming empty, or livestock being depleted. Avoid the *xū* hour with *jīxīn*.

**Ordinary Day (*Píngrì*):**
May submit memorials with **seventeen passages**. Favorable for resolving prohibitions and capturing all malevolence.
**Taboos:** Do not post protective talismans for wealth; livestock, masters, or servants will suffer. Avoid the *hài* hour.

**Fixed Day (*Dìngrì*):**
May submit memorials with **twenty-eight passages**. Favorable for protecting the five directions and stabilizing the residence. Dissolves the *Tǔgōng* (Earth Official’s) depletion.
**Taboos:** Do not post talismans to dispel residual *qì*; the *Tiānyī* (Heavenly Unity) will harm elders. Avoid the *zǐ* hour.

**Execution Day (*Zhírì*):**
May submit memorials with **five passages**. Favorable for capturing ghosts and bandits, and releasing captives.
**Taboos:** Do not post healing talismans; the sick will suffer. Avoid the *chǒu* hour with the *dǒuxì* descending leftward.

**Destruction Day (*Pòrì*):**
May submit memorials with **seven passages**. Favorable for demolishing ancestral halls and exterminating monstrous spirits—today’s offenses will die.
**Taboos:** Do not post talismans to dissolve tombs; this severs lineage. Avoid the *yín* hour.

**Perilous Day (*Wēirì*):**
May submit memorials with **two passages**. Favorable for guiding lost souls, reconnecting seven generations, and summoning descendants.
**Taboos:** Do not post talismans to stabilize a residence; livestock will suffer. Avoid the *mǎo* hour.

**Completion Day (*Chéngrì*):**
May submit memorials with **eighteen passages**. Favorable for recording officials and protecting minor illnesses.
**Taboos:** Do not post talismans for safe travel; travelers will not return. Avoid the *chén* hour.

**Collection Day (*Shōurì*):**
May submit memorials with **one hundred twenty passages**. Favorable for resolving calamities, protecting livestock, and safeguarding the home.

**Taboos:**
Do not submit memorials to resolve legal disputes—this will bring imprisonment and misfortune. Avoid the *wǔ* hour.

**Opening Day (*Kāirì*):**
May submit memorials with **one hundred twenty passages**. Favorable for dispelling residual *qi*, banishing ancestral spirits, shamans, and livestock demons, as well as household *wǎngliàng* and杂神 ghosts.
**Taboos:** Do not submit memorials to guide the deceased—this will cause livestock to die. Avoid the *wǔ* hour.

**Closing Day (*Bìrì*):**
May submit memorials with **five passages**. Favorable for lifting prohibitions and breaking taboos that disrupt lifespan.
**Taboos:** Do not submit memorials to protect the household—this will harm wealth and bring misfortune. Avoid the *wèi* hour.

**Stem-Branch Memorial Taboos:**
- **甲子** (*Jiǎzǐ*): Perilous.
- **甲午** (*Jiǎwǔ*): Auspicious.
- **乙丑** (*Yǐchǒu*): Perilous.
- **乙未** (*Yǐwèi*): Auspicious.
- **丙寅** (*Bǐngyín*): Perilous—eldest daughter dies by sitting.
- **丙申** (*Bǐngshēn*): Great auspice.
- **丁卯** (*Dīngmǎo*): Perilous (eldest male dies by sitting; also taboo for officials).
- **丁酉** (*Dīngyǒu*): Inauspicious—death by sitting.
- **戊辰** (*Wùchén*): Perilous—taboo for purification.
- **戊戌** (*Wùxū*): Great peril—violent purification taboo.
- **己巳** (*Jǐsì*): Inauspicious.
- **己亥** (*Jǐhài*): Great auspice.
- **庚午** (*Gēngwǔ*): Inauspicious.
- **庚子** (*Gēngzǐ*): Great auspice.
- **辛丑** (*Xīnchǒu*): Inauspicious.
- **辛未** (*Xīnwèi*): Eldest son dies by sitting in three years.
- **壬申** (*Rénshēn*): Eldest son dies by sitting in one year.
- **壬寅** (*Rényín*): Auspicious (some say perilous).
- **癸酉** (*Guǐyǒu*): Mother dies by sitting.
- **癸卯** (*Guǐmǎo*): Great auspice.
- **甲戌** (*Jiǎxū*): Great auspice.
- **甲辰** (*Jiǎchén*): Inauspicious—death by sitting.
- **乙亥** (*Yǐhài*): Household prospers in sericulture.
- **乙巳** (*Yǐsì*): Inauspicious—death by sitting.
- **丙子** (*Bǐngzǐ*): Three deaths by sitting.
- **丙午** (*Bǐngwǔ*): Great auspice.
- **丁丑** (*Dīngchǒu*): Great auspice.
- **丁未** (*Dīngwèi*): Death by sitting occurs.
- **戊寅** (*Wùyín*): Husband and wife die by sitting.
- **戊申** (*Wùshēn*): Inauspicious—death by sitting.
- **己卯** (*Jǐmǎo*): Minor auspice.
- **己酉** (*Jǐyǒu*): Great auspice.
- **庚辰** (*Gēngchén*): Great auspice.
- **庚戌** (*Gēngxū*): Great auspice.
- **辛巳** (*Xīnsì*): Great auspice.
- **辛亥** (*Xīnhài*): Death by sitting.
- **壬午** (*Rénwǔ*): Great auspice.
- **壬子** (*Rénzǐ*): Great auspice.
- **癸未** (*Guǐwèi*): Great auspice.
- **癸丑** (*Guǐchǒu*): Great auspice.
- **甲申** (*Jiǎshēn*): Auspicious.
- **甲寅** (*Jiǎyín*): Death by sitting.
- **乙酉** (*Yǐyǒu*): Great auspice (some say perilous).
- **乙卯** (*Yǐmǎo*): Inauspicious.
- **丙戌** (*Bǐngxū*): Death in the household.
- **丙辰** (*Bǐngchén*): Inauspicious.
- **丁亥** (*Dīnghài*): Inauspicious.
- **丁巳** (*Dīngsì*): Great auspice.
- **戊子** (*Wùzǐ*): Minor auspice.
- **戊午** (*Wùwǔ*): Great auspice.
- **丁巳、戊午**: Perilous.
- **己未** (*Jǐwèi*): Great auspice.
- **己丑** (*Jǐchǒu*): Death by sitting.
- **庚申** (*Gēngshēn*): Auspicious.
- **庚寅** (*Gēngyín*): Great peril—death.
- **辛酉** (*Xīnyǒu*): Death by sitting.
- **辛卯** (*Xīnmǎo*): Auspicious.
- **壬戌** (*Rénxū*): Inauspicious.
- **壬辰** (*Rénchén*): Auspicious.
- **癸亥** (*Guǐhài*): Inauspicious.
- **癸巳** (*Guǐsì*): Daughter dies by sitting.

**Memorial Submission Rules:**
When submitting memorials, use a separate brush and inkstone—do not mix with others. Grind ink in a leftward motion, passing over the paper **forty-nine times**. If regrinding, follow the same method.

**Ritual Observances:**
Burn incense while writing memorials, facing north, and aligning with the hours of *hài* (亥), *sì* (巳), *wèi* (未), or *chǒu* (丑).

**Auspicious Hours for Memorials:**
Coincide with *mǎo* (卯), *sì* (巳), *shēn* (申), or *hài* (亥)—these hours are favorable for healing. Other hours are perilous and must be avoided.

**Taboos:**
Avoid submitting memorials during one’s own birth hour (*shēngnián*) or birth year (*běnmìng*). Do not violate these prohibitions.

**Execution Day (*Jiànrì*):**
May post talismans to dismantle ancestral halls and bind malevolent spirits.

**Monthly Taboos for Memorial Submission:**
- **January, July:** Submit at *bǔ* hour (哺时).
- **Regular Days:** Submit at *rén dìng* hour (人定时).
- **Destruction Day (*Pòrì*):** Submit at *píng dàn* hour (平旦时).
- **Collection Day (*Shōurì*):** Submit at *yú zhōng* hour (禺中时).
- **Purification Day (*Chúrì*):** Submit at *rì rù* hour (日入时).
- **Stabilization Day (*Dìngrì*):** Submit at *yè bàn* hour (夜半时).
- **Perilous Day (*Wēirì*):** Submit at *rì chū* hour (日出时).
- **Opening Day (*Kāirì*):** Submit at *rì zhōng* hour (日中时).
- **Completion Day (*Mǎnrì*):** Submit at *huáng hūn* hour (黄昏时).
- **Execution Day (*Zhírì*):** Submit at *jī wū* hour (鸡鸣时).
- **Closing Day (*Bìrì*):** Submit at *rì yì* hour (日昳时).

**Universal Taboos:**
Avoid submitting memorials during *dǒuxì* hours (斗系) on these twelve days—this harms the officiant and the ritual master. Also avoid during funerals, weddings, or betrothals.

**Taboo Days for Healing:**
*Jiǎwǔ* (甲午), *Jiǎshēn* (甲申), *Jiǎxū* (甲戌), *Jiǎyín* (甲寅), *Yǐmǎo* (乙卯), *Bǐngchén* (丙辰)—all perilous. Additionally, avoid *yín* (寅), *mǎo* (卯), *shēn* (申), *yǒu* (酉), *wǔ* (午), and *chǒu* (丑) hours, especially *xīnwèi* (辛未). All memorial rituals, supplications, and petitions must avoid *dǒuxì* hours.

**Monthly *Jiànrì* Hours:**
- **February, August:** *xū* hour (戌时).
- **March, September:** *zǐ* hour (子时).
- **April, October:** *yín* hour (寅时).
- **May, November:** *chén* hour (辰时).
- **June, December:** *wǔ* hour (午时).

**Ritual Timing:**
Approaching the main day, submit memorials at *tài yī* hour (太一下) to avoid *dǒuxì* conflicts.

**Commandeering Rituals (*Zhàomìng*):**
Use one’s birth day and birth year (e.g., *jiǎchén* (甲辰), *yǐsì* (乙巳)). Food from birth-year rituals must not be fed to outsiders; other ritual food must be distributed to guests.

**General Precautions:**
When petitioning celestial officials or making vows, avoid inauspicious days:
- **January:** *gēngshēn* (庚申)
- **February:** *xīnyǒu* (辛酉)
- **March:** *jiǎxū* (甲戌)
- **April:** *guǐhài* (癸亥)
- **May:** *rénzǐ* (壬子)
- **June:** *guǐchǒu* (癸丑)
- **July:** *jiǎyín* (甲寅)
- **August:** *yǐmǎo* (乙卯)
- **September:** *jiǎchén* (甲辰)
- **October:** *dīngsì* (丁巳)
- **November:** *bǐngwǔ* (丙午)
- **December:** *guǐwèi* (癸未).

**Ritual Precautions:**

On days of *Zhàomìng* murderous harm (上章杀害), no petitions may be made—all undertakings are forbidden.

On days of the **Five Virtues/Powers** (*wǔdé*), one may atone for sins or seek blessings for good intentions.

- **Days of Virtue/Power (*Dé Rì*) and Taboo for *Zhàomìng* Rituals:**
  *Jiǎchén* (甲辰), *Cǐngchén* (丙辰), *Wùchén* (戊辰) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.
  *Gēngchén* (庚辰) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.
  *Yǐsì* (乙巳) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.
  *Xīnsì* (辛巳) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.
  *Guǐsì* (癸巳) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.
  *Jǐsì* (己巳) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.
  *Dīngsì* (丁巳) — avoid *Zhàomìng* rituals.

On days of the Five Virtues/Powers, it is auspicious to seek blessings and fulfill vows.

For any vow, use the birth-year day of the vow (*tiān yuàn rì*), specifically *Jǐchǒu* (己丑), which grants ease in attaining one’s desires.

**Favorable Days for *Zhàomìng* Rituals and Exorcisms:**
*Jiǎzǐ* (甲子) day: *Rénshēn* (壬申), *Guǐyǒu* (癸酉), *Xīnsì* (辛巳), *Rénwǔ* (壬午).
*Jiǎshēn* (甲申), *Yǐyǒu* (乙酉), *Dīnghài* (丁亥), *Wùzǐ* (戊子), *Jǐchǒu* (己丑), *Xīnmǎo* (辛卯), *Jiǎchén* (甲辰), *Cǐngwǔ* (丙午), *Dīngwèi* (丁未), *Wùshēn* (戊申), *Gēngxū* (庚戌), *Rénzǐ* (壬子), *Guǐchǒu* (癸丑), *Cǐngchén* (丙辰), *Dīngsì* (丁巳), *Wùwǔ* (戊午), *Jǐwèi* (己未), *Gēngshēn* (庚申), *Xīnyǒu* (辛酉), *Jiǎwǔ* (甲午), *Cǐngshēn* (丙申), *Dīngyǒu* (丁酉).

These are favorable days for *Zhàomìng* rituals; inauspicious days are excluded.

**Additional Precautions:**
Avoid overlapping inauspicious hours (*dǒuxì* conflicts):
- *Zǐ* hour (子时) conflicts with *wǔ* hour (午时).
- *Wǔ* hour (午时) conflicts with *zǐ* hour (子时).

When initiating *Zhàomìng* rituals, use *zǐ* (子) and *wǔ* (午) hours for invocation. If encountering conflicting hours or *dǒuxì* strikes, avoid them:
- If *dǒuxì* strikes at *zǐ* hour (子), avoid *zǐ* hour (子时).
- If *dǒuxì* strikes at *wǔ* hour (午), avoid *wǔ* hour (午时).
If the patient is critically ill, rituals may be performed outside these hours.

**Taboo Directions for Treating Illness:**
- **January:** Do not face east—patient will die.
- **July:** Do not face west—patient will die.
- **February:** Do not face north—patient will die.
- **August:** Do not face south—patient will die.
- **March:** Do not face west—patient will die.
- **September:** Do not face east—patient will die.
- **April:** Do not face south—patient will die.
- **October:** Do not face north—patient will die.
- **May:** Do not face east—patient will die.
- **November:** Do not face west—patient will die.
- **June:** Do not face north—patient will die.
- **December:** Do not face south—patient will die.

On *Gēngxīn* (庚辛) days, avoid treating illness during *bǔ* hour (哺时) or *rìrù* hour (日入时)—patient will die.

**Celestial Officials and Their Corresponding Days:**
- **January, December:** *Tài Shàng Xūwú Zhàngrén Gōng* (太上虚无丈人宫).
- **June, July:** *Tài Shàng Jiǔ Qì Wénchāng Gōng* (太上九气文昌宫).
- **February:** *Tài Shàng Xuánlǎo Xiāndū Gōng* (太上玄老仙都宫).
- **August:** *Tài Shàng Tiān Dì Gōng* (太上天帝宫).
- **March, April:** *Wúshàng Sān Tiān Tàiqīng Guān* (无上三天太清官).
- **September, October:** *Tài Shàng Dàdào Gōng* (太上大道宫).
- **May:** *Tài Shàng Zhòngdào Gōng* (太上重道宫).
- **November:** *Tài Shàng Shìzhōng, Zuǒyòu Jiànshén, Zhū Jiāngjūn Gōng* (太上侍中、左右监神，诸将军宫).

**Ritual Officials and Their Corresponding Days:**
- **1st day:** *Jiàn Yùcāo* (建玉曹) — invokes *Chìxū Gōng* (赤虚宫).
- **16th day:** *Sī Fēicāo* (司非曹) — invokes *Běifǔ Gōng* (北府宫).
- **2nd day:** *Tàisūcāo* (太素曹) — invokes *Tàiwēi Gōng* (太微宫).
- **17th day:** *Sī Jiàncāo* (司奸曹) — invokes *Nánjī Gōng* (南箕宫).
- **3rd day:** *Tàiwēicāo* (太微曹) — invokes *Běipíng Gōng* (北平宫).
- **18th day:** *Tǒngshècāo* (统摄曹) — invokes *Tōngmíng Gōng* (通明宫).
- **4th day:** *Dūzhèngcāo* (都正曹) — invokes *Tàiqīng Gōng* (太清宫).
- **19th day:** *Tǒnglùcāo* (统录曹) — invokes *Xīxū Gōng* (西虚宫).
- **5th day:** *Zhèngyīcāo* (正一曹) — invokes *Tōngmíng Gōng* (通明宫).
- **20th day:** *Jiànkǎocāo* (监考曹) — invokes *Sīmìng Gōng* (司命宫).
- **6th day:** *Xuányīcāo* (玄一曹) — invokes *Shàngmíng Gōng* (上明宫).
- **21st day:** *Jiànsīcāo* (监司曹) — invokes *Yángmíng Gōng* (阳明宫).
- **7th day:** *Tàisūcāo* (太素曹) — invokes *Gāolíng Gōng* (高灵宫).
- **22nd day:** *Diǎnkǎocāo* (典考曹) — invokes *Tàiyáng Gōng* (太阳宫).
- **8th day:** *Língjícāo* (灵集曹) — invokes *Zǐwēi Gōng* (紫微宫).
- **23rd day:** *Sīgōngcāo* (司宫曹) — invokes *Shàoyáng Gōng* (少阳宫).
- **9th day:** *Mǔlíngcāo* (母灵曹) — invokes *Dàichūn Gōng* (待春宫).
- **24th day:** *Xuányuáncāo* (玄元曹) — invokes *Tàiyīn Gōng* (太阴宫).
- **10th day:** *Tàiqīngcāo* (太清曹) — invokes *Wǔlíng Gōng* (武灵宫).
- **25th day:** *Tàixuáncāo* (太玄曹) — invokes *Shàoyáng Gōng* (少阳宫).
- **11th day:** *Sānshuǐcāo* (三水曹) — invokes *Sùnǚ Gōng* (素女宫).
- **26th day:** *Dūsīcāo* (都司曹) — invokes *Běichén Guān* (北辰官).
- **12th day:** *Sīlùcāo* (司录曹) — invokes *Jùyě Gōng* (巨野宫).
- **27th day:** *Dūhòucāo* (都候曹) — invokes *Tàibái Gōng* (太白宫).
- **13th day:** *Qīngxùcāo* (清叙曹) — invokes *Xīmíng Gōng* (西明宫).
- **28th day:** *Zhíshǐcāo* (直使曹) — invokes *Línmíng Gōng* (林明宫).
- **14th day:** *Xuánzhèngcāo* (玄正曹) — invokes *Shàngjiàng Gōng* (上绛宫).
- **29th day:** *Zhēnsīkǎocāo* (真司考曹) — invokes *Qīngyáng Gōng* (清阳宫).
- **15th day:** *Zhōngdūcāo* (中都曹) — invokes *Qǔpíng Gōng* (曲平宫).
- **30th day:** *Diǎnkǎocāo* (典考曹) — invokes *Qǐmíng Gōng* (启明宫).

The **Supreme Celestial Masters** (*Wúshàng Sān Tiān*, *Wújié Dàdào*, *Tài Shàng Lǎojūn*, *Dūzhèng Jícāo*) command nine million nine hundred ninety-nine thousand soldiers, male and female officials. The *Rìyuè Gōngcāo* (日月宫曹) remain unchanged.

**Ritual Petitions:**
When submitting petitions to celestial officials for blessings or vows, examine the scriptures meticulously and distinguish the appropriate officials. According to the **One Thousand Two Hundred Official Rituals** (*qiān èr bǎi guān yí*), for minor illnesses or light matters, one should only state: *"I humbly prostrate myself twice."*

For severe illnesses or grave matters, one should state: *"I humbly prostrate myself, guilty of death, and bow twice."*

For severe illnesses or grave matters, one must also specify the appropriate officials:
*"To the Supreme Celestial Master (*Tàixuán Dūzhèngyī*), the Pacifying Virtue/Power (*Píngqì*) of the Celestial Teacher (*Tiānshī*), the humble servant [Name] prostrates, guilty of death, and bows twice."*

*"In [Name] district, county, village, and among the male and female households, in the year of *Rén* (壬), at age [X], with [Y] households, the illness is as follows: [describe illness].*

*Later, it is stated: *"I have gone to the [appropriate] Celestial Officials as usual. The humble servant [Name] is sincerely fearful, prostrates, guilty of death, and bows twice."*

On *Jiǎchén* (甲辰) days, the **Forest Chariot Master** (*Línchē Zhǔrén*) enters the court; retain this record."

For the **Six Celestial Stems** (*Liùjiǎ*), the **Forest Chariot Master** (*Línchē Zhǔrén*) enters the court—retain this record.

**Fire Master** (*Huǒshǔ*) enters on *Jiāxū* (甲戌) days—retain this record.
**Grass Master** (*Cǎoshǔ*) enters on *Jiāshēn* (甲申) days—retain this record.
**Water Master** (*Shuǐshǔ*) enters on *Jiāzǐ* (甲子) days—retain this record.
**Disease Master** (*Bìngshǔ*) enters on *Jiāyín* (甲寅) days—retain this record.
**Military Master** (*Jiānbīngshǔ*) enters on *Jiāwǔ* (甲午) days for **martial disputes, litigation, and warfare**—retain this record.
The **Six Celestial Stems** (*Liùjiǎ*) are to be kept in mind for their **divine influences**.

In the **first month**, at **dawn** (*Píngdàn*), it is the **Master’s auspicious hour** (*Shǔshí*); at **sunrise** (*Rìchū*), it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour** (*Shǔfùshí*).
In the **seventh month**, at **midday** (*Rìbǔshí*), it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **mealtime** (*Shíshí*), it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.

In the **second month**, at **sunrise**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **dusk** (*Huánghūnshí*), it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.
In the **eighth month**, at **sunset** (*Rìrùshí*), it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **midnight** (*Yǔzhōng*), it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.

In the **third month**, at **sunrise**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **midnight** (*Réndìngshí*), it is the **Master’s Daughter’s auspicious hour** (*Shǔnǚshí*).
In the **ninth month**, at **dusk**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **sunrise**, it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.

In the **fourth month**, at **midnight**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **midnight** (*Réndìngshí*), it is the **Master’s Mother’s auspicious hour** (*Shǔmǔshí*).
In the **tenth month**, at **midnight**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **sunrise**, it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.

In the **fifth month**, at **noon** (*Rìzhōng*), it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **cockcrow** (*Jīmíng*), it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.
In the **eleventh month**, at **month’s end** (*Jǐnshí*), it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **midday** (*Rìbǔshí*), it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.

In the **sixth month**, at **sunrise**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **dawn**, it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.
In the **twelfth month**, at **cockcrow**, it is the **Master’s auspicious hour**; at **sunset**, it is the **Master’s Wife’s auspicious hour**.

The **twelve months** above: the **Celestial Officials** (*Guānshì*) for **Master and Wife** (*Shǔfù*) are two—**Celestial Teacher** (*Tiānshī*) and **Celestial Master** (*Tiānshǔ*). If one encounters these **inauspicious hours** (*shuāishí*), one must avoid them and not violate them. If the **fate** (*mìng*) of an illness is at the **turning point of the candle** (*zhuǎnzhú*), one may report it to the officials.

For those **Celestial Officials** who are **worthy and capable** (*néng*), they can **move mountains, stop floods, summon clouds, and create rain**; they can **summon ten thousand spirits** (*wànshén*) with a single command, **cause plants to grow in winter** (*dōngshēng cǎomù*), and **induce frost in summer** (*xiàjié bīngshuāng*). If one can perform such deeds, then **this ritual manual** (*cèshū*) is **not needed for oneself** (*bùyòng cìshū qí shēn*). Therefore, when one is **harmed by water, fire, knives, or weapons**, one must **clearly report to the Celestial Officials** (*chénggào Zhǔshì*) and **heed these prohibitions** (*míng jiē qǐshí*).

For **Daoist laypersons** (*dàodù mín*) offering **sacrificial meals** (*jiěshí*), one must **contemplate the Five Celestial Emperors** (*wǔ Dì*) and **name the Six Celestial Stems** (*Liùjiǎ*), invoking the **worthy and noble deities and Daoists** (*shénxiān zūnxián, wǔyuè míngshān dàoshì*) to **pray for blessings** (*qǐng yuàn zhǔrén défú*) on the host.

The following **twelve days** are **forbidden for submitting petitions or conducting rituals**:
First month, the **11th day**; second month, the **3rd day** and **18th day**; third month, the **7th day** and **9th day**; fourth month, the **15th day**; fifth month, the **2nd day** and **5th day**; sixth month, the **3rd day** and **13th day**; seventh month, the **1st day** and **17th day**; eighth month, the **2nd day** and **18th day**; ninth month, the **9th day**; tenth month, the **5th day**; eleventh month, the **4th day** and **16th day**; twelfth month, the **21st day**. These are **days of great misfortune**.

The following **twelve favorable days** are **suitable for burning incense and submitting petitions**:
First month, the **11th day**; second month, the **3rd day** and **18th day**; third month, the **7th day** and **9th day**; fourth month, the **15th day**; fifth month, the **2nd day** and **5th day**; sixth month, the **3rd day** and **13th day**; seventh month, the **1st day** and **17th day**; eighth month, the **2nd day** and **18th day**; ninth month, the **9th day**; tenth month, the **5th day**; eleventh month, the **4th day** and **16th day**; twelfth month, the **21st day**.

The **five sacrificial festivals** (*wǔlà*) are as follows:
First month, the **1st day**—**Celestial Sacrifice** (*Tiān là*);
Fifth month, the **5th day**—**Earth Sacrifice** (*Dì là*);
Seventh month, the **7th day**—**Dao and Virtue Sacrifice** (*Dàodé là*);
Tenth month, the **1st day**—**Commoner’s New Year Sacrifice** (*Mínsuì là*);
Twelfth month—**Noble’s Sacrifice** (*Wánghóu là*).

These are **auspicious days**. For households that **follow the Dao**, they should **conform to these festivals** (*yīncì*) when **honoring ancestors**. One must **first submit a petition** (*shàngzhāng*), **inviting the ancestors** (*qǐng xiān rén*), and then **arrange the sacrifices**. This is the **way of filial children**.

The above **prohibitions for submitting petitions** (*shàngzhāng jìnyì*) must **not be violated**. Be cautious in conducting rituals—**great auspice** (*dàjí*) will follow.

For treating illnesses, one may use the **auspicious hours of the Vermilion Pine Child** (*Chìsōngzǐ shí*).

In any **single day**, one must **not repeatedly enter the Pure and Serene Hall** (*Jìngshàng*) to submit petitions.

**Important Ritual Instructions** (*Xiūyào shìyì jìyìuè zhī shí jìng, xiūyào kēyì jìyìuè zhī shíyī*)
Compiled by the **Three Cavern Daoist** (*Sāndòng dàoshì*) **Zhū Fǎmǎn**.

**Ritual Manual for Petitions and Auspicious Hours** (*Zhāngkē xìnyì cèshū*).

1. **Chapter for Initial Purification and Expiation** (*Chūhuà chúzuì zhāng*).
2. **Chapter for Couples Seeking a Son or Male Child** (*Fūfù qiúzǐ qǐnán zhāng*).
3. **Chapter for Treating Chronic Illnesses in Couples** (*Fūfù jībìng yīzhì zhāng*).
4. **Chapter for Postpartum Illnesses, Confessing Guilt, and Seeking Recovery** (*Chǎnhòu jíbìng, shǒuzuì qǐyù zhāng*).
5. **Chapter for Couples Cultivating Vital Qi and Mutual Resonance, Confessing Guilt** (*Fūfù xīngqì, xiāngyìng shǒuguò zhāng*).
6. **Chapter for Severe Illnesses, Reporting to Celestial Officials, and Seeking Assistance** (*Kùnbìng qǐngguān, yīshí xiāngfù zhāng*).
7. **Chapter for Household Calamities, Seeking Official Assistance, and Praying for Protection** (*Jiādào lùnlè juézǐ, qǐngguān qǐyòu zhāng*).
8. **Chapter for Supernatural Phenomena in the Residence, Surrendering and Seeking Clarity** (*Zhái zhōng guāngguài, guīmìng qǐbái zhāng*).
9. **Chapter for Illnesses Caused by Violations, Removing All Prohibitions, and Seeking Official Salvation** (*Jíbìng diétuó suàn, yíxí zhūjì, qǐngguān jiùzhāng*).
10. **Chapter for Illnesses Due to Spiritual Discord, Rectifying the Heart and Mouth, and Seeking Divine Mercy** (*Jíbìng guīhuà, xīnkǒu yǒuwéi, gǎi gēng qǐ’ēn zhāng*).
11. **Chapter for False Accusations by Officials, Seeking Exculpation** (*Qīngguān shōubǔ, wàngzuò yīfǎ zhāng*).
12. **Chapter for Couples Separated, Terminating Oaths and Dispelling Supernatural Ills** (*Fūfù líbié, duànzhù xiāoguài zhāng*).
13. **Chapter for Violating Rituals and Breaking Prohibitions, Confessing and Seeking Pardon** (*Wéikē fànjìn, shǒuxiè qǐyuán zhāng*).

For the above rituals, use **white silk forty *zǐ* (尺)**, **uncooked rice one *dǒu* (斗)**, **oil one *dǒu* (斗)**, **incense one *jīn* (斤)**, **paper one hundred sheets**, **two brush pens**, **one ink pellet**, **one writing knife**, **two mats**, and **five *zǐ* (尺) of cloth towels**.

For **Chapter of Gratitude and Expiation for Sorrows, Hardships, and Oppressions** (*Yōuyù kùnrǔ, xièguò jiějiù zhāng*), use:
**paper one hundred sheets**, **two brush pens**, **one ink pellet**, **one pair of golden rings**, **one writing knife**, **five *dǒu* (斗) of rice**, **two mats**, and **five *liǎng* (两) of incense**.

For **Chapter of Treating Illnesses in the Awakened, Confessing Guilt, and Seeking Mercy** (*Zhìjué yǒují, shǒuzuì qǐ’ēn zhāng*), use:
**one hundred twenty coins**, **three *dǒu* (斗) of rice**, **paper one hundred sheets**, **one brush pen**, **one ink pellet**, **one *liǎng* (两) of incense**, **one mat**, and **one writing knife**.

For **Chapter of Terminating an Epidemic** (*Duànwēn yì zhāng*), use:
**paper one hundred sheets**, **three *liǎng* (两) of incense**, **one brush pen**, **one ink pellet**, **one writing knife**, and **two mats**.

For **each household member** (*suí jiā kǒukǒu bié*), use:
**one *shēng* (升) of oil**, **one hundred coins**, and **one *zhàng* (丈) of silk**.

For **Chapter of Couples’ Illnesses and Sorrows, Terminating Ghostly Litigation, and Safeguarding the Perilous** (*Fūfù jíyù, duànchú guǐsòng, fúdāng bǎo’ān zhāng*), use:
**paper three hundred sheets**, **three *dǒu* (斗) of oil**, **forty *zǐ* (尺) of green silk**, **one ink pellet**, **two brush pens**, **five *liǎng* (两) of incense**, **five *dǒu* (斗) of rice**, **two mats**, and **one writing knife**.

For **Chapter of Invoking Rain** (*Qǐngyǔ zhāng*), use:
**three *dǒu* (斗) and six *shēng* (升) of oil**, **two brush pens**, **paper one hundred sheets**, **one ink pellet**, **one *liǎng* (两) of cinnabar**, **three *liǎng* (两) of incense**, **two mats**, **five *dǒu* (斗) of rice**, and **three hundred sixty-five coins**.

**Chapter of Invoking Clear Weather** (*Qǐngqíng zhāng*).
**Use:** five *jīn* (斤) of wax, two brush pens, paper one hundred sheets, two *shí* (十) of ink pellets, five *liǎng* (两) of cinnabar, one writing knife.

**Chapter of Terminating the Ill-Fated Hour of *Zìwǔ* (子午) and Safeguarding the Perilous** (*Jiě zǐwǔ yuánchén jíyù huì zhāng*).
**Use:** white rice, one *dùn* (顿) and three *dǒu* (斗), four mats, one *dǒu* (斗) and two *shēng* (升) of oil, one *jiàng* (绛) silk.

For those without illness (*wújí zhě*), **use:** paper one hundred sheets, two brush pens, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, one writing knife, one hundred twenty *mái* (枚) of tally counters, one pair of gold rings, three *jīn* (斤) of incense, three colored strings, nine varieties, each string one hundred twenty *zhǎng* (丈) in length. For severe ill-fatedness (*jíyù zhòng zhě*), **use:** five colors, each three *liǎng* (两).

**Chapter of Terminating the Great Ill-Fated Hour of the Eight *Guà* (卦) and Safeguarding the Perilous** (*Jiě bāguà yuánchén dàjíyù zhāng*).
**Use:** plain white silk forty *zǐ* (尺), one *shuò* (硕) of rice, plain silk three *liǎng* (两), one pair of gold rings (weight two *fēn* (分)), paper one hundred sheets, two brush pens, one ink pellet, thirteen *liǎng* (两) of incense, two mats, and one writing knife.

Daoists who have not yet received the **Three *Wǔ* (五) Red *Zhù* (箓)** or the **Ill-Fated Hour River Chart** (*Yuánchén hé tú*) and similar methods are **not permitted** to perform the **Great Ill-Fated Hour Ritual** (*dà zhāng*) or other major ceremonies. Those who have received the **One Hundred Fifty *Jiāng* (将) *Zhù* (箓)** and **ritual office records** (*zhì zhí*) may only perform the remaining chapters.

**Chapter of Resettlement and Household Relocation Due to Inauspiciousness** (*Rùjū gǎiyì bùlì, dàxiǎo xièzhái zhāng*).
**Use:** paper one hundred sheets, one ink pellet, one brush pen, one writing knife, five *jīn* (斤) of wax, five colored fabrics each according to their respective numbers, two mats, five *dǒu* (斗) of rice, one hundred twenty *zhèn* (镇) coins, and three *liǎng* (两) of incense.

**Chapter of New Residence Fear and Household Pacification** (*Xīnjū kǒngjù, zhènzhái zhāng*).
**Use:** silk ten *zǐ* (尺), one hundred twenty coins, five *dǒu* (斗) of rice, two mats, paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, three *liǎng* (两) of incense, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Ceasing Unnatural Expenditures and Terminating Ghostly Litigation** (*Xūhào guǐguài, duànjué yāngzhù zhāng*).
**Use:** paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, one writing knife, one mat, one *dǒu* (斗) of oil, twenty-four *zǐ* (尺) of yellow cloth, white rice one *shuò* (硕) and two *dǒu* (斗), and two *liǎng* (两) of incense.

**Chapter of Terminating the Litigation of the Three Generations and Five Ancestors** (*Shì sānzēng wǔzǔ yāngzhù zhāng*).
**Use:** wood fifty *jīn* (斤), burned or ground into powder as per the method; alternatively, twenty-five *jīn* (斤) or fifteen *jīn* (斤). Yellow cloth five *zhàng* (丈), rice one *dùn* (顿) and five *dǒu* (斗), paper one hundred sheets, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, one brush pen, one *liǎng* (两) of incense, and one mat.

**Chapter of Official and Private Litigation, Death and Disease in Succession, and Terminating the Five Tomb Litigation** (*Guān sī jiùyì, sǐbìng xiānglián, duàn wǔmù yāngzhù zhāng*).
**Use:** paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, one mat, one *dǒu* (斗) of oil, twenty-four *zǐ* (尺) of yellow cloth, raw rice one *dùn* (顿) and two *dǒu* (斗), one *liǎng* (两) of cinnabar, and one *liǎng* (两) of incense.

**Chapter of Dreaming of the Deceased and Confusion, and Terminating the Tomb Litigation** (*Shù mèng jiàn wángrén hùnxiāo, xiāo mùzhù zhāng*).
**Use:** yellow cloth five *zhàng* (丈), plain white silk forty *zǐ* (尺), three *dǒu* (斗) and six *shēng* (升) of oil, paper one hundred sheets, two brush pens, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, one writing knife, three *liǎng* (两) of incense, and two *liǎng* (两) of cinnabar.

**Chapter of Minor Exorcism for Household Anomalies** (*Zhái zhōng guàiyì, xiǎo qūchú zhāng*).
**Use:** paper fifty sheets, one brush pen, one ink pellet, three *dǒu* (斗) of rice, one mat, one *liǎng* (两) of incense, and seventy-two coins.

**Chapter of Major Exorcism After Funeral and Burial** (*Sàngwáng bìn hòu, dà qūchú zhāng*).
**Use:** paper one hundred sheets, two brush pens, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, one writing knife, two *liǎng* (两) of incense, one mat, one hundred twenty coins, one *liǎng* (两) of cinnabar, ten *zǐ* (尺) of plain white silk, and three *dǒu* (斗) of rice.

**Chapter of Death and Disease Persisting, Using a Silver Figure as Substitute** (*Sǐbìng bùjué, yínrén dài xíng zhāng*).
**Use:** a thin silver figure, according to the number of household members; if no silver is available, use ninety-nine *qián* (钱) of tin coins. The figure is to be inscribed and cast into water. Paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, one writing knife, five *dǒu* (斗) of rice, two *liǎng* (两) of incense, and twelve *zǐ* (尺) of plain white silk.

**Chapter of Capturing Wandering *Qi* (气) and Treating Strange Illnesses** (*Shìbìng duō guài, shōubǔ gùqì zhāng*).
**Use:** sixty *dìzào* (地奏) tablets, each measuring one *zǐ* (尺) and two *cùn* (寸) in length, one *cùn* (寸) and two *fēn* (分) in width, and three *fēn* (分) in thickness. Nine *dǒu* (斗) of red small beans, one hundred twenty *zǐ* (尺) of left-spun silk thread, one large knife, paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one mat, two *liǎng* (两) of incense, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Terminating the Twenty-Four *Yù* (狱) Ill-Fatedness** (*Chénzhì jíyù, jiě èrshísì yù zhāng*).
**Use:** twenty-four *zǐ* (尺) of blue-patterned silk, three *liǎng* (两) of incense, paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one *shí* (十) of ink pellets, five *dǒu* (斗) of rice, one writing knife, and one mat.

**Chapter of Extracting the Five *Mountain Peaks* (*Wǔyuè*) and Rescuing Illness** (*Bá wǔyuè, jiùbìng zhāng*).
**Use:** plain silk three *liǎng* (两), one pair of gold rings, ten *liǎng* (两) of incense, paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one ink pellet, two mats, five *dǒu* (斗) of rice, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Terminating the Five *Dǒu* (斗) Closed Litigation and Rescuing the Severely Ill-Fated** (*Jiě wǔdǒu bìxì, jiāojué bá mìng zhāng*).
**Use:** plain white silk forty *zǐ* (尺), white silk three *liǎng* (两), one pair of gold rings, paper two hundred sheets, two brush pens, one ink pellet, two mats, five *liǎng* (两) of incense, five *dǒu* (斗) of rice, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Dreaming of the Deceased in Closed Litigation, and Great Relocation for Rescue** (*Mèng jiàn wángrén bìxì, dà qiāndá zhāng*).
**Use:** plain white silk forty *zǐ* (尺), paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, one *dǒu* (斗) of oil, two mats, three *liǎng* (两) of incense, one hundred twenty coins, and five *dǒu* (斗) of rice.

**Use:** paper one hundred sheets, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, one *dǒu* (斗) of oil, three *liǎng* (两) of incense, one mat, three *dǒu* (斗) of rice, and one hundred twenty coins.

**Chapter of Requesting Grace After Ritual Completion** (*Fú mǎn hòu, qiāndá qǐng’ēn zhāng*).

**Chapter of Dissolving Curses and Malicious Spells** (*Jiě zhòu zhǔ zhāng*)

**Chapter of Dissolving the Five Directions’ Curses and Malicious Spells** (*Jiě wǔfāng zhòu zhǔ zhāng*)
**Use:** three hundred twenty-six coins, colored silk strips according to age, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, five *dǒu* of rice, two mats, five *liǎng* of incense, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Quelling Slanderous Words and Defamation** (*Xiāo kǒushé fěibàng zhāng*)
**Use:** one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, five-colored silk threads according to directional quantities, two hundred forty coins, five *dǒu* of rice, two mats, and three *liǎng* of incense.

**Chapter of Pursuing Thieves** (*Zhuī dào zhāng*)
**Use:** three *jīn* of wax, fifty *jīn* of charcoal, one hundred twenty coins, three *dǒu* of rice, one mat, three *liǎng* of incense; fifty sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Requesting a Son** (*Qǐ zǐ zhāng*)
**Use:** five-colored left-twisted cords according to directional measurements, ninety *zǐ* of blue-patterned silk, one large knife, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, nineteen ink pellets, three *liǎng* of incense, two mats, one writing knife, and five *dǒu* of rice.

**Chapter of Dissolving Calamity and Extending Life** (*Jiě è yánmìng zhāng*)
**Use:** two *dǒu* and four *shēng* of oil, two *shú* and four *dǒu* of rice, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, two *liǎng* of cinnabar, one writing knife, and one mat.

**Chapter of Saving Critical Sudden Illness and Requesting Life** (*Jiù jī bìng hū jù sè qǐngmìng zhāng*)
**Use:** five *dǒu* of rice, seven *shēng* of oil, one hundred twenty coins, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, two *liǎng* of incense, and two mats.

**Chapter of Extending Fate and Drawing Out Life** (*Yán suàn bá mìng zhāng*)
**Use:** forty *zǐ* of plain white silk, one *shú* of rice, five *shēng* of oil, three *liǎng* of incense, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, one mat, and one ink stick.

**Chapter of Recording Soul and Spirit** (*Lù húnpò zhāng*)
**Use:** one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, five *liǎng* of incense, two *liǎng* of cinnabar, one writing knife, two mats, a pair of gold rings, three *liǎng* of plain silk, one *jī* of gauze, one *shú* and two *dǒu* of rice, and one hundred twenty *suànzǐ* (divination counters).

**Chapter of Measuring Calamity and Protection** (*Dù è bǎohù zhāng*)
**Use:** one hundred twenty coins, one mat, one *liǎng* of cinnabar, two *liǎng* of incense, one writing knife, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, and three *dǒu* of rice.

**Chapter of the Eight Directions’ Great Protection** (*Bāfāng dà bǎohù zhāng*)
**Use:** five *jīn* of incense, one mat, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, three *dǒu* of rice, one thousand two hundred coins, and three sets of clothing.

**Chapter of the Five Directions’ Life-Nurturing Protection** (*Wǔfāng shēngyǎng bǎohù zhāng*)
**Use:** one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, one *jī* of gauze, one *shú* and two *dǒu* of rice, a pair of silver rings, three *liǎng* of black silk, three *dǒu* of oil, two mats, and one *dǒu* of blended incense.

**Chapter of Stagnant Illness and Retreat, Dissolving the Net of Fate** (*Zhì jí jìntuì, jiě luówǎng zhāng*)
**Use:** one *shí* and two *dǒu* of rice, forty *zǐ* of plain white silk, five *liǎng* of incense, two mats, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, and one writing knife.

**Chapter of Supporting Decline, Measuring Calamity, and Dissolving the Net of Fate** (*Fú shuāi dù è, jiě luówǎng zhāng*)
**Use:** forty *zǐ* of plain white silk, one *shú* of rice, a pair of gold rings, one hundred sheets of paper, five *liǎng* of cinnabar, one brush pen, one ink pellet, one writing knife, two mats, and five *liǎng* of incense.

**Chapter of Prolonged Illness and Great Calamity, Golden and Purple Substitution of Form** (*Jiǔ bìng dà è, jīnzǐ dài xíng zhāng*)
**Use:** two hundred sheets of paper, two brush pens, one ink pellet, one writing knife, ten *liǎng* of incense, two mats, one *shú* and two *dǒu* of rice, one *dǒu* of oil, five *liǎng* of cinnabar, a golden figurine weighing one *liǎng* and one *chǔ*, forty *zǐ* of purple-patterned silk, and two hundred forty *zhèn* coins.

**Note from Master Zhang of the Celestial Teacher:**
For petitions to the Celestial Officials (*Jǐ yì zhì qǐng zhāng*), the larger version requires one hundred sheets of paper and two brush pens, one ink pellet; the smaller version requires fifty sheets of paper and one brush pen. These are drafts for the petitioner’s use; errors may be corrected, but the seal of authenticity must not be altered. The laws of petitions must be clearly observed.

Petitions without proper seals are invalid. After submitting petitions, surplus offerings should be given to the poor to cultivate *yīndé* (hidden virtue); one must not hoard them all. Of the total, the master may use only three parts if calculations are made. The Celestial Laws are strict—offenders will be punished by the Three Officials, and their misfortune will extend to nine generations, condemning them as lower ghosts forever. Be most cautious.

For each mat, two *liǎng* of incense, one hundred sheets of paper, one brush pen, one ink pellet, and one writing knife: the poor may adjust according to means, while the wealthy should increase accordingly.

The *Fán Cāo Zhāng* states: If there are errors or omissions, submit them to the *Gōngcāo* (Functionary of Affairs). This method was originally intended for the dim-witted. Those who act with sincerity and precision may submit to the *Zhèngzhī* (Upright Official) for verification, using *qìyìn* (spirit-seal) to authenticate the petition, demonstrating humility and sincerity. Such petitions are permissible.

For those of sharp intellect and ambition, if they are capable of self-correction but instead act lazily, they will be reported to the *Gōngcāo*. The Celestial Officials will surely examine them, and repeated arrogance will not be pardoned. All *sàijiǔ* (sacrificial attendants) must be especially diligent and cautious.

**Order of Petitions for Illness:**
The *Tài Zhēn Kē* states: For all illnesses, first submit the *Shǒuzhuàng Zhāng* (Initial Symptom Petition). If not cured, then submit the *Jiě Kǎo Zhāng* (Exoneration Petition).

For illnesses that persist, submit next the *Exoneration of the Deceased’s Crime and Demotion Petition*; if still not cured, submit the *Ascension to High Status Petition*. For cases of deep stagnation, submit the *Reversal of Killing and Ghostly Debt Petition*; if again stagnant, submit the *Great Exoneration of Calamity and Misfortune Petition*. If still no improvement, submit the *Five-Generations Tomb Demotion Petition*; if yet no change, submit the *Great Exoneration of Declining Epidemic and Severe Misfortune Petition*. If the illness remains uncured, submit the *Soul Return and Spirit Recovery Petition*; if still not cured, submit the *Tomb Pacification and Exoneration of the Five Soils’ Harm Petition*; if still not cured, submit the *Residence Pacification, Spirit Pacification, and Driving Away Ghostly Debt Petition*; if still not cured, submit the *Great Exoneration of Internal and External Debt Petition*. If the illness is urgent and constraining, submit the *Child-Midnight Petition for Life Extension*, along with the *Reversal of the Three Officials’ Death and Exoneration Petition*; if the illness fluctuates between improvement and relapse, submit the *Supplication to the Thirty-two Heavens Petition*. In cases of extreme peril, submit the *Ransom of Life and Offering of [Sacrificial Animal]*, along with the *Extraction of Life, Candle-Lighting, Exoneration of Retrogression and Connection*, *Five Lamps, Twenty-eight Constellations, Verification of Constellations*, and *Great Exoneration of the Deceased’s Debt*, totaling eighty-one petitions. Those without misfortune or illness must not presumptuously seek these petitions. Violators shall be subject to three punishments.

**Petitions During Avoidance of Taboos:**
The *Tài Zhēn Kē* states: On days of grand festivals and celebrations, submit petitions and offerings by name, without avoiding fierce winds or heavy rains, eclipses of the sun or moon, or celestial prohibitions. On such days, the Heavenly Emperor convenes a grand assembly. The *science* (法) decrees: On days of grand festivals and auspicious occasions, all must attend in their proper names, without avoiding daily or monthly taboos, and gather as usual. On these days, all great saints descend together, convening in the Hall of Treatment, their forms and shadows manifesting, and their resonance echoing uniformly across ten thousand *lǐ* (里). On these days, submit all petitions to the celestial hierarchy, conferring degrees and spirit-seals (*luóqìèqì* 箓契). Male and female officials, through virtue and merit, shall dissipate calamities and disperse misfortunes, all without restriction.

The *Xuāndū Lǜ* (玄都律) states: When submitting petitions for treatment, avoid the *wùchén* (戊辰) day. On the *wùxū* (戊戌) day, one must not submit petitions; days of impurity or defilement must not be used for petitions; nor should the *yuècháng* (月朝, new moon), *huìshuò* (晦朔, full moon), or days when commoners purify themselves be used for visiting the Hall of Treatment. Violators shall be penalized with two years of *suàn* (算, karmic reckoning). When submitting petitions for treatment, one must stand upright and walk properly, observe the order of the *science* (法) and its classifications, maintain solemn reverence, and avoid mixing men and women or looking about with disrespect. Violators shall be penalized with three *liǎng* (两) of *yù* (玉, jade). One must not submit petitions on behalf of those guilty of the *Ten Evils* or *Five Treasons*; the petitions must be sincere yet not overly ornate, clumsy yet not inept, plain yet not vulgar, truthful yet not deceptive, direct yet not insolent, eloquent yet not verbose, humble yet not filthy, pure yet not turbid, true yet not deceitful, concise yet full of sincerity. Then they shall move the heavens and earth, stir the ghosts and spirits, and be heard by the celestial bureaucracy, with responses arriving swiftly. Violators of the *science* (科) shall be penalized with one *jì* (纪) of *suàn* (算, karmic reckoning). Petitions must not be submitted with the back turned.

**《The Great True Science》** states:
When presenting petitions, face east. Subsequent petitions and exposed petitions must face north.

During daylight hours, when granting degrees, face east to break the contract. For urgent petitions from the **Star Hosts** (星宿) or the **Midday-Midnight Command Stars** (子午请命星), all face north and honor the **Great Emperor** (大帝). Unless it is a grand petition from the **Star Hosts** or a major ritual on the altar, all urgent petitions must be collected and expelled without bothering the **Exalted Ones** (露上).

**《The Mystic Capital Precepts》** states:
For petitions to **dispel illness** (消疾病), face the **Ghost Gate** (鬼门).
For petitions to **remove calamities and misfortunes** (消灾厄), face the **Earthly Portal** (地户).
For petitions seeking **longevity, wealth, and prosperity** (求长生、求富贵财利), face the **Heavenly Gate** (天门).
For petitions to **dispel slander and curses** (消口舌咒咀), face the **Human Gate** (人门).
To **ward off tigers**, face the **Tiger Direction** (寅); to **ward off serpents**, face the **Serpent Direction** (巳). When aligned with the **Heavenly Ganges** (天罡), great fortune follows.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **one hundred days of karmic reckoning** (罚算百日).

The Precepts state:
Petitions for **cultivating virtue and extending life** (修福延年), **dispelling disasters** (消却灾害), or **warding off a hundred ailments** (厌百病) must all face east.
Petitions for **clearing tomb curses** (解墓除责), **opening wisdom** (开心聪明), or **passing through calamities** (过灾度厄) must all face west.
Violation of these precepts results in **one hundred days of illness** (病百日).

For **life-or-death illnesses** (疾病百死一生), petitions must face north.
For **nurturing the body and preserving life** (修身养命), **softening and enriching fortune** (温润富贵), petitions must face south.

The Precepts state:
When presenting petitions to **acknowledge guilt** (谢罪), all household members must first face north and bow to the **Thirty-Two Heavens** (三十二天).
For **family-wide atonement** (举家大小), with hair unbound and hands clasped, face north and bow at the head of the petition.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **ten days of illness** (罚病十日).

**Regarding the use of auspicious days:**
The Precepts state:
Petitions for **seeking wealth** (求财) must be submitted on **Heavenly Granary Days** (天仓日) or **Steward Days** (戊子日).
For **seeking noble rank** (求爵位), use **Heavenly Treasury Days** (天府日) and avoid **Self-Punishment Days** (自刑日).
**Midday** (午), **Rooster** (酉), **Water Buffalo** (亥), and **Dragon** (辰) are all **Punishment Days** (刑日).
**Tiger** (寅) punishes **Snake** (巳), **Dog** (戌) punishes **Sheep** (未), **Rat** (子) punishes **Rabbit** (卯), **Monkey** (申) punishes **Tiger** (寅), **Rabbit** (卯) punishes **Rat** (子), and **Snake** (巳) punishes **Monkey** (申).
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **fifty days of illness** (考病五十日).

The Precepts state:
On **New Moon** (月朝), **Full Moon** (月半), **Dark Moon** (月晦), **Steward-Dragon Days** (戊辰), and **Steward-Dog Days** (戊戌), only **ritual worship** (应礼拜) and **reciting scriptures** (修诵经文) are permitted. Petitions and lawsuits are forbidden.
Violators shall be examined by the **Water Officials** (水官) and incur a penalty of **sixty days of illness** (罚六十日病).

The Precepts state:
On **auspicious days** (吉日), specifically **Steward-Dragon** (戊辰) and **Steward-Dog** (戊戌), one may present **functional petitions** (功章).
On **great celebratory days** (大庆之日), no additional petitions may be submitted.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **one hundred days of illness** (考病百日).

**Regarding mixed violations:**
The Precepts state:
Petitions from **Daoist female officials** (道士女官), **state and county officials** (州县官人), and **common Daoist laypeople** (百姓道民) must not be intermingled or submitted together, as their ranks differ.
Violators shall incur a penalty of **fifty days of illness** (考病五十日).
When **Daoist female officials** present petitions for **fasting assemblies** (斋会呈章), they must wear **proper ritual attire** (笏褐法服) in full order.
If a petition is submitted for **healing**, the host must not slaughter animals or offer sweets to the Daoist. If a Daoist knowingly consumes them, both the Daoist and the host shall be penalized, with **two *jì* of karmic reckoning reduced** (减算二纪).

During petition submission, household members must not **disrupt the order**, speak loudly, or disturb chickens and dogs, lest the **ritual energy** (法气) be unsettled.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **one *jì* of karmic reckoning** (罚算一纪).
Once a petition is completed, **documents bearing the name of the Most High** (太上名字) must not be left carelessly in secular homes. They must be burned by the **tenth month of the year**.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **one *jì* of karmic reckoning** (罚算一纪).
If a petition is submitted under the influence of alcohol, the penalty is **one thousand days of illness** (罚病一千日) and **five years of reduced lifespan** (减五年寿).

The Precepts state:
During **great winds or heavy rains**, petitions must not be submitted.
If there are **continuous winds or rains**, petitions must still not be submitted.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **one year of illness** (罚病一年).

The Precepts state:
Those with **six grave illnesses** (六疾) must not submit petitions on behalf of the common people.
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **three *jì* of karmic reckoning** (罚算三纪).

The Precepts state:
In cases of **unending familial calamities** (丧祸不绝) or **clearing cursed tombs** (解凶墓谪), wooden tablets (**木札**) may be submitted instead.

The Precepts state:
**Daoist female officials** submitting petitions must abstain from **alcohol, meat, and the five pungent spices** (五辛).
Violation of these precepts incurs a penalty of **one *jì* of karmic reckoning** (罚筹一纪).

If submitting petitions to **great star hosts** (大星宿), it must be done at **midnight**, with **five lamps**, **five-colored talismans**, and ink-written scriptures to **ward off and kill** (厌杀). The lamps must be extinguished only after their oil is fully consumed.
If the petition is **heard and acknowledged**, bow twice and descend to the **lowest rank** (下极), where it may be placed in the **next row for further review** (次行安以闻).
If a petition is **completed but minor matters arise**, it may not be submitted again for a year.
If the **fine details are not yet inscribed**, it may be resubmitted after a month.
The standard dimensions for petitions are:
- **Top section**: three inches and five *fēn* (分),
- **Middle section**: four inches and five *fēn*,
- **Bottom section**: five inches.
Exceeding these is forbidden, though some modern practitioners incorrectly add an extra inch and a half—this is a well-intentioned but unauthorized deviation from the law.

If a petition reaches the **Yearly Deity** (太岁) but the paper is insufficient, any remaining lines may be submitted. If there are **two lines remaining**, the entire sheet may be continued.
Errors in characters must be corrected by the **Heavenly Emperor’s full ritual** (天帝具仪).
Small petitions must not exceed **three characters**; larger petitions may be adjusted as needed.

When submitting a single petition, **four bows** may be made before and after reading it. Upon finishing, the **Yearly Deity must be given utmost reverence**—one must **calm the mind, maintain order, and uphold the law**.

The method for reading the **fine details** (细字) is as follows: kneel in **long prostration**, speak softly, and utter the words in one breath. The law forbids raising the case and reading aloud; the fine details must be recited in a single exhale.

If **inner officials** (内官) receive an **oral petition** (口章) according to court law, **outer officials** (外官) must not accept oral petitions.

**The *Wei Tradition*** states:
For **urgent matters**, petitions must be marked with **cinnabar ink** (朱笔).
If a **petition to expel ghosts** (逐鬼章) is not submitted, the name of the **Sacrificial Deity** (祭酒) must be written in **cinnabar**.
For **treating demonic illnesses** (治邪病), **blue paper** must be used, as the **Three Officials** (三官君吏) favor this color.
For **diseases caused by ghostly *qi*** (注气鬼病), compose a **Strike-Ghost Petition** (击鬼章) on **blue paper with cinnabar ink**.
After submission, place **two parts cinnabar and one part true cinnabar** (真朱二分) in a mortar, grind them, mix with honey to form pills, and ingest them immediately.
At dawn, enter the **Hall of Tranquility** (靖内), face north, bow twice, and take the pills. Even those on the verge of death shall be revived.
Ensure no one witnesses this. For other illnesses, compose a petition, burn incense, and write facing north.

If suffering from **severe illness**, burn incense on all four sides and place **four incense offerings** (四香火).

**Regarding petition brushes and inkstones:**
**The *Wei Tradition*** states:
When writing petitions, use **separate brushes and inkstones**; do not mix them.

Grind the inkstone, turning left forty-nine times, and remold it likewise.

Regarding the **inkstand**:
The *Xuandu Regulations* state:
When presenting petitions, one must use a **curved-leg inkstand**.
If not curved-leg, one may not present petitions.
Violation: Penalty of one *jì* of illness.

The inkstand for presenting petitions must be:
Length: 2 *chǐ* 4 *cùn*,
Width: 1 *chǐ* 2 *cùn*,
Height: 8 *cùn*,
With curved legs.
Violation: Illness penalty of one hundred days.

Regarding those writing **talismans**:
The *Xuandu Regulations* state:
Each method of issuing talismans has its own **incantation and command**.
Violation: Illness penalty of one hundred days.

The talisman-writing board must be:
Length: 1 *chǐ* 8 *cùn*,
With the upper 6 *cùn* reserved for the seal,
And the lower 1 *chǐ* 2 *cùn* for writing.
When preparing talisman incense, one must not use stove ash.
Violation: Illness penalty of ten days.

The *Sanhuang Jing* states:
The **Celestial Elder** asked:
"Why must talismans be made on the *wùxū* day?"
The **Three Sovereigns** replied:
"*Xū* is the **Heavenly Gate**; *wù* is **Earth**, the likeness of the Central Palace Sovereign."
The **Heavenly Emperor** often, on *wùxū* days,
Descends from the **Western-North Heavenly Gate** to wander and inspect.
When talismans are made on this day, the Heavenly Emperor takes delight,
Granting whatever is desired.
*Wù* is **Earth**, and one must surely attain **official rank and title, ennoblement, and fiefs**.
That is why it is worn at **noon**—noon is the essence of the **Sun** and the pure radiance of **refined gold**,
Ensuring one attains the likeness of **high rank in gold and purple**.

Regarding the **original storage of petitions**:
The *Taizhen Science* states:
After completing a petition for another,
And after all minor petitions have been burned in the furnace,
Roll them into the case and carry them out.
Then, separately, retrieve all the major petitions,
Taking them all at once and recording them as prescribed.

If what is to be burned, then relight the furnace before the table and burn it;
If elsewhere, return the petition with the one who submitted it.

At the head of the petition, mark the name of the petitioner,
Seal the original copy and keep it securely—
Do not let it be exposed to insects, rodents, or bartered for gain.
If violated, the **Supreme Sovereign’s decree** states:
The petition contains the true titles of officials, names of spirits and ghosts,
Sacred incantations of the **Numen**, all inscribed within—
Do not let them be stained or dishonored.

All petitions have an **original copy**—
Transcribe them carefully, verify them clearly,
And do not use them arbitrarily.

For **original records and statements**,
Do not submit them to officials for verification or alteration;
Common households must not retain original petition copies.
Violations shall be punished by the **Five Penalties**.

**The Ritual of Termination** (*Taizhen Science* states):
*"The petitioner solemnly examines the documents:
I, [Name], of rank [Title], follow the Dao in practice,
Propagate the **Dao-qi**, and petition for the summoning of **True Officials**
To save and protect the myriad people.

The petitions submitted—
Those to be burned, burn;
Those not to be burned, seal and store in chests.
When rolled and stacked in abundance,
The ritual forbids scattering them—
Lest insects, rodents, dampness, or decay cause loss,
We have always adhered with caution, never daring to defy the decree.

On this day, according to the **Science**, at the appointed time,
From the [Year] Month Day Hour to the present Year Month Day,
There are a total of **X** petitions.

Now, at the **Pure Altar of [Name]**, in a clean place,
We incinerate the petitions as smoke, ascending to clouds,
Descending **qi**, spreading blessings and dispelling calamities.
We humbly petition the **Directing Officer of the Orthodox Unity Bureau**,
The **Central Authority of the Tiger Guard**, and the **Awe-Inspiring Rites**,
With **Five Commanders**, **Two Wu-Bo**, **Twelve Officers**,
**Five Functionaries, Clerks, Junior Attendants, and Golden-Light Children**,
And **Two Supervisors from the Central Department, Postal Inspectors, and Envoys**,
To jointly oversee and verify,
Burning away the old and adopting the new.

For my own shortcomings and inadequacies,
I beg that the previously inscribed copies be forever recorded in the **Celestial Registry**,
And that future petitions be exempt from the **Cold Pool** [of punishment].

The officials shall attest, reward, and assist in merit—
According to the **Grand Register’s** record of deeds,
Without failing in sincerity—
The grace of the **Supreme Sovereign** is thus fulfilled."*

**Termination of the Petition**—
The total number varies.

In times of abundance or scarcity,
The ritual has phases of **active** and **hidden** practice—
When hidden, practice is minimal;
When active, count until full.
A hundred petitions constitute a **Termination**.

As in the previous text,
Each year by the **10th month**, the **Termination** is observed.

**Completion of the *Essential Rules for Ritual Conduct and Precepts*, Volume 11**
**Excerpt from the *Essential Rules for Ritual Conduct and Precepts*, Volume 12**

**Fasting the Worthy (Bian Xian Yuan) – First Chapter**

When the sacred teaching flourishes and the Dao’s winds prevail,
Worthy ones arise, and the sovereign’s virtue is exalted.
The principle of resonance being manifest,
The ritual of fasting the worthy is now revealed.

*The Taizhen Precepts* state:
When sickness or calamity befalls a household,
Public or private, a kitchen is established—
This is called fasting the worthy.
One may invite pure and worthy Daoists—
Upper, middle, or lower ranks—
Ten, twenty-four, thirty, fifty, or a hundred in number.
Never fewer than ten, lest the merit be incomplete.

The worthy, though frugal, may refuse food,
Or eat sparingly if they do.
They require only simple gruel and medicine,
Not lavish feasts—
For the world honors them as upholders of the Dao.

At this time, an altar must be erected.
Three days of purification precede,
Three days of merit-recitation follow.
The worthy, being divine within,
Are honored with abundance;
Their virtue demands fullness.
Food should suffice for satiety,
Flavor should suit moderation.
The offering must match the purity of an abstinence meal—
No meat or defilement is permitted.
Violators face five punishments.

During the guest month, three invitations suffice;
Names need not be enumerated.
Greedy or gluttonous guests must not be repeatedly summoned to the sacred kitchen.
The finer details of the ritual—
Exceeding ten folios—
Are rarely observed today,
So they are omitted here.

*The Xuandu Statutes* decree:
On auspicious triple assemblies,
Confronting celestial officials,
Teaching the ignorant and vulgar,
Disseminating merit and virtue,
If impurity mingles with human and ghostly resonance,
The calamity will fall upon future rulers.
The penalty: one *jì* of reckoning.

*The Statutes* further state:
For those of the Zhengyi sect ranked *Pingqi* or above,
One person’s merit counts as seven.
For mountain-dwelling Daoists,
One counts as three.
For those bearing talismans or holding military rank,
One counts as two.
For junior acolytes,
Two count as three.
For commoners,
One counts as one.

For sons born, the upper kitchen is used;
For daughters, the middle kitchen.
Increasing household members or wealth,
The lower kitchen suffices.

*The Statutes* decree:
When a Daoist hosts a kitchen for others,
They must select a person of great virtue and goodwill—
Never one of wickedness or disrespect,
Lest the merit be lost.
Violators face one *jì* of reckoning.

*The Statutes* decree:
When hosting a kitchen, guests must be seated uniformly,
All harboring the Supreme Sovereign’s benevolent intent.
No talk of slaughter, hunting, or fishing is permitted.
Violators—both host and guests—suffer three years of reckoning.

*The Statutes* decree:
If a Daoist hosts a kitchen,
Incense must be burned before guests—
No meat or defilement allowed.
Violators face a hundred days of reckoning.

---

**Constructing Temple Halls (Zao Dian Tang Yuan) – Second Chapter**

To establish righteousness,
One relies on compassion’s power,
Seeking proof of cause and effect,
Demanding faith as its foundation.
Merit manifests in prior causes,
And wondrous causes shine through future kalpas.

*The Taizhen Precepts* state:
If a layperson donates wealth to build
A single walled hall or refined chamber,
They are granted a small reckoning of 120.
For three halls, 360.
The more the merit, the greater the reckoning.

*The Great Precepts Sutra* declares:
To erect a *Jingguan* observatory,
Ensures noble lineage for generations,
Ascension to celestial halls,
Natural sustenance,
And eternal abiding in non-action.
Donating even a single coin yields
320,000-fold repayment;
A donation of ten thousand or more—
Its reward is boundless.

*The Benji Jing* recounts:
When the Great Brahmin King’s realm suffered drought,
Turning scriptures brought relief.
He then built a grand hall.

*The Benxiang Jing* recounts:
King Qinghe, who scorned Daoist law,
Built the *Xixian Guan* and the temples of *Xilings* and *Qizheng*.

*The Benji* records:
In the reign of Zhou King Kang,
The True Beginning Immortal wove grass into a pavilion,
Observing stars and celestial omens.
Upon attaining the Dao, the pavilion became legendary.
Later, Zhou King Mu, revering his legacy,
Renovated the halls, naming them *Louguan*,
And erected a temple in his honor.
In the thirty-first year of Qin Shi Huang’s reign,
A temple to the Venerable Lord was built to his south.

*The Benzhuan* records:
In the second year of Emperor Wu’s *Yuanfeng* era (January 1st, *jiāzǐ*),
He ascended Mount Song,
Entered the Great Yu Stone Chamber,
Established Daoist offices,
And commanded Dongfang Shuo and Dong Zhongshu to purify themselves in meditation.

---

**The Pondering of the Dao (Nian Dao Yuan) – Third Chapter**

The Dao is subtle, beyond measure,
Empty yet generative, boundless in use.
Five reflections shine in sacred ritual,
One mind unites with true essence.

*The Dao Canon* states:
Constantly ponder the Dao,
And the Dao will ponder you.
In tribulation, think of the Dao;
In sickness, think of the Dao;
In poverty or disgrace, think of the Dao;
In hardship or want, think of the Dao;
In eating and drinking, think of the Dao;
In traversing mountains and marshes, think of the Dao;
In crossing rivers, think of the Dao.
Ever in action, think of the Dao—
Then the Dao walks beside you.

Where the Dao emerges,
All things are born, all spirits fulfilled,
Nothing remains unnourished.
When the Dao is lost, even for an instant,
The body descends into the Eight Dark Realms.

*The Yinyuan Jing* declares:
Pondering the true heart never wanes,
Loyalty and sincerity are never forgotten.
Honoring the Dao’s worthies,
No hardship shall befall.
Moreover, honoring virtuous Daoists,
Abstinence reveals the True King.
Steadfast in contemplation,
Seven ancestors ascend to the Celestial Hall.

*The Miaozhen Jing* states:
The Daoist seeks life,
Yet does not crave fame.
Rags for robes, worn-out sandals,
No longing for honor.
The heart is pure as white,
The mind uncluttered.
The will flows like water,
The dwelling is empty as a city.
Guarding non-action,
One attains longevity.

The Dao is singular.
If one knows it, clarity shines like the sun;
If one does not, they remain buried in the earth.
The Dao takes nothing—
Righteous qi abides naturally.
The Dao departs from nothing—
Evil qi is expelled.
This is not the Dao of petitioning spirits and gods.

It can be held yet does not fill the hand;
Released, it spreads across the four seas.
Those who study life attain life;
Those who study the Dao attain the Dao.
Like one drowning who knows how to swim—
They live.
The ignorant drown.
The undiseased are easily healed;
The undying realm is easily governed.

「Those who do not embrace the Dao/Way have scattered and distinct thoughts.
The sparrow and quail fly high, yet their hearts dwell on the fields of grain;
The wild goose takes flight over marshes and pools, its will fixed on shallow waters.
The great crane and wild goose soar in the realm of **Tàiqīng** (太清), traversing the Nine Regions, resting at the Eight Extremes, and thus finding their true abode.
Though these two birds differ in joy and sorrow, their aspirations vary, yet each claims to have attained its own desire.

Thus the depths of great waters hold the divine dragon,
While small fish scurry to escape;
Deep mountains and dense marshes delight the tiger and leopard,
Yet repel the chicken and dog.
Therefore, rules differ, and the hearts of the people vary—
Hence, those who follow the Dao/Way
Diminish their sharpness of mind,
Abandon clever scheming,
Return to authenticity and simplicity,
Dwell in the realm of **Tàisù** (太素),
Hold light the world and scorn its entanglements,
Their radiance untainted,
Their joy and anger not stirred by external influences,
Their concerns for gain and harm not lodged in their thoughts—
This is the conduct of the Great Sage.

The *Lǎojūn Jìnjié Jīng* (《老君禁戒经》) states:
*"Accumulating virtue brings kingship,
Accumulating resentment brings ruin,
Piling stones forms mountains,
Gathering waters creates seas—
What is achieved without accumulation has never been seen.
Accumulate **dáodé** (道德), and Heaven grants it,
Earth assists it,
Ghosts and spirits aid it,
The **fèngniǎo** (凤鸟) alights in your courtyard,
The **qílín** (麒麟) and **lín** (鳞) roam your outskirts,
The divine dragon rests in your marshes.
Thus, if one governs the world with the Dao/Way,
They are the world’s virtue;
If one does not govern the world with the Dao/Way,
They are the world’s thief.
Yáo and Shùn flourished through having the Dao/Way,
Jiě and Jié perished through lacking it."*

**Section on Avoiding Defilement (Fourth Chapter)**
The **shénqì** (神气) is pure and void,
Guarded by divine spirits;
The body and mind are turbid and impure,
Inviting harm from malevolent forces.
To enter stillness and ponder the True,
One must first prevent defilement—
Not treading upon evils,
Then blessings will naturally reside.

The *Xuāndū Lǜ* (《玄都律》) states:
*"If households are defiled and unclean,
They shall not exceed the duration of **huìzuò** (晦朔)—
Only then may they enter **jìngzhì** (靖治) to perform rites, offerings, or submit petitions.
Weeping for three days brings defilement.
During the three-year mourning period,
Before the hundredth day has passed,
They shall not enter **jìngzhì** to perform rites, offerings, or submit petitions.
Violating this law incurs a penalty of **suàn** (算) for one **jì** (纪).*
It further states:
*"Upon encountering the great mourning of a teacher, master, or parents,
Defilement lasts thirty days—
They shall not fast or offer petitions.
Once the thirty days have passed,
And the outer mourning period concludes,
They must bathe, burn incense, and purify themselves.
Violating this law incurs a penalty of **suàn** for two **jì** (纪)."*

The law states:
*"Officers of the **Tàiyī Jífǎ** (太一极法) Daoists,
Whether male or female,
Shall not be defiled by mourning—
Even weeping shall not bring defilement.
They must wear their **gē** (箓) talismans on their persons,
Not removing or passing them to others."*

The law states:
*"If Daoist officers, male or female,
Are imprisoned or detained by secular authorities,
They must first purify themselves with fragrant baths.
After three days of defilement have passed,
They may enter **jìngzhì** to perform rites or submit petitions.
Violating this law incurs a penalty of **suàn** for one **jì** (纪).*

*If Daoists or female officers
Suffer private secular punishment,
And their wounds are not yet healed,
Before thirty days have passed,
They shall not enter **jìngzhì** to perform rites or submit petitions.
Violating this law incurs a penalty of **kǎo** (考) twenty."*

The law states:
*"Those who wear the **gē** (箓) talismans
Shall not enter defiled spaces—
If they do, they face no restrictions.
If they tread upon unclean **qì** (气), their penalty comes from the **Tàiqīng Cáo** (太清曹).
If they do not, their penalty comes from the **Qīngtiān Cáo** (清天曹)."*

The *Sānyuán Pǐndié* (《三元品戒》) states:
*"On the fifteenth days of the first, seventh, and tenth months,
At dawn, noon, and midnight,
One must bathe the body
And purify with the **wǔxiāng** (五香) five fragrant substances.
At the moment of bathing,
Facing south, use a golden ladle
To stir the fragrant water in a circular motion,
Turning counterclockwise thirty-two times in the southeast.
Close the eyes and meditate on the sun’s light in the left eye,
The moon’s light in the right eye,
The **wǔxīng** (五星) Five Stars encircling the head,
The **wǔsè yún** (五色之云) five-colored clouds
Enveloping the body,
The **Qīnglóng** (青龙) Azure Dragon, **Báihǔ** (白虎) White Tiger, **Zhūquè** (朱雀) Vermilion Bird, **Xuánwǔ** (玄武) Dark Warrior, **Shīzǐ** (狮子) Lion, and **Báihè** (白鹤) White Crane
Arrayed on either side,
Fairy attendants holding towels,
Celestial maidens scattering flowers,
Flying immortals riding steeds,
Guarding and attending the form.
Then strike the teeth thirty-two times,
And recite the invocation:
*"Heaven is clear, the **qì** (气) is pure,
The Five Colors radiant and bright."*

The sun and moon emit their radiance,
Irrigating my body and form.
Within the divine pool, I bathe,
With fragrant waters refining my essence,
Illuminating all with radiant splendor,
Shining upon the **Upper Purity** (上清),
My **qi** (气) untainted by dust,
The Five **Palaces** (府) receiving their spirits.
Sins vanish from the Three **Tus** (徒),
Calamities disperse from the Nine **Mings** (冥),
Evil roots severed and cut,
Bliss and joy naturally arise.
Today’s grand vow:
All things now made clear,
My body receiving liberation,
Ascending into the Imperial Court.

Finished, I then draw in **qi** (气) thirty-two times,
And wash with the five fragrant essences.
After bathing, I don a crown and sash,
And change into my garments.
Again, I strike the teeth twelve times,
And recite the invocation:
*"The Five Impurities now purified,
The Eight **Scenes** (景) now illuminated,
Today I undergo refinement,
Sins vanish, blessings arise.
Long may I align with the Five **Emperors** (帝),
Equal to the **True Ones** (真) of the highest **Ling** (灵),
Then depart and enter the chamber,
Conducting the **Dao** (道) according to the law."*

The *Natural Precepts, Lower Section* (《自然诀下》) states:
*"If the scriptures are defiled,
And one does not bathe,
First, it invites many diseases and calamities,
Second, it shows the people the distinction between purity and impurity,
Third, the spirits and **demons** (鬼) will not aid in communion,
Fourth, the **True Officials** (真官) of the scriptures will charge one with guilt,
Fifth, others seeing it will not show reverence."*

The *Three Sovereigns Scripture* (《三皇经》) declares:
*"When I purify myself, I recite:
By the sun, I cleanse my body,
By the moon, I refine my essence,
The **Fairy Ones** (仙人) assist me,
The **Jade Maidens** (玉女) aid my form,
The Twenty-Eight **Lunar Lodges** (宿) unite with me,
A thousand deceits and impurities are swept away by the water.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the **Precepts** (律令) command."*

The *Laozi’s Scripture on Nourishing Life* (《老君养生经》) states:
*"On the **waning day** (晦日), bathing is auspicious,
On the **new moon** (朔日), bathing is auspicious."*

The *Thousand True Precepts* (《千真科》) prescribe:
*"In winter, bathing must occur every **decade** (旬).
First, prepare a secluded chamber,
Six feet square,
With a water trough, fire stove, and bamboo pipe,
To pour the hot water in.
Into the water, add **peach twigs** (桃枝), **bamboo leaves** (栢叶), **orchid** (兰), and **bamboo leaves** (竹叶),
Boil and take three **liang** (两),
Once it boils, remove the dregs,
Then add the five fragrant essences,
And filter the water through a cloth strainer.
The high and low must bathe in order,
Not sharing with the vulgar masses,
All must wear bathing garments,
Or else it violates the **Precepts** (律)."*

**Section on Theft and Robbery** (贼缘第五)
*"Those who leave the secular world
Must cultivate upright thoughts and sincere hearts,
Facing the **True One** (真) each morning,
And thus safeguarding body, speech, and mind.
If the heart moves with even a trace of greed,
It is as if one sinks into **endless kalpas** (万劫),
How much more so if one habitually steals?
One will forever lose the **Dao** (道) of humanity."*

The *Precepts of the Mystic Capital* (《玄都律》) decree:
*"Theft of scriptures, offerings, or anything of value—
Even a single **file** (文) or more—
Will be met with severe retribution.
If the stolen goods exceed a **file** (文),
Five **cun** (疋) of punishment for each **file**,
And one **Palace** (府) of the household will perish.
If the stolen goods are less than a **file** (文),
Seven thousand days of **karmic illness** (病),
And twelve years of life will be forfeited.
Theft of **talismans** (符), **arrow-writing** (箓), official seals, or contracts—
All will be met with retribution.
If one finds them outside and does not claim them,
It is not permitted.
Theft of **Heavenly Officials’** (天官) taxed rice—
Five **dou** (斗) or more—
Guilt enters retribution.
One **hu** (斛) or more—
Guilt enters criminal punishment.
If the theft is not reported,
Seven thousand days of **karmic illness** (病),
And twelve years of life will be forfeited.
Robbery—
Taking even a single **file** (文) of another’s possessions—
