Guilt enters criminal punishment,
And one thousand days of **karmic illness** (病) or death.
Repayment for stolen goods:
For each **cun** (疋) stolen, repay ten **cun** (疋),
And robbers will not be allowed to enter the **Dao** (道),
Their **karmic guilt** (赃) collected like **demonic spoils** (鬼赃),
Ten **cun** (疋) collected, two **cun** (疋) repaid.

The **Precepts** (律) say:
*"No sin is greater than robbery.
Forcibly taking, forcibly borrowing, forcibly buying—
All are theft.
Taking without the **Dao** (道) is judged as theft.
The **Precepts** (律) say:
If one borrows but does not return the principal,
Or if the lender does not repay the borrower,
Both the principal and the lender are guilty of theft,
And shall be charged with the corresponding crimes.
If one borrows but does not return the principal,
They will be subjected to **karmic illness** (病) under the **Superintendent of the Storehouse** (监仓令).
If one borrows and does not repay the lender,
They will be subjected to **karmic illness** (病) under this **Precept** (律).
When guilt is full, it becomes **fierce** (凶),
And when **fierce** (凶), it shall be sentenced to death."*

The **Precepts** (律) say:
*"Theft of a single **scroll** (卷) of scriptures—
One thousand days of **karmic illness** (病),
And seven years of life forfeited;
Theft of a single **scroll** (卷) or more from the **Heavenly Officials’ Secret Archives** (天官秘书)—
Guilt enters criminal punishment,
And the **Precepts** (律) will prescribe death.
Theft of clothing, utensils, knives, axes, or finished goods—
All incur double the punishment,
And destruction of the **karmic guilt** (罪) is one level reduced.
For those who incite theft or speak of it,
They will be subjected to **karmic illness** (病) under the **Superintendent of the Storehouse** (监仓令).
Theft of an **incense burner** (香炉)—
Retribution is death,
And the thief’s guilt enters criminal punishment.
Theft of a **scripture knife** (书刀)—
Twenty years of life forfeited,
And two thousand days of **karmic illness** (病);
Theft of a **case** (函)—
Ten years of life forfeited,
And one thousand days of **karmic illness** (病);
Theft of **abacus beads** (算)—
Five years of life forfeited,
And one hundred days of **karmic illness** (病);
Theft of **ink** (墨)—
Three years of life forfeited,
And three hundred days of **karmic illness** (病);
Theft of **paper** (纸)—
Two years of life forfeited,
And one hundred days of **karmic illness** (病);
Theft of food utensils, cups, bowls, **incense censers** (昙缶), or miscellaneous items—
Twelve years of life forfeited,
And two thousand days of **karmic illness** (病);
Theft of **boats or carriages** (船车)—
Guilt enters criminal punishment, as prescribed by the **Precepts** (律)."*

The *Scripture on the Original Form* (《本相经》) states:
*"Wealth gathered invites **misfortune** (祸),
Money amassed invites **thieves** (盗).
Thus, the **Dao-heart** (道心) must be:
Diligent in the **Dao** (道), not in wealth,
Cultivating **virtue** (德), not in silk.
It further says:
Thieves are the worst of mankind,
Greedy for stolen goods.
They lurk day and night,
Waiting for opportunities to strike,
Plundering what others love,
And hoarding it for themselves.
If their spoils are exposed to the **King’s Law** (王法),
Their souls will descend into the **Hell of Earth** (地狱).
The **Sand-Demons** (抱沙鬼) of the sea,
Iron needles without rest.
To behold them causes sorrow,
Yet they are not learned from—
Their **karmic guilt** (罪) is not sealed.
The **lustful thief** (淫贼), though guilty of **lewdness** (淫),
Still competes to cultivate **blessings and virtue** (福德).
When the **Dao** (道) descends into the human body,
Joy and ease are ever present.
It further says:
If a **Daoist** (道士) steals,
Their **guilt** (罪) will not be pardoned—
**Daoists** must uphold the **Law** (法),
Not indulging in **crookedness** (倾邪).
Wearing the **Supreme Contract** (无上契) of their master,
They must not be extravagant in their thoughts.
Even if they give alms, they must not take,
How much more so if they become thieves!
They will suffer **mutilation** (剕刖) and **body punishment** (受身刑),
And be bound in the **Northern Torture Hall** (北酆枷).
Their ancestral shrines will not be established,
And their **karmic retribution** (罪) will extend to seven generations."*

The *Scripture Admonishing the World* (《劝世经》) declares:
*"Robbery harms body, speech, and mind,
Swallowing the blade into the belly’s depths.
It brings **decay and ruin** (衰穷),
And **shriveling** (申缩) cannot restore **prosperity** (泰).
Whether moving or still,
One’s life is extinguished,
And bones lie in filth.
Ultimately, one will face **retribution** (殃考),
And their lineage will be utterly severed,
Leaving no descendants."*

**On the Mind of the Unknowing Child**
Why not cultivate the Dao of virtue,
And strive to build meritorious deeds?
Merits and faults balance each other—
Extending years through calamitous times.
Accumulate good and gather blessings,
Accumulate evil and invite retribution.
Yet within a single lifetime,
Why bring shame upon oneself?

*The Laws of the Mystic Capital* (*玄都律*) decree:
*"To harm or kill another—
The case is referred to the Magistrate of Northern Peace."*

*The Scripture of Ascension to the Mystic* (*升玄经*) states:
*"If one kills before encountering the Dharma,
Or slays with their own hands,
They must redeem it by saving a dying person.
Once the guilt is purged,
They also earn the merit of saving a life."*

*The Laws of the Mystic Capital* (*玄都律*) further decree:
*"Quarrels over fields and homes, violent disputes—
The case is referred to the Magistrate of Equitable Qi."*

**The Sixth Cause: Transgressions of the Sixth Degree**
To cultivate oneself, one must first avoid fault.
Greed and wrath arise from the Six Desires,
Transgressions from the Five Emotions—
Their errors manifest in action.

*The Laws of the Mystic Capital* (*玄都律*) declare:
*"Within the human body,
A spirit constantly ascends, reporting one’s virtues and vices to Heaven.
When transgressions reach one hundred twenty,
They bring illness—
Illness brings more misfortune than fortune.
At one hundred eighty transgressions—*a depletion*—
Livestock will not thrive.
At one hundred ninety—*a leak*—
Good fortune brings sickness.
At five hundred thirty—*a minor calamity*—
Miscarriages and child harm.
At seven hundred twenty—*a major calamity*—
Few sons, many daughters.
At eight hundred twenty-nine—*a retribution*—
Sickness, muteness, blindness, deafness.
At one thousand eighty—*a disaster*—
Sudden, untimely death.
At one thousand two hundred—*a ruin*—
Rebellious, lawless offspring.
At one thousand two hundred sixty—*a fault*—
No descendants, severed lineage.
At one thousand four hundred—*a blockage*—
Retribution extends to five generations.
At one thousand six hundred twenty—*an exile*—
No posterity remains.
At one thousand eight hundred—*a calamity*—
Slavehood, domestic chaos.
At one thousand nine hundred eighty—*a tyranny*—
Madness, epilepsy, insanity in the household.
At two thousand six hundred—*a violence*—
Death by blade or treachery.
At two thousand three hundred forty—*a void*—
Parental and sibling strife, mutual destruction.
At two thousand five hundred twenty—*an excess*—
Death by famine, evil sickness.
At two thousand seven hundred—*a harm*—
Deafness, witchcraft, spectral illness.
At two thousand eight hundred—*a calamity*—
Incestuous lust among kin.
At three thousand sixty—*a violence*—
Blindness, leprosy, mutilation.
At three thousand two hundred forty—*a mutation*—
Legal execution, clan annihilation.
At three thousand four hundred twenty—*a monstrosity*—
Begging in the marketplace; after death, the corpse is discarded.
At three thousand six hundred—*a sickness*—
Fulfilling the sentence of certain death."

*The Scripture of Marvelous Truth* (*妙真经*) proclaims:
*"No sin is greater than lust,
No disaster greater than greed,
No fault greater than miserliness—
These three are the chariot of calamity.
The small bring peril to the body,
The great destroy the family."*

In this world, there are three noble riches:
No guilt surpasses nobility,
No joy surpasses peace,
No wealth surpasses contentment.
Contentment is true sufficiency—
Heaven’s grace bestowed.
Ignorance of restraint brings harm to oneself.
To lose it brings sorrow,
To gain it brings joy—
Yet those who barricade their gates
Will surely face the undoing of their defenses.
Death and dishonor descend upon descendants,
Serving Heaven with virtue,
Not arrogance toward others.

**The Seventh Cause: Meritorious Deeds**
If the heart is coarse and wild,
Worldly habits remain unbroken;
If nature is gentle and yielding,
One must know the highest virtue—like water.
When evil ceases,
Good deeds naturally arise.

*The Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* (*洞神经*) declares:
*"The Heavenly Elder honors a hundred virtues."*

If a person has ten good deeds,
They will bear fortunate children.
If twenty,
Divine protection guards them.
If thirty,
Evil spirits are repelled.
If forty,
Death is averted.
If fifty,
Guilt is erased for life.
If sixty,
The Daoist Sovereign preserves them.
If seventy,
They connect with the Five Sacred Peaks.
If eighty,
They escape the name of death.
If ninety,
They must become celestial messengers.
If a hundred,
They ascend to the Nine Heavens.

*The Scripture of the Original Vow* (*本愿经*) states:
*"To learn the Dao of Ascension,
One must establish one thousand two hundred meritorious deeds.
With three thousand deeds fulfilled,
They ascend in daylight,
Saving those doomed to die."*

*The Record of Lists* (*列记*) teaches:
*"Those who study the Dao and cultivate practice
Must widely cultivate hidden virtues,
Show mercy to all beings,
Rescue those in peril,
Deliver those in distress,
Value the Dao over wealth,
Bestow kindness and virtue without stint,
Not sparing treasure to aid the destitute,
Invoking true qi with solemn oaths,
Bowing humbly in reverence."*

The True Person of the Great Void declares:
*"Feeding a hundred common folk
Is not as meritorious as feeding one virtuous person;
Feeding a thousand virtuous persons
Is not as meritorious as feeding one Daoist practitioner."*

*The Family Orders of the Laozi* (*老君家令经*) states:
*"A Daoist’s hundred practices
Must encompass a thousand virtues.
Though nine hundred ninety-nine virtues are fulfilled,
One unfulfilled virtue—
If moved by self-interest—
All prior merits are lost.
Only by guarding the body and mind,
Upholding precepts without fail,
Can one attain salvation for the world."*

*The Supreme Lord’s Edicts* (*太上科令*) command:
*"Teaching three to amend their faults—
This is one merit.
Persuading three households to reform—
This is one merit.
Assisting three destitute, orphaned, or widowed—
This is also one merit."*

「Promote and protect wealth and goods,
Yet harbor no resentment when gains are not contested—
Fulfilling this threefold act also counts as one merit.

Grieve over guilt and wrongdoing,
Heal and cure three afflicted souls—
This too is counted as one merit.

All such acts as these,
Seek them by their kindred nature.

*The Scripture of the Original Form* (*本相经*) states:
*"When merits reach ten thousand,
One ascends to the boundless void.
Those who recite the scriptures,
Each character as one merit—
When three thousand are fulfilled,
Their names are inscribed in the *Upper Purity Register* (*上清*).

If one can establish Daoist halls, altars, scripture chambers, fasting rooms, and kitchens,
And provide for Daoist practitioners—
Clothing, bedding, and all necessities given freely—
Such merits earn celestial rewards:
Food and garments come naturally,
As needed, without summoning;
When unused, they vanish.

If one is wealthy at home,
Yet further cultivates blessings and constructs virtuous deeds,
That person shall be recorded by the *Bright Register* (*明受记*) and attain Dao.

Even the most foolish and deluded
Shall have a time of attaining Dao.
Just as infants grow into elders,
So too shall those who persist in cultivating virtue
Sufficiently attain Dao.

*The Scripture of Great Peace* (*太平经*) declares:
*"Evil persons entering the Dao
Undermine the merits of the virtuous—
Like clumsy artisans ruining fine materials,
Or incompetent women spoiling silk and cloth,
They shall never achieve true merit.

Yet when evil persons oppose the virtuous,
It is like a sick man being offered fine food—
He refuses, for it is not to his liking,
And starves to death from eating only bitter fare.
So too, when evil persons hear virtuous teachings,
They recoil as if offered poison,
And cling ever more firmly to their wickedness.

Virtuous persons rejoice when they see virtue,
The worthy rejoice when they see the worthy,
The wise rejoice when they see wisdom,
Evil persons rejoice when they see evil,
And deceitful persons rejoice when they see deceit—
Each finds delight in their own kind.

If sons cannot exert themselves in serving their parents,
Or disciples cannot exert themselves in honoring their teachers,
Or subjects cannot exert themselves in obeying their rulers,
These three acts, though performed,
Shall not be counted as merit—
Their guilt cannot be absolved."

*The Scripture of Causes and Conditions* (*因缘经*) proclaims:
*"Aiding the destitute and rescuing those in peril—
The merit is vast and boundless.
Extending life and increasing longevity,
One shall enjoy eternal prosperity throughout their years."

It further states:
*"Accumulating virtue knows no limit;
Disseminating kindness should not be stingy.
Merit and virtue move the Immortal and True—
Their names shall naturally be recorded in the Celestial Registers."

*The Scripture of the Wondrous True* (*妙真经*) declares:
*"Those who do not cultivate virtue
Do not recognize the Primordial Sovereign,
Nor behold the Root of All—
They blaspheme Heaven, scorn Earth,
Deceive ghosts, and mock the spirits.
Their words are false, their intentions deceitful,
They harbor grudges and sow doubt—
Such are the unvirtuous.

The unvirtuous, in action, oppose Heaven,
In stillness, defy Earth.
Their speech harms living beings,
Their silence betrays the dead.
Thus they divide the Dao and sever virtue,
Scatter simplicity and dilute purity.
They twist words and manipulate meaning,
Cling to pretense while feigning benevolence.
Their potions and talismans bear no efficacy,
Their rituals rely on false celestial calculations.
They abandon truth for deceit,
Seeking only to topple the state.
They open paths of calamity,
Shut doors of loyalty and rectitude,
And curry favor with rulers
To maintain the nation’s favor—
Such are the schemers."

*The Scripture of Ascending Mystery* (*升玄经*) states:
*"Cultivating virtue yields virtue—
Even one’s spirits become virtuous.
Committing evil yields evil—
Even one’s spirits become evil.
Thus, half a person dwells in our Daoist halls,
Half in the demonic hells.
Their responses echo like a call—
None remain unanswered.

The Eighth Cause of Ascending to the Dao:
When one has cast off all afflictions,
Their secular attachments shall also fade.
They abandon familial affection to embrace the Dao,
Break free from worldly bonds to attain the True.
They transcend the Eightfold Path as their guiding principle,
And abandon the Tenfold Cycle to align their conduct."

*The Scripture of the Original Form* (*本相经*) further declares:
*"The Great Brahman King,
In his own heart, spoke thus:
*'My realm, with its Three Treasures’ power,
Should be revered and offered in gratitude to the Heavenly Sovereign above.*

Thus he selected his royal sons,
And the children of his ministers and subjects,
Choosing those of noble bearing,
First-rate intelligence,
And virtuous hearts—
All were made to leave home,
To uphold and propagate the True Law."

*The Scripture of the Original Form* (*本相经*) also states:
*"The King of Pure Harmony,
Issued an edict to ordain three thousand five hundred men and women of his realm,
Commanding the men to dwell in the *Habitual Spirits Hall* (*习灵庙*),
And the women in the *Seven Governors Hall* (*七政庙*),
To practice the Dao for the nation."

*The Original Record of the Tower Observation* (*楼观本记*) recounts:
*"King Mu of Zhou revered the Immortals,
And thus, through the guidance of Master Yin,
Constructed the Tower Observation Daoist retreat.
He then selected the recluse, You, and appointed him as a Daoist,
Setting him as a model of moral conduct for the people,
And ordering him to cultivate and expand the Dao’s teachings."

*The Scripture of the Original Form* (*本相经*) further relates:
*"The Model, Master Zi,
Together with four others,
Retreated into the mountains of Great Yuan to cultivate the Dao.
After thirty-six years,
He dreamed of the Immortal and True Daoists,
Their necks bearing luminous halos,
Countless and beyond reckoning.
After six more years,
He remained without any trace of worldly attachment,
While the four others returned home.
Master Zi wished to stay in the mountains.
The four doubted his attainment of the Dao,
And went to investigate—
Only to see the *Great Purity Jade Stele* (*太清玉碑*) inscribed with their names,
And two white cranes descending upon them,
Which died at the halfway point,
Transforming into *Yōuyǔ* birds (*犹预鸟*).
Three lifetimes later,
They were reborn in the Two-Faced Kingdom of the Western Lands,
With human form but lacking human sentiment."

It also states:
*"The King of Flaming Brilliance had a daughter,
Named Haoqiu,
Who at fifteen vowed to leave home.
She prayed to be reborn as a man,
And thus, through the Heavenly Sovereign’s radiant light,
Her female form ascended to the void—
In broad daylight, she ascended to Heaven.
After her departure,
The grieving king constructed
The Immortal Daoist Palace,
The Gathering of Spirits Platform,
Four surrounding halls,
And Three Teachers’ Chamber.
He further issued decrees throughout the land,
Urging all to leave home."

*The Thousand True Edicts* (*千真科*) decree:
*"How shall boys and girls,
Following the scriptures and precepts,
Be ordained by the king’s law?
What rites shall they perform to attain ordination,
And how shall they properly honor their parents thereafter?"

The response states:
*"To uphold and propagate the Dao’s lineage,
One must respectfully select those entering the Dao—
Choosing the noble, compassionate,
And those with Daoist hearts.
The teacher shall first instruct them in precepts and cultivation,
And after ten years of discipline,
They may be permitted to recite and study.

When the king ordains them,
They shall follow the king’s established rites and institutions.
They shall reside in the grand Daoist retreat,
Maintain strict order in the Mysterious Altar,
And construct the *Anran Pavilion* (*安阑纂*).

Following the method of *Bright Truth and Expiation* (*明真拔罪*),
They shall ordain men and women in advance.
At the altar’s southern face,
They shall stand in two rows—
Left and right—
And be ordained as they stand."

The response states:

*"When the officials stand in the southern row and the Daoist master in the horizontal row,
The Daoist master shall set a table before the horizontal row,
And recite the incense-offering hymn:
‘Great Sage, honored by heaven and humanity,
Revered through all ages!
Now we have a precious and noble one—
The great king of our realm.
Out of compassionate intent,
He universally commands entry into the True Dao.
Having entered the True Dao,
They owe it all to the king’s boundless virtue.
Forever free from worldly attachments,
They seek the sacred realm.
They shall surely gain the Dao’s blessings,
And together pursue the path of birthless enlightenment.’

After the hymn is finished,
The master declares to the newly ordained:
‘From this day onward,
You shall honor the True Sage and the True Dao,
Sever ties with kin and the secular world,
Each performing three bows,
And taking leave of the common life.
The first bow is to the king’s imperial virtue—
Endless as the heavens’ grace.
The second bow is to the county officials’ merit of liberation.
The third bow is to your living or deceased parents,
Who have granted you permission to leave the secular world.’

After completing the three bows,
The master seizes the first newly ordained by their clothing and crown,
And proclaims:
‘Great is the sacred transformation—
Its blessings extend infinitely,
The stars as crown,
The sun and moon as robes,
The Daoist path aligning with heaven’s way,
Unchanging through the four seasons,
Widely liberating all beings,
Forever transcending the three realms.’

The master commands the assembly to universally chant ‘Goodness!’
And strike the palms three times for expiation.
The former initiates also chant ‘Goodness!’
And strike the palms.
When all have completed three strikes,
They are collectively dressed in the Daoist robes.

The ceremony concludes,
And the officials present incense,
Each walking three times around the Daoist retreat.
The former initiates lead the way,
Then ascend the altar and recite the hymn of completion.
After the rites are finished,
A vegetarian feast is set.

When the feast is concluded,
Each thanks the Daoist disciples.
From the eldest to the youngest,
They sit in order before their parents and siblings,
Who have come to pay respects at their side.
Parents and siblings all address them as ‘disciple,’
And vow:
‘May the teacher surely attain enlightenment,
And join us, the disciples,
In entering the True Dao!’

Someone asks:
‘Among those who leave the secular life,
From young to old,
What are their ranks?’

The response states:
‘Among those who leave the secular life,
There are five ranks:
From seven to eleven years—*Puchē Daoist* (蒲车道士);
From twelve to fourteen—*Qīngxìn Daoist* (清信道士);
From fifteen to nineteen—*Shīhuì Daoist* (施惠道士);
From twenty to sixty—*Hónghù Daoist* (弘护道士);
From seventy to ninety—*Zhùchí Daoist* (住持道士).’

The text asks:
‘What is the guiding principle of the *Three Vehicles*?’

The response states:
‘The principle of the *Small Vehicle* is:
To dwell in seclusion among mountains and forests,
And to cultivate oneself for self-liberation.

The principle of the *Middle Vehicle* is:
To extend virtue universally,
And to aid and liberate all beings.

The principle of the *Great Vehicle* is:
To abandon merit and sever selfishness,
And to take the *Four Great Vows* of boundless compassion.

The text asks:
‘What merit does one gain from persuading others to leave the secular life?’

The response states:
‘To persuade others—men and women alike—
And even to give up one’s own children to leave the secular life,
Is like the merit of a world as numerous as dust grains—
Yet it still cannot compare to the merit of persuading others
To give up their children and leave the secular life.

Even if one constructs banners and pavilions
To reach the *Three Pure Ones’* realm,
The merit is still not as great as persuading others
To leave the secular life.

---
**End of the Twelve Precepts of Rituals and Ordinances**
**End of the Thirteen Precepts of Rituals and Ordinances***"

To establish rules and laws,
It is essential to rely on those capable of enforcing them.
Among the assembly, those ignorant of the Dao/Way—
No matter how many there are—
Must not be permitted to dwell together.

Those who dwell together must uniformly follow the sacred teachings,
Conduct themselves in accordance with ritual propriety in all actions,
Sever all evil with resolute intent,
And collectively safeguard all virtue.

For those who exhort evil-doers,
Their matters are addressed in other precepts.

**Precept:** The Dao/Way is pure and empty,
Seeking neither fame nor gain—
This is called the "family of the transcendent."
Yet among my disciples,
Many hoard money, treasures, cattle, slaves,
And cling to them without end.
Such persons sever the root of the *Three Treasures*,
Strip the blessings of all beings—
Though they may recite scriptures and uphold precepts,
They are all destroyers of the Dao/Way.

**Precept:** Those of great virtue/power,
Who preside over the assembly,
Must avoid even minor suspicion when those below err.
If any do not harmonize with the king,
Queens, attendants, ministers, officials, commoners,
Or with sons and daughters, junior Daoists, or the *Pure Ones*,
Or bear grudges from past or present disputes,
They must not be openly rebuked.
If punishment is warranted,
Summon them secretly first,
And speak privately.
If their transgressions are unbearable,
And they are hated by the assembly,
Then the matter must be presented to the assembly for judgment.

**Precept:** Those who have left the secular life
Must strive for simplicity and tranquility.
Unlawful conduct in action
Leads inevitably to heresy.

Unlawful conduct includes:
1. Extravagantly seeking wealth and provisions,
And boasting of one’s own abilities;
2. Greedily accumulating boundless riches,
And acting as matchmakers or fortune-tellers;
3. Forcefully claiming vast knowledge,
And gazing at celestial omens;
4. Associating with the *Pure Ones*,
And personally engaging in plowing, harvesting, or reaping;
5. Stirring discord among fellow Daoists,
And consorting with wicked friends;
6. Not taking the true Dharma/Way as one’s concern,
But allying with violent commoners;
7. Sitting or rising without distinction,
And confusing the ranks of the Dao/Way;
8. Not adhering to the proper precepts,
And sharing beds with the secular;
9. Venturing forth at night
Without holding a torch to light one’s own path;
10. Gambling with dice or *double-six*,
Engaging in robbery or other crimes,
Acting without restraint,
And failing to self-correct.

Those who enter the Dao/Way and follow the assembly
May remove such conduct.
If they do not self-punish,
They undermine the Dao/Way’s precepts.

**Precept:** All junior Daoists who visit eminent masters
Must refine their appearance and bearing,
Adjust their headgear and footwear,
Walk with measured dignity,
And bow three times with their foreheads touching the ground.
After bowing, kneel respectfully and say:
*"I, [name], am your humble disciple.
Though unworthy of the Dao/Way’s teachings,
I have come from afar.
I pray that the great master
Will graciously instruct and bind me.
Whatever I may hear,
I will never dare to disobey."*

The great master then addresses the assembly:
*"Now, Daoist [name],
From birth until today,
Has committed acts of anger and wrath,
Acts of robbery and theft,
Acts of greed and all manner of unvirtuous deeds.
Today, he bows in repentance,
And vows not to repeat his offenses.
He will now study the correct precepts,
And penetrate the profound principles of the Dao/Way.
After his confession,
He must rise only in accordance with what has been said,
And bow three times more before departing."*

**Precept:** Those who disturb the assembly
Often do not follow the true Dao/Way.
If they drink wine and act in disorder,
Or belittle those above and below,
They are fined in money or grain.
If they possess other goods or wealth,
And initially agree to contribute,
But later refuse or obstruct,
They are punished with rods.
If they seize property or cloth
To provide for the assembly,
Or if they subject others to harsh labor—
Cutting grass, felling trees, plowing fields, or reaping crops—
And the entire assembly cannot endure it,
The punishment is levied collectively.
If the Daoist assembly cannot resolve it,
They may be handed over to the king
To be judged by secular law.

**Precept:** If any do not follow the true Dao/Way,
And wander into other observatories,
Acting with arrogance or disrespect,
They must repay with wine and meat;
Or if they act as mediators in marriages,
Or purchase slaves for others,
Or other livestock and goods;
Or if they fabricate laws to suit the secular,
And are imprisoned for crimes,
Yet pardoned and released;
Or if they bribe officials
To escape punishment;
Or if they take stolen goods
And seek reconciliation through profit,
They must be charged according to the proper precepts
And punished as the law dictates.

**Precept:** Daoist male and female officials
Must each guard against disorderly conduct.
Daoists must not keep women,
Female officials must not keep men—
Each must maintain separation,
Cultivate purity of mind,
See no desirable form,
Hear no tempting sound.
If such temptations arise,
They must immediately report to the assembly.
If the assembly does not restrain them,
The king’s law will apply.

**Precept:** The private treasuries of great observatories
Are often in chaos,
Due to the eminent ones
Who fail to exercise caution,
Acting without restraint;
Or because the rules are not strictly enforced,
And those in charge occupy sacred lands
With impure and greedy hearts,
Luring junior disciples
To open wicked paths together,
Nurturing cruelty and evil,
Blocking the Dao/Way’s source,
Leaving true believers
With no foundation for their faith.

**Precept:** Those who enter the sacred treasury
Must open paths of virtue;
Yet harbor anger and strike;
All betray the Great Compassion.

Keeping livestock—cows, horses, dogs, or cats—without restraint, nurturing only the intent to harm, violates the precepts of purity. Such practices are forbidden to those who uphold the precepts.

**Precept:** There are ranks among people and degrees in the precepts. Some may outwardly observe the precepts yet inwardly lack sincerity, failing to cultivate stillness and retreat. Instead, they adorn halls and temples, gathering wicked companions and acting unlawfully. When the temple bell tolls for worship, they laugh and enter the assembly; when they see the virtuous conduct of the worthy, they slander them externally. This stems from their own lax discipline—how can they then unite the assembly and uphold the Dao/Way, letting righteous teachings flourish daily?

**Precept:** If one within the assembly acts unvirtuously, they should be privately admonished: *"The true path of the Dao is trodden by all—it has no fixed form, yet depends on people to propagate. The Ten Methods of the Daoist Way assist in spreading its teachings. When one hears of the sacred principles, they emulate them to perfect their own conduct. How can they commit faults and let others know?"*
Now, since the great virtuous ones commit no offenses, only this matter does not align with the Dao—let it be corrected immediately, like the moon waxing and waning, or the orchid’s fragrance returning. I humbly suggest this for the sake of upholding the law. Do not immediately report this to the assembly.

**Precept:** Those who have left the secular world must reside separately from laypeople and their households. If Ten Methods disciples travel through, their accommodations should be arranged based on their merit and conduct—high, middle, or low. Their living quarters must suit their station.

**Precept:** Each temple or hall must carefully consider separate lodgings for distinguished guests, hosting them in the main assembly hall. If travelers arrive from afar to stay temporarily, first inquire where they wish to reside. If their conduct is pure and their merit high, arrange them in distinguished lodgings. If their conduct is unremarkable, place them in ordinary quarters. If they are senior figures, they may be accommodated in lower ranks, but they must decline and change their lodging. If their conduct is unfit for their assigned place, they must withdraw humbly.

**Precept:** Cultivating stillness and entering meditation is the essence; wearing the yellow robe and headdress is the outward form. If one’s nature is as clear as frost, as pure as jade, and as refined as ice, they become a blessing for the world—without blemish, upholding the true precepts. Five parables illustrate this:
1. Like a noble family suddenly giving birth to a blind child, who after three months regains sight, filling the household with joy—those without precepts are like one blind.
2. Like polishing a mirror, gradually increasing its brilliance—those who uphold the precepts accumulate merit with each thought.
3. Like an infant growing step by step—those who uphold the precepts ascend from low to high.
4. Like a starving person who finally obtains food—without it, death is certain. Those who do not receive the precepts wander blindly through the Dao.
5. Like a ship crossing the great sea—those who uphold the precepts will surely traverse the sea of birth and death.

**Precept:** If kings, ministers, patrons, or artisans can benefit the assembly, they may be provided with food, firewood, and supplies upon request, with approval from the assembly.

**Precept:** Even those with power or malicious intent who might harm the assembly must be supplied with food—this is to prevent those ignorant of the law from destroying the community.

**Precept:** The temple’s funds and property must not be borrowed or used for private purposes. In cases of urgent illness, one may request permission from the assembly and repay double the amount afterward.

**Precept:** Non-Daoist possessions must not be given as offerings.

**Question:** What constitutes non-Daoist possessions?
**Answer:** Cattle, horses, slaves, and military weapons are such possessions.

**Precept:** During famines or chaos, people may seek refuge where resources are abundant. Those who can defend the assembly may be allocated supplies according to their needs.

**Precept:** If one speaks maliciously with a venomous tongue, associates with wicked groups, and harbors resentment, they must strive to suppress their emotions. If they cannot, they will cause grave harm to others.

**Precept:** Sacred and mundane items—statues, scriptures, and offerings—vary in weight and significance.
**Answer:** Temple bells, censers, banners, incense burners, canopies, sacred banners, and scripture rolls are sacred and thus heavy in merit. Hats, shoes, mats, robes, and undergarments are mundane and thus lighter. If one initially intends to donate a sacred item but later changes to a mundane one, they violate the Five Penal Laws. If one initially donates a mundane item but later upgrades to a sacred one, no offense is committed.

Statues also follow three ranks: celestial deities are supreme, true persons are middle, and lesser spirits are low, with Daoist masters at the lowest. If one initially intends to donate a high-ranking statue but later donates a lower one, they violate the Five Penal Laws. If one donates a low-ranking statue and later upgrades to a higher one, no offense is committed. The same applies to scriptures: *Upper Clarity* (Shangqing) is the great path, the *Great Net*; *Cave of Mystery* (Dongxuan) and *Soul Jewel* (Lingbao) are the middle path; and *Cave of the Gods* (Dongshen) and the *Three Sovereigns* are the lesser path. If one initially donates a great path scripture but later donates a middle or lesser one, they violate the Five Penal Laws. If one donates a lesser path scripture and later upgrades to a middle or great one, no offense is committed.

**Precept:** Stealing sacred or mundane items is punishable by the Five Grave Offenses. Stealing materials for statues is punishable by the Ten Evils. If one steals a statue from another’s home and claims it was found along the way, they incur the Five Tribunals and twenty-four million kalpas of suffering. If one creates a statue with the intent to claim it as a find, they suffer eight gates of torment for a million kalpas with no escape.

**Precept:** Those who have left the world must live in solitude, detached from worldly attachments, abandoning desires and honors, and dwelling in tranquil seclusion. If they fall into impurity, they will not be revered by the world.

**Precept:** If a mother, aunt, maternal uncle’s wife, or elder sister falls ill or faces urgent need, one may assist them without violating the precepts.

If others’ children are drowning or burning, even if one harbors impure thoughts, they must still be rescued—no violation of precepts shall occur.

**Precept:** When traveling along roads and encountering women with requests or begging for food and drink, one may only speak from ten paces away. If given food or drink, it must be placed on a bed or the ground, and taken later—never received directly into one’s own hands. If encountering women on the road, one must yield the path and pass by.

**Precept:** Fellow Dao/Way followers, differing from the secular world, are my lawful disciples. Together, they conceal each other’s faults and promote virtue, fostering mutual gratitude, so that near and far they are praised and deeply trusted. The saying goes: Benevolent people are few, the wicked many. In this age, men scrutinize minutely for flaws, slander and envy one another, unaware of their own faults while eagerly pointing out others’. Even if one does good, they will be maligned; unable to reform themselves, they instead seek to destroy virtue and align with vice—thus corrupting the Dao/Way and its teachings. This stems chiefly from such people. Great Virtue-wielders must be sternly admonished.

**Precept:** When lust arises, visualize:
- Encountering a raging tiger,
- Seeing a venomous snake,
- Beholding a king,
- Being caught by thieves before their master,
- Sitting in a house engulfed in flames,
- Boarding a sinking ship in mid-ocean.
With these six reflections, lust shall find no foothold.

**Precept:** Within shared monastic halls, pavilions, gardens, and lands—belonging to the Three Treasures—halls are for celestial reverence, pavilions for Dao/Way practitioners. If constructed, their rank must be observed. Private chambers are built by individual practitioners, their size and quality determined by their own merit during life. If no posthumous instructions are given, the community may dispose of them. If a lay novice constructs a dwelling and, after ordination, is reassigned elsewhere, they may retain it—though the land belongs to the Three Treasures and cannot be altered. If prior agreements exist among the assembly, these rules do not apply.

**Precept:** Novices newly entered into the Way, whose precepts are not yet complete, who rely on villages and do not dwell in monastic halls, lack revered elders to inspire awe and associate with cunning companions who seduce children, sharing beds and laughter, singing and drinking wine and eating meat. Secular people, seeing this, will despise the Way, deeming such conduct virtuous. Such actions extinguish the Dao/Way and shatter others’ reverence. Great Virtue-wielders must investigate and punish according to these precepts; if unable, the king’s law shall prevail.

**Precept:** If a practitioner of the Three Treasures gives their possessions to officials or the powerful, seeking personal gain, they will instead foster secular hopes. Even if they build temples, it is better to remain seated in meditation—such actions incur guilt, equivalent to theft.

**Precept:** Monastic halls and empty chambers, if excessively occupied, accumulate ten grave offenses:
1. Seizing vast wilderness lands and privately holding fields and residences;
2. Cultivating gardens and orchards for personal gain;

4. Keeping and trading slaves;
5. Cherishing and raising livestock;
6. Greedily hoarding delicacies;
7. Indulging in music and playthings;
8. Ornately decorating curtains and bedding;
9. Wearing extravagant attire;
10. Accumulating wealth with excessive diligence.

These ten acts, when held by one, do not constitute purity and emptiness, but rather bring misfortune. If one possesses them, they obstruct the mind of the Dao and hinder pure insight and wisdom.

**Precept:** If someone comes to beg, it is because of the Three Treasures’ alms, transmission of teachings, lectures, or scripture recitation, and receiving offerings. However, what is obtained through the Three Treasures must conform to the clear and true precepts, following the twelve-fold transmission penalties. If obtained otherwise, one may distribute it with goodwill, but must not accept impure things to make impure offerings—all such actions constitute wrongful violations of the law.

**Precept:** If disciples habitually fear cold, chaos, famine, and other calamities, and thus store silk, cotton, fabrics, and grains to prepare for emergencies and charitable giving, this is not forbidden.

**Precept:** If someone offers weapons, wild beasts, or unlawful items as alms, they must not be accepted.

**Precept:** If someone offers servants or slaves for service, they must not be accepted. However, if the servants can prepare vegetarian meals and uphold precepts, they may be received.

**Precept:** Monastic dwellings adjacent to secular households must close their doors at night. Failure to do so violates the precepts.

**Precept:** Practitioners must never speak of others’ hidden or shameful secrets, even if it means accepting the guilt of stealing temple bells or sacred images.

**Precept:** If hidden treasures are found in the wild and belong to the king, they must be returned. If the treasure contains a deed marking it as belonging to a scripture hall or temple, the finder may use it to construct or repair the designated place, following the inscription, without reporting to the king. Otherwise, it violates the ten grave offenses. If found on the roadside, the finder must return it to its owner. If the owner cannot be found, it becomes communal property.

**Precept:** Practitioners who witness fighting, filial disobedience, sibling disrespect, theft, or military conflict must return to their observatory, bathe in fragrant water, and enter contemplation. Failure to do so violates the precepts.

**Precept:** If Daoist priests or priestesses are unjustly mistreated by secular people, they may seek protection from their parents, siblings, or influential villagers.

**Precept:** When the Celestial Sovereign first attained enlightenment, only men were permitted to take monastic vows. How then did women gain admission to the Dao?

**Answer:** The Celestial Sovereign, through the merit of a husband-wife dispute, achieved enlightenment and became the Primordial Origin. Thus, men were universally permitted to take vows, while women, as those who awaited the Great Lady in the Fruitful Earth, were also allowed to join the Dao after scripture transmission and precept reception, becoming the Great Cavern Priestesses. Men who see women enter the Dao, having already received the Natural Law of the Old Lord, must respect and guide them according to the precepts, honoring the sacred lineage. If they see faults, they must not scold or slander them. When ordaining novices, they must defer to the Great Cavern Priestesses out of reverence for the law.

**Precept:** If someone’s donated lands, houses, or gardens are seized by others, they must be reclaimed.

**Answer:** If donated lands or gardens are seized, the original donor must be notified to reclaim them.

**Precept:** When encountering one’s teacher or their acquaintances on the road, one must step aside to avoid obstructing their path, not crossing in front of them. If speaking is necessary, one must bow deeply; otherwise, one must retreat without speaking.

**Precept:** When accompanying a venerable master, one must carry their staff and shoes. When ascending or descending perilous paths, one must stand close, supporting them with both hands, never letting go or straying far, regardless of age or companionship.

**Precept:** As a disciple’s duty, one must report before leaving and inquire after returning, greeting superiors and inferiors appropriately before resuming one’s duties.

**Precept:**
If the assembly is doubtful, I do not urge them to act;
If the assembly debates, I examine it carefully;
If the assembly acts arbitrarily, I follow what is fitting;
If the assembly travels, I do not conform to vulgar customs.
I remain consistently humble, respecting those before me.

**Precept:** For a master’s great virtue in governing the assembly, they must be broad and upright in establishing conduct, loving and disciplining the assembly, laboring diligently in their deeds, and maintaining solemn reverence in their morning rituals. Thus, superiors remain equitable without favoritism, and inferiors bear no resentment—this is the mark of great virtue.

**Precept:** If one performs good deeds, they should share the merit with those below, not claiming it solely for oneself.

**Precept:** Those who study the Dao must not expose others’ faults, boast of their own abilities, reject others’ counsel, or harbor grudges against themselves.

**Precept (from *Tai Zhen Science*):**
Novices of the same Daoist lineage and aspiration must mutually refine each other, proclaiming the wondrous transformations. Junior disciples must relay teachings to juniors without idle speech. If a servant, they must treat fellow disciples as brothers, united in heart, carefully observing the precepts and conduct. Their actions must be precise and strict, adhering to statutes and propriety, without negligence. They must seek their own blessings and pray for others without duplicity, devoting themselves earnestly to transforming vice into virtue. Violations shall be punished by the five penalties.

**Precept:** Even if a disciple surpasses others in talent and virtue, if they are junior in age, they must still yield with respect.

**Precept:** If others advance me, I shall accept their promotion with humility and not feign modesty. If they wrong me, I shall swear not to retaliate. If they exalt me, I shall swear not to presume. Though unable to yield in the moment, when circumstances demand it, or if it is fitting for them to instruct me, I shall defer three times. Even if later I hold a position of authority, my heart shall still honor my elders, and I shall not neglect the rites of respect as set by precedent.

Again, those who are acquainted must be called friends only if their Daoist aspirations are aligned—this is true friendship. Though they may share the same Daoist lineage, if their resolve and conduct are not steadfast, this is merely casual association. Some merely observe each other’s demeanor, hoping to form connections without genuine affinity. Such examples are numerous, and broadly there are five:
1. They come from similar family backgrounds,
2. Their official ranks are comparable,
3. They hold low status but possess influence,
4. They are of humble birth but wealthy,
5. Their age and appearance are alike.
All are worldly friendships.

In Daoist friendship, one must select companions whose aspirations align, valuing not their noble or lowly station but their shared Way and resolve. The humble must not seek the exalted, nor the exalted reject the humble. Forgetting distinctions of age and power, they unite only in shared Dao and virtue. Violations shall be punished by the seven penalties.

**Precept:** Though one may have formed bonds earlier, if later their official ranks diverge—whether as teacher and disciple, master and friend, or ruler and subject—they must sever ties and observe the rites of their current station. If the superior does not dissolve the bond, all must still act with humility and maintain the relationship. Those in higher ranks must not call inferiors to dissolve the bond; those in lower ranks must not pledge allegiance to superiors unless commanded by them.

**Precept on Ritual Platforms (Third in Sequence):**
The *Twenty-Four Lives Diagram* states: The Primordial Sovereign of the Dao extended an invitation to his guests in the Pure Hall, crafting a platform of yellow gold and a foundation of white silver.

The *Original Source Scripture* says: The Great Brahman King, having secured the teachings of the *Original Source Scripture*, built a grand hall within his kingdom and erected a magnificent ritual platform.

It further states: The Absolute Harmony King, who delighted in music, constructed three ritual platforms each month, repeating the cycle.

It also states: Master Lin established a platform, but a woman, relying on her beauty, mocked and seduced him, and afterward, he became disfigured.

It further says: At that time, a seven-jewel spirit platform emerged from the earth, rising a hundred or more zhang above the ground, with nine tiers and eight sides. Each tier had nine openings, and within them were eighty-one golden bells and jade chimes. They rang naturally at six times each day and night, all eighty-one sounding in unison.

It also says: The disciple of Still Mystery questioned the Celestial Sovereign: "Why does the ritual platform arise from the earth when the *Original Source Scripture* is being expounded?" The Celestial Sovereign replied: "When the Highest Emperor first expounded the *Original Source Scripture*, the Void King constructed this platform, but it sank into obscurity. Now that the *Original Source Scripture* is being expounded again, the platform emerges in response."

The *Five Talismans Sequence* states: The platform at the Northern Altar is where the Emperor sacrificed to the Celestial Sovereign.

**Precept on Memorial Steles and Gateways (Fourth in Sequence):**
The *Original Source Scripture* says: Fan Zezi, following his son Fan Shunzi, attained the Dao. Upon arriving, he saw only two white cranes on the Pure and Clear Jade Stele, and the inscription read: "In the past, we studied the Daoist scriptures together, adhering to the thirty-six sects, yet our hearts were not focused, and our aspirations failed to converge."

**Essential Ritual Statutes and Precepts (Completion of Volume Thirteen, Beginning of Volume Fourteen):**
To be continued in Volume Fourteen.

**Precept on Abstinence from Alcohol (From the *Three Caverns Daoist Canon* by Master Zhu Faman)**

The *Scripture on the Origins of Drinking* states:
*"To abstain from alcohol in ritual observance, harmonizing qi and nature."*

The *Taiping Jing* records:
The True Person asked: *"Why do people brew and drink alcohol, selling it along the roads? When ordinary folk drink, they become intoxicated—singing wildly, fighting to the death, or harming one another. Some commit adultery through it, others fall into ruin. The harms of alcohol are countless and incalculable.

Consider the four seas within: how many markets exist? In a single day, they consume billions of *dou* and *hu* of grain. Because of this, disasters extend even to the county magistrates, leaving descendants in lamentation. The heavens are moved, yin and yang are disrupted, and the qi of the Four Seasons and Five Phases are thrown into disorder.

Why, then, do people brew this madness as a drink? Should it be forbidden?"*

The Divine Person replied: *"Well spoken. Food and drink sustain life. My words may be followed in part or not at all—but let virtuous rulers decree:
From this day forward, any who drink alcohol without cause shall be punished as follows:
One *dou* – twenty lashes;
Two *dou* – sixty strokes;
Three *dou* – ninety strokes."*

「One *hu* – three hundred strokes. Let this be the standard, and widely promulgate it throughout the realm, so that the wise and virtuous may know the law and fear disgrace, and thus dare not transgress.

But what of the foolish among them who do offend? They shall be punished accordingly. Those who brew alcohol shall also be treated the same as those who drink it.

The Divine Person asked: *"What if there are travelers from afar, or households with the elderly and infirm, or rites honoring deities and spirits? How should they be handled?"*

The **Godperson** replied: *"If virtuous travelers from afar know the land has prohibitions, they shall abstain individually and not gather together. For households with the aged or sick, medicinal wine may be permitted for passage.

The *Qian Zhen Ke* (Scripture of the Thousand True Precepts) states: Those who have taken the **Dharma vow** (出家之人) must not drink alcohol. Yet some feign cold weather, claim stomach pains, and after drinking, change countenance. Others disturb the order of **supreme and subordinate** (尊卑), or accept offerings at **vegetarian meals** (斋), or engage in **ritual exorcisms** (章醮), or wander the roads, or respond to public and private invitations. Not only do they themselves violate **ritual decorum** (礼仪), but they also sully the **Dao community** (道众), extinguishing the **Dao Law** (道法) and hindering the **pristine propagation** (无生弘赞).

Yet, those who attend others’ requests should prioritize **purity and cleanliness** (清洁), and when moving between public and private affairs, they must uphold **proper decorum** (端严). Such instances are all violations of the **precepts** (律论).

The *Lingbao Jing* (Scripture of the Numinous Treasure) says: Those born who drink alcohol shall, upon death, be **condemned to draw endless oceanic waters** (连汲溟波水) to irrigate the **Four Great Waters** (沃四渎), or it is said that within the **Dao Law** (道法), some are permitted to drink alcohol.

The *Lingbao Jing* further states: *"To set wine upon the Floating Cloud Observance (浮云观), to drink high upon the Jade Purity Platform (玉清台)—how is this suddenly forbidden?"*

The answer is: *"This is a mistaken view."*

The *Taiping Jing* (Scripture of Great Peace) says: *"To transmute gold and jade into the **Thirty-Six Waters** (三十六水), gold as water becomes **golden nectar** (金浆), red jade as water becomes **glistening nectar** (琼浆), white jade as water becomes **jade nectar** (玉浆), or it is also called **jade essence** (玉液). The five do not intoxicate, and one must always reflect upon **pure conduct** (净行). Why, then, is this allowed?"*

The *Wu Yue Tu Xù* (Five Peaks Diagram Sequence) states: *"Abstaining from grains and taking medicinal elixirs according to the **Danlao Divine Prescriptions** (丹蜡神方), one may go a thousand years without eating, yet remain plump and not emaciated, and have the strength to bear heavy burdens. The prescription is as follows: **True cinnabar** (真丹) one pound, **mirabilite** (芒硝) half ounce, **Poria** (茯苓) one pound—all crushed and mixed together. Then, **white wax** (白蜡) two pounds is added, and the mixture is simmered nine times upward and nine times downward before forming into pills, which are swallowed whole like **Chinese parasol tree seeds** (梧桐子). Ten pills shall suffice for one month of abstinence from grains.

The **Laojun’s Method of Guarding the Middle** (老君守中赤丸法) involves the following: Take **white honey** (白蜜) one pound, **true cinnabar** (真丹) one pound, **one part of the prescription** (一方三两), and **white wax** (白蜡) one pound. First, finely chop the wax, then boil it in **copper vessels** (铜器) with wine until the wine boils. Next, add the cinnabar to the wine, then pour the mixture into a **copper vessel with cold water** (玲水). The wax solidifies again, and it is removed from the water. Repeat this process three times upward and three times downward. After the wax solidifies, discard the wine and place the wax alone in the copper vessel over a fire until it boils nine times, then remove it. Add the **white honey** (白蜜) to the wax and boil it once more. Then add the **true cinnabar** (真丹), stirring until they combine. When the mixture begins to congeal, quickly form it into pills the size of **bullet-shaped pills** (弹丸). To abstain from grains, take one pill daily, beginning with one pill on the first day, two on the second, and three on the third. Then resume with one pill, continuing for nine days, taking a total of eighteen pills as one dose. Afterward, one may **guard the middle** (守中). For forty years, one shall not hunger, and one’s complexion, **qi**, and strength shall remain unchanged. One may carry heavy burdens and travel long distances. If thirsty, one may drink a little cold water or a little wine, but must not eat anything else, for this makes one immune to poison—though it cannot prolong life or achieve **immortality** (长生). One’s body shall be light, and one’s strength shall not diminish, even when traversing mountains.

If one cannot swallow large pills, they may also be divided into smaller ones, ensuring the total amount of medicine is correct.

After fasting for seven days, the **royal alchemist’s full-moon day** (王相建满定日) is set for mixing the medicine. Do not allow children, women, or poultry to see it. Later, if one wishes to resume eating grains, boil **Chinese water chestnut** (葵子) one pint to make a thin gruel and drink it. The medicine shall then pass through. Before eating, one should gradually consume **gruel** (糜), not suddenly gorge oneself.

This method was used by **Master Shen** (沈君) to feed cattle and horses, who afterward no longer ate grass but remained fat as before.

A **secret and verified method** (秘验一方) involves boiling the **white wax** (洋蜡) three times upward and three times downward, then adding **white honey** (蜜) for one boil, and finally incorporating **true cinnabar** (丹) while stirring cold—thus forming the **Guarding the Middle** pill.

As for the **Four Calming Pills** (诸镇丸法), the prescription is as follows: **Poria** (茯苓), **dried yellow berry** (乾黄), **fine wood** (精木), **kudzu root** (楮实), and **ginseng** (人参), each one ounce. Crush and sift them, then mix with **white honey** (白蜜) five ounces and **white wax** (白蜡) two ounces. Combine with the earlier medicines, and pound them together for a thousand strokes. Take one pill the size of a **child’s fist** (小儿拳), then proceed to take the **large and small Four Calming Pills** (大小四镇).

After taking the pills, one should also take the **previously mentioned *Bole* pills** (栢叶丸) and **narrow Poria pills** (狭苓丸) as optimal.

The **Small Calming Pill** (小镇丸法) prescription is as follows: **cinnabar powder** (丹沙) half pound, **narrow Poria** (狭苓) half pound, **Agrimony root** (禹余粮) half pound, **Ophiopogon** (麦门冬) one pint, and **white honey** (白蜜) three ounces—totaling five ingredients. The **cinnabar powder**, **Agrimony root**, and **narrow Poria** are mixed with honey into a thin paste and pounded for three thousand strokes. The **Ophiopogon** (麦门冬) is stripped of its heart, and three ounces are divided into four pills, which are rubbed with the hands until they shine.

On the full-moon day at dawn, facing east, take one pill. Then take one pill every ten days, repeating this for another ten days, totaling four pills over thirty days. Those who have taken this medicine and survived are more than thirty in number.

When mixing the medicine, use the **royal alchemist’s full-moon day** (王相满日), and one must fast and abstain, not allowing children or women to see it. Do not eat **Chinese water chestnut** (葵菜), raw vegetables, or enter homes where there are births, deaths, or childbirths. This prescription is recorded in the *Changshi Book* (长史书).

The **Simple Method of Guarding the Middle** (守中径易法) is as follows: Take **fresh soybeans** (大豆) three pints, which must be alive. Rub them with the hands until they are smooth and warm. After finishing a meal, swallow them all at once. This shall suffice to abstain from grains for fifty days or a hundred days. If thirsty, drink water, but do not eat anything else. To stop the abstinence, consume two pints of hot gruel, and the soybeans shall pass through.

Another method states: Each day, bow twice in reverence, then take one pint of the prescription in the mouth. While reciting the *Liu Jia Tong* (Sixfold Passage), swallow it. After three days, divide the pint into three portions. For children, halve it.»

「Moreover, **red bean (赤豆)** and **pork**—swallow two pints of red bean or three pints of pork—also sustains one for a year. Another method: Take **large soybeans (大豆)** and **yellow millet (黄米)** three pints each, and swallow them all at once in one meal; this too allows one to abstain from grains for ten or five days.

When desiring to eat again, take **boiled hemp stalk ash (葵茎灰)** one square inch, seven times, then swallow it with **pork fat (猪膏)** and **sour milk (酪苏)**—this is also beneficial.

Another method: First chew **wax (蜡)** into a large piece like a walnut, then soften it thoroughly. Next, insert **a type of date (枣)** from the **Yi (猗氏)** region, along with the chewed wax, and swallow it all after thorough mastication. This will dissolve in the stomach, fortify the **true qi (正气)**, and cure illness while abstaining from grains.

Alternatively, simply consume **one square inch of wax (一方寸蜡)**, and it will suffice for one day.

Another method: Take **one pound each of white mulberry bark (檀榆皮)** and **white willow bark (白榆皮)**, with **one dou (斗)** of wine, steep them until dry, then re-steep them until all the wine is exhausted. Take a dose of **two liang (两)**, and after ten days, one can travel **three thousand li (里)**.

Another method: Take **black mulberries (桑椹)**, dry them in the sun, and pound them into a powder. Consume with **three he (合)** of water, three times daily, and one will not feel hunger.

Another method: On the **third day of the third month (三月三日)**, or the **thirteenth (十三日)** or **twenty-third day (二十三日)**, take **white dewberry roots (白茅根)**, clean them, wash them, and cut them finely. Consume with water, or dry them into a powder and prepare them in advance. Take **five or six doses daily**, but do not overeat. Long-term use will enhance one’s complexion and prevent aging, while also warding off **two types of malevolent spirits (伏鬼神)**.

Another method: Take **five jin (斤)** of **white dewberry (白茅)**, **one dou (斗)** of **rice (稻米)**, **one dou (斗)** of **fermented broad beans (豉)**, and **half a he (合)** of **salt (盐)**. Boil them in **three dou (斗)** of water until fully cooked and mushy. Initially, eat until full, then gradually reduce portions; one will not feel hunger. This method removes **cold and heat (寒热)**, prolongs life.

**Pine root (松根) method**: Take **pine roots (松根)** from the east-facing slope, strip off the white bark, and finely chop it. Dry them in the sun, pound into a powder, and sift. Consume them after a full meal; this allows one to abstain from grains. If thirsty, drink water.

Alternatively, simply take **pine leaves (栢叶)**, dry them in the sun, and form them into pills with **honey (蜜)**. Consuming these will prevent hunger. They can also be consumed as a powder with water or wine. Mix the powder with **white wine (白酒)**, dry it, and then pound and sift it again. Take it with wine or water. No matter the method, long-term use will lighten the body, prolong life, reduce body odor, and diminish sleep. The body will grow **green hair that turns white (绿毛还白)**, and one will abstain from grains without feeling hunger. When consuming, maintain consistency—this applies equally to pine leaves.

**Qi-abstinence grain abstention method (服气断谷法)**: First, close your mouth and swallow **internal qi (内气)**, avoiding inhalation of **external qi (外气)**. Perform **three hundred and sixty swallows (咽)** daily, or more if desired, up to a thousand—this is even better, achieved gradually. After ten days of grain abstention, one will naturally no longer feel the need to eat. If, after three days of abstaining from grains, one feels slight hunger or has **urine that is red-yellow without pain (小便赤黄无苦)**, consume **two or three dried dates (乾枣)**, up to nine per day. **Wine (酒)**, taken midday, can be **one or two pints (升)**; initially take small amounts, then gradually increase.

**Twelve-times-per-day qi swallowing method (食十二时气法)**: Always swallow qi at the following times: **midnight (夜半)**, **three times (九九)**; **cockcrow (鸡鸣)**, **eight times (八八)**; **dawn (平旦)**, **seven times (七七)**; **sunrise (日出)**, **six times (六六)**; **mealtime (食时)**, **five times (五五)**; **noon (禺中)**, **four times (四四)**; and **midday (日中)**, resume with **three times (九九)**.

Each swallow should be done with the mouth closed to allow the **qi (气)** to enter the abdomen. Swallowing once per hour is sufficient, then rinse and stimulate the **saliva (津液)**. Swallow multiple times in succession, and each time, face the corresponding direction for optimal results. Within **four or five days**, one may experience **head dizziness and extreme emaciation (头眩瘦极)**; after this, the effects will gradually improve.

**Consuming amulet water to abstain from grains (服符水断谷)**: Write the **Sixfold Passage (六甲)** *yin-yang amulets (阴阳符)* according to their respective day branches and stems, and place them in the prescription. Beforehand, keep the amulets in your mouth, then take them on their designated days, bless the water, and consume it.

When taking the *yin-yang amulets (阴阳符)*, face east at dawn, hold the amulet in your **left hand (左手)** and the water vessel in your **right hand (右手)**. Recite the blessing:

*"True Person [Name] loves and delights in the True Dao/Way (真道). Consuming the harmonious qi (中和之气).*
*In the **Tenth of the Heavenly Stems (甲子)**, the **Supreme Mysterious (太玄)** and **Jade Lady (玉女)** take wing and attend [Name]. Use the **kitchen’s location (厨所)** as the designated place, and remove what should be removed. Without hunger or thirst, whether the army is large or small, whether the people are few or many, all shall be sated.*
*After reciting, place the amulet in your mouth and let the water carry it down. Only the number of people varies.*

If you wish to make others abstain from grains, whether for a thousand or a hundred people, all should face east and stand in a row, bow twice, and each recite their own name. Then, write the amulets for them and let them all drink from **one vessel of water**.

*For the **Tenth of the Heavenly Stems (甲子旬)***, the **Supreme Mysterious Jade Lady (太玄玉女)** is **Winged Attendant (承翼)**.
*For the **Tenth of the Earthly Branches (甲戌旬)***, the **Yellow Jade Lady (黄素玉女)** is **Flying Censor (飞廉)**.
*For the **Tenth of the Firely Branches (甲申旬)***, the **Supreme Jade Lady (太素玉女)** is **Jewel Rock (琼石)**.
*For the **Tenth of the Earthly Stems (甲午旬)***, the **Descending Palace Jade Lady (降宫玉女)** is **Cloud-Longevity (云龄)**.
*For the **Tenth of the Heavenly Stems (甲辰旬)***, the **Precise Reverence Jade Lady (拜精玉女)** is **Spiritual Essence (灵素)**.
*For the **Tenth of the Woodly Branches (甲寅旬)***, the **Green Vitality Jade Lady (青要玉女)** is **Kindly Essence (惠精)**.
*These six names of the **Jade Ladies (玉女)** must be correctly invoked—do not err.*

**Jade Lord’s Resolute Abstention Amulet (玉君绝毅符)**: Write in **cinnabar (丹)** on paper and burn it at the end of the day. With **divine water (神水)**, face north and bow twice before consuming the amulet. Hold the water and face the moon, reciting three blessings:

*"Gold, wood, water, fire, and earth—*
*the **qi of the Five Stars (五星之气)**,*
*the **essence of the Sixfold Passage (六甲之精)**,*
*the **Three True (三真)** and **Heavenly Granary (天仓)**.*
*Pure **qi (清气)** constantly fills,*
*the **yellow text and red child (黄文赤子)** guard the center without tipping.*
*After reciting, knock the teeth three times and sip from the cup three times. Then swallow the amulet and drink **one pint (升)** of water.*

All the above methods are from the **Lower Scroll of Supreme Clarity (太清下卷)**.

**Laozi’s Method of Consuming Water to Abstain from Grains (老君服水断谷法)**: Regardless of whether it is a clear dawn, simply drink water whenever you feel the need. Fill a cup with water and bless it toward the water, reciting:

*"Gold, wood, water, fire, and earth—*
*the **qi of the Five Stars (五星之气)**,*
*the **essence of the Sixfold Passage (六甲之精)**,*
*the **True Person’s Heavenly Granary (真人天仓)**.*
*Pure **qi (清气)** constantly fills,*
*the **yellow text and red child (黄文赤子)** guard the center without tipping.*
*After reciting three times and knocking the teeth three times, drink the water. This will make one unaware of hunger or thirst, and if consumed again, it will have extraordinary spiritual efficacy.*

Recently, many people have gained strength from this method, recorded in the **Nourishing Life Canon (养生经)**. Later, the blessings were transcribed, differing slightly from the original. No other editions have been verified for comparison.

*The **Dao Basis (道基)** states*: The blessing for abstaining from grains among the **Six Livestock (六畜)** is as follows:

*"All things contain water—*
*like **living water (生水)** entering the abdomen."*

「All **spirits (万神)** tremble in fear—
**pulsed beings (有脉之物)** may be severed, **non-pulsed beings (无脉之物)** cannot be.
The **Six Livestock (六畜)** are all drawn toward the **King (王)**.

**Treatment and invocation (治祝缘)** from *The Secrets of Ascending the True (登真隐诀)*:
All practices of **moving (诸行事)**, **retention (存想)**, and **invocation (祝愿)** are included here.
Now, I briefly extract a few key **urgent (急)** methods.

Whenever traversing **treacherous paths (危崄之路)** or **ghostly temples (鬼庙之间)**,
or encountering any **doubtful or perilous (疑难)** places in mind,
or when the heart harbors **subtle misgivings (微忌)** about those who tread upon them,
one should first **reverse the tongue (反舌)** inward,
then **reverse the tongue upward (反舌向上)** toward the throat’s pillar.
Before invoking, **forcefully swallow saliva (申之咽唾)** three times,
then with the **left hand’s second and third fingers (左手第二、第三指)**,
**twist the nostrils (捻)** below the **human middle (人中)**—
the **nasal septum’s inner boundary (鼻中隔孔之内际)**—
**thirty-six times (三十六过)**, until the breath stills.
**Do not count with raised fingers (勿举指计数)**.

This **urgent pressing (急按)** of the **mid-yin point (中阴数)**—
a single breath as one **pass (过)**—
the **nasal septum’s inner boundary (鼻中隔孔之际)**, known as:
**Mountain Source (山源)**, also called **Ghost Well (鬼井)**,
**Spirit Pool (神池)**, **Perverse Root (邪根)**, **Soul Terrace (魂台)**.
Afterward, these five names appear in the invocation,
so they are listed first.

**Madame Purple Clarity (紫彻夫人)** says:
*"Mountain Source (山源)** is the root below the **human middle (人中)**;
it lies beside the **small human valley (小入谷)** beneath the nose.
Piercing it with a needle also treats sudden death and **covering the corpse (掩毕)**.
Afterward, **knock the teeth seven times seven (叩齿七七通)**,
then press the **palm of the hand (手心)** over the nose,
before removing the hand, **still knocking the teeth (仍叩齿竟)**.
Then advance the **left hand’s palm (左手掌)** to cover the **nose and mouth (鼻口)**,
reaching to the **hairline (发际)** and covering the **Bright Hall (明堂)** above.
Thus, **facing the eyes (临目)**,
while inwardly retaining the **Three Lords of the Bright Hall (明堂中三君)**,
use a **bell and mirror (铃镜)** to flash **red light (赤光)** upon them,
then **retain the Red Child of the Earthly Pill (泥丸赤子帝君)**,
who holds the *Great Cavern True Scripture (大洞真经)*,
and **threaten them with its majesty (以威摄之)**.

Then softly invoke:
*"The Vermilion Bird (朱鸟) soars through the heavens,
its **spiritual might (神威)** internally expands—
Mountain Source’s **four guardians (四镇)**,
Ghost Well’s **flight into exile (逃亡)**?
Spirit Pool **exhales its breath (吐气)**,
Perverse Root **submits in concealment (伏藏)**,
Soul Terrace **shines with clarity (四明)**,
Jade Chamber’s **resplendent brilliance (琼房玲琅)**,
Jade Gate’s **towering grandeur (玉莫巍峨)**,
sits enthroned in the Bright Hall.
With a **wave of the hand (手挥)**, summon **Purple Mist (紫霞)**,
and **erect the head (头建)**, invoke the **Morning Light (晨光)**.
Reciting the *Thirty-nine Chapters of the Great Cavern True Scripture (洞经三十九章)*,
within which lies the **Divine Tiger (神虎)** that repels evil,
**Severing the Mountain (截岳)** and **beheading the Ridge (斩冈)**,
wild beasts **flee like cattle (奔牛)**,
**swallowing blades (冲刀)** and **devouring spears (吞枪)**,
**lifting mountains (揭山)** and **plucking the heavens (攫天)**,
the **Divine Sparrow (神雀)** strikes the **Poisonous Dragon (毒龙)**,
**six leaders (六领)** exhale **flames (吐火)**,
and **consume the King of Ghosts (啖鬼之王)**—
**Thunder Pig (电猪)** and **Lightning Sire (雷父)**,
**dragging stars (掣星)** and **flowing crosswise (流横)**,
**Jackal’s (枭)** howling and **scorching (磕驳灼)**,
**counter-winds (逆风)** and **horizontally rampant (横行)**,
**heavenly beasts (天禽)** arrayed in **nets (罗陈)**,
all **beside me (在我傍)**.
A **ten-thousand-zhang flame (吐火万丈)** dispels **inauspiciousness (不祥)**,
**military precision (军精)** opens the **Dao (启道)**,
and **seals the Mountain Village (封落山乡)**.
**Thousand spirits and hundred souls (千神百灵)** all **bow and submit (并首叩类)**,
**the Marshal of Dew (泽尉)** presents the **lamp (捧灯)**,
to **burn incense for me (为我烧香)**.
Wherever I go or tread,
**all souls (万灵)** pay homage in welcome.
After the **nineteen stanzas (十九韵毕)**,
**knock the teeth three times (叩齿三通)**,
then open the eyes and remove the left hand.

Thus, **stirring the spiritual roots (感激灵根)**,
**heavenly beasts (天兽)** come to guard me,
**thousand spirits (千精)** tremble and submit,
**none dare harm my qi (莫干我气)**.

These are the **names of divine beasts and spiritual officials (神兽灵司之名号)**,
so they may be invoked to **shock away evil spirits (震却精邪)**.

The above is the **Supreme Invocation to Restrain Evil (遏邪大祝)** from the *Great Cavern True Scripture’s (大洞真经) Highest Inner Chapter (高上内章)*,
recorded by **Chief Clerk (长史)**.

**The Northern Emperor’s (北帝) Method to Slay Ghosts (杀鬼之法)**:
First, **knock the teeth thirty-six times (叩齿三十六下)**,
then invoke:
*"O **Heavenly Scourge (天蓬)**! O **Heavenly Scourge (天蓬)**!
**Nine Elements (九元)** slay the **child (杀童)**,
**Five Ding (五丁)** command the **officers (都司)**,
**High Siao Northern Lord (高刁北公)**,
**Seven Rectitudes and Eight Spirits (七正八灵)**,
**Supreme Sovereign’s (太上) Vast Wrath (浩凶)**,
**long-skull giant beasts (长颅巨兽)**,
holding the **imperial bell (帝钟)** in hand,
**three white jackals (素枭三神)**,
**strictly mounted upon the **Kui Dragon (夔龙)***,
**Sword Spirit King (威剑神王)**,
**severing evil (斩邪)** and **eradicating traces (灭踪)**—
**purple qi ascends the heavens (紫气乘天)**,
**crimson mist surges upward (丹霞赫冲)**,
**devouring demons (吞魔)** and **consuming ghosts (食鬼)**,
**crossing the body (横身)** to **drink the wind (饮风)**,
**black tongue and green teeth (苍舌绿齿)**,
**four-eyed old man (四目老翁)**,
**Heavenly Ding’s (天丁) mighty laborers (力士)**,
**threatening the South (威南)** to **subdue the ferocious (御凶)**,
**Heavenly Steed (天驺)** incites the **rebellious (激戾)**,
**threatening the North (威北)** to **terrify the sharp (吓锋)**.
**Thirty myriads of soldiers (三十万兵)** guard my **ninefold enclosure (卫我九重)**,
**clearing a thousand-li path (辟户千里)**,
and **repelling inauspiciousness (却不祥)**.
Should any **minor ghosts (小鬼)** dare to approach,
**the Heavenly Axe (玃天大斧)** will **execute them with five punishments (斩鬼五刑)**,
**Emperor Yan’s (炎帝) blood-splitting wrath (裂血)***,
**Northern Emperor’s (北帝) bone-searing judgment (然骨)***,
**Four Bright Ones’ (四明) corpse-shattering might (破骸)***,
**Heavenly You’s (天猷) annihilation of their kind (灭类)***,
and **one strike of the divine blade (神刀一下)**—
**all ten thousand ghosts (万鬼)** will **collapse in rout (自溃)**.*

**Thirty-six four-character stanzas (三十六句四言)**,
each followed by a **peck of the teeth (啄齿)** as a **pause (以为节)**.
A total of **thirty-six plus six stanzas (凡三＋六句)**,
each separated by **thirty-six plus six pecks of the teeth (则三＋六啄齿)**.
Whether in **midnight darkness (冥夜)** or **broad daylight (白日)**,
this invocation is **always effective (得祝为恒)**.

This has **no fixed time (无正时节)**.
When engaged in **spiritual cultivation (修事)**,
during **leisure hours (有闲)** or at **dawn and dusk (及晓夜之际)**,
or in **all shadowy and obscure (诸疑暗)** places,
one may invoke it. Within are **threefold references (三被)** to ghosts:
their **eyes will be blinded (盲烂)** and they will die.

This refers to **all killing ghosts (杀鬼)**,
**evil ghosts (邪鬼)***, and those of **darkness in heaven and earth (天地暗)**,
as well as **malevolent spirits (恶强)** and **ghostly cohorts (鬼辈)**,
who upon hearing this invocation will die.
It does not apply to **the souls of the deceased (死之魂爽)** that become ghosts,
but to those **ghostly eyes (鬼眼)**—
even they have **eyes (睛)**—
so when blinded, they will perish.

The **upper invocations (上神祝)** are all **names of ghost-slaying officials (斩鬼之司名)**.
Within the invocation are **names of the Underworld (酆都)**,
and **all spirits and deities (及诸神名字)**—
thus, ghosts hear and **die in terror (怖死)**.
Grant them **command of a thousand southern soldiers (许其领威南兵千人)**,
and they will be the **ones who subdue the ferocious (即此御凶者)**.
**Emperor Yan (炎帝)** is the **Great Sovereign (大帝)**,
**Four Bright Ones (四明)** are the **various lords (诸公)**.

**The Northern Emperor (北帝)** conceals this method,
for if a **ghost-slaying Northern Emperor (建鬼杀人)*** encounters this invocation,
he **cannot prevail (便不可复得)**.
Thus, the method is kept secret.
If **mortals (世人)** obtain this invocation,
and **constantly practice it (恒能行之)**,
they will **never die (便不死)**.
For **all deaths (人之死)** are caused by **ghosts (所杀)**.

Now that this invocation **cannot be seized (既不可取)**,
one will **never die again (不复死)**.
Both **men and women (男女)** and **all ages (大小)** may perform it.
Only those who **do not know this invocation (患其不知此祝)*** suffer.

The **wise (智者)** who **secretly employ it (密用)***
will **face no limits (无限)** in size or age.
This is spoken to **inform the Chief Clerk’s family (令告长史家)**:
if one **suffers from illness (困病)** and practices this,
one will **recover instantly (立愈)**.
If one **even flees in thought (思既幸走)***,
how much more will **disease be dispelled (病岂不除)**?

**Knocking the teeth (叩齿)**,
one should **face the eyes (临目)*** and **retain the five viscera (存神五藏)**.
When the **five viscera (五藏)** are fully present,
the **five spirits (五神)** will naturally **reside within (自然存在)**.

This means that **initially (初)**, during the **thirty-six knocks of the teeth (叩齿三十六时)**,
one should **face the eyes (临目)*** and **introspectively observe (内视)** the **five viscera (五藏)**,
sequentially **retain them (以次想之)**,
and **clearly distinguish (皆令分明)** the **spirits of the five viscera (五藏之神)**,
ensuring they **are fully present within (备在於内)**.
Then one may **ride upon the upright (乘正)** to **ward off evil spirits (御邪神)**,
and **to exterminate ghosts (以诛鬼)**.*

The **Zheng** capital concealed this incantation,
now it is secretly recited—
do not reveal it.
Only those who **follow the Dao/Way (有道者)**,
should **keep it secret together (宜共秘之乎)**.

Though this is not the **most exalted of sacred rites (高贵之至典)**,
it is the **supreme defense against ghosts (杀鬼之上卫)**.
Once **malevolent and fierce (凶恶)** energies are dispelled,
the **upright qi (正气)** can be restored.
Moreover, it serves as the **essential method (要法)** to **exterminate evil spirits (诛邪)** and **restrain those who test (遏试)** the practitioner—
yet most people **dismiss its simplicity (轻其浅少)**,
often **leaking it (传泄)**,
causing the **spiritual incantation (神祝)** to fail,
the **ritual recitation (呵执)** to be ineffective.
This is truly **blameworthy (殊为可责之也)**.

Yang Jun’s clerk **wrote two volumes (书两本)**.
While resting on the pillow, **leaning against (枕)** the *Daoqi Jing* says:
*"If the pillow is too high, the liver contracts (枕高肝缩),
if the pillow is too low, the lungs are obstructed (枕下肺塞).
Four cun is the balanced height (以四寸为平),
and the bed should be level (枕席令平),
then the breath will become long (其息乃长)."*

The *Daolin Pin* and *Guangmen Jing* state:
*"When **cultivating the qi (行气)**,
the pillow should be raised two and a half cun (枕高二寸半)."*

The *Taqing Jing* says:
*"The **method of lowering the spirit (下神枕法)**:
On the fifth day of the fifth month,
or the seventh day of the seventh month,
take the **wood of the *zhi* tree (栢)** from mountains and forests as a pillow,
one foot two cun long (长一尺二寸),
four cun high (高四寸),
with a hollow center holding one dou two sheng (空中容一斗二升).
Its width is three cun five fen (广三寸五分),
and its top is covered with a **red cloth (相心赤)**,
four fen thick (厚四分).
The **lowering method (下之钻)** is well-applied,
and the cover has **three rows of forty-nine holes (为三行四十九孔)**,
totaling **one hundred twenty holes (凡百二十孔)**.
For every **grain-sized cavity (容一黍栗)**,
insert medicine (乃取药).
